VTT Bot Test Sequences
======================

Each scenario starts fresh with its own match id (m1, m2, ...). You can run
any scenario independently, or run all in sequence and they won't collide.
Quote any argument containing spaces, just like in a shell.


SCENARIO 1 — Setup, formulas, and inline $() substitution
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new m1 demo 8 8
!match use m1
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 5 5 20
!list
!eval "entity[rogue].hp + entity[hero].hp"
!eval "min(entity[hero].hp, entity[rogue].hp)"
!ent set_var hero regen 7
!ent hp hero "$(entity[this].hp * -1 + 5)"
!eval "entity[hero].hp"
!ent hp hero "$(entity[self].regen)"
!eval "entity[hero].hp"

Expected: list shows two entities; sum eval returns 55; min returns 25; the
$(entity[this].hp * -1 + 5) expression damages Hero by 25 (HP 30 -> 5);
$(entity[self].regen) then heals by 7 (HP 5 -> 12).


SCENARIO 2 — Entity passives + hook firing
-------------------------------------------

!match new m2 passives 8 8
!match use m2
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 5 5 20
!ent set_var hero stamina 5
!ent set_var hero max_stamina 50
!passive hooks
!passive add hero regen on_turn_start "entity[self].stamina = min(entity[self].stamina + 10, entity[self].max_stamina)"
!passive list hero
!passive info hero regen
!eval "entity[hero].stamina"
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].stamina"
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].stamina"
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].stamina"
!passive remove hero regen
!passive list hero

Expected: stamina starts at 5. First !turn next fires on_round_start +
on_turn_start (regen 5 -> 15). Second !turn next is Rogue's turn (no regen,
still 15). Third !turn next is Hero again (15 -> 25). After remove, list
reports no passives.


SCENARIO 3 — Global passives + buggy passive isolation
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new m3 globals 8 8
!match use m3
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 5 5 20
!gpassive add gas on_round_start "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 1"
!gpassive list
!gpassive info gas
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].hp"
!eval "entity[rogue].hp"
!passive add hero broken on_turn_start "entity[self].hp = 1 / 0"
!turn next
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].hp"
!gpassive remove gas
!passive remove hero broken
!gpassive list

Expected: First !turn next applies gas to both (Hero 30 -> 29, Rogue 25 ->
24). The broken passive fires on Hero's next turn and shows a "CRASHED"
log line, but Hero's hp is unaffected and the turn cycle continues
normally. Final gpassive list reports none.


SCENARIO 4 — Custom entity_line_format
---------------------------------------

!match new m4 templates 8 8
!match use m4
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 5 5 20
!list
!system set default entity_line_format "{name} | HP {hp}/{max_hp} | ({x},{y})"
!list
!ent set_var hero shields 50
!system set default entity_line_format "{name} | HP {hp}/{max_hp}{?shields?} | Shields {shields}{/?}"
!list
!system set default entity_line_format "{name} (init {initiative}) HP:{hp}/{max_hp}"
!list

Expected: First list uses the default format. After first set, both lines
use pipe-separated format with no shields section. After adding shields
to hero and using a conditional template, only Hero shows the Shields
section; Rogue does not. Final template shows initiative in parens.


SCENARIO 5 — Conditional + dotted-path placeholders (inventory display)
------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m5 inventory 8 8
!match use m5
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 5 5 20
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.type melee
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.damage 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.type ranged
!system set default entity_line_format "{name}: HP {hp}{?inventory?} carrying {inventory}{/?}"
!list
!system set default entity_line_format "{name}: HP {hp} sword_dmg={inventory.sword.damage} bow_dmg={inventory.bow.damage}"
!list
!system set default entity_line_format "{name}: HP {hp} weapon_type={inventory.sword.type}"
!list

Expected: First custom template shows Hero with "carrying {sword, bow}"
summary; Rogue has no inventory so the conditional collapses. Second
template renders concrete numeric values via dotted paths. Third shows the
nested string "melee" for Hero and a "<?inventory.sword.type?>" sentinel
for Rogue (path not present).


SCENARIO 6 — Custom entity_info_format + !ent dump
---------------------------------------------------

!match new m6 info_card 8 8
!match use m6
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero stamina 25
!ent set_var hero max_stamina 50
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!passive add hero regen on_turn_start "entity[self].stamina = entity[self].stamina + 5"
!ent info hero
!system set default entity_info_format "{name} [{id}]\nHP: {hp}/{max_hp}\nStamina: {stamina}/{max_stamina}\nPos: ({x},{y}) facing {facing}{?passives_csv?}\nPassives: {passives_csv}{/?}{?inventory.sword?}\nSword damage: {inventory.sword.damage}{/?}"
!ent info hero
!system set default entity_info_format "BROKEN_TEMPLATE_NO_PLACEHOLDERS"
!ent info hero
!ent dump hero

Expected: First !ent info uses the default multi-line card. Second uses
the custom card with stamina line, passive list, and sword damage all
populated. Third deliberately breaks the template (info renders the
literal string). !ent dump still shows everything: name, position, team,
status, vital var config, full vars json (with nested inventory dict),
and the passives section.


SCENARIO 7 — Help text reflects template-aware behavior
--------------------------------------------------------

!help ent info
!help ent dump
!help passive
!help gpassive add
!help system set
!system rules

Expected: !help ent info and !help ent dump describe the template/raw
distinction. !system rules lists entity_line_format and entity_info_format
with their full descriptions of placeholder + conditional syntax.


SCENARIO 8 — Save/load round-trips templates, passives, state
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m8 saveload 8 8
!match use m8
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 5 5 20
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!passive add hero regen on_turn_start "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 1"
!gpassive add gas on_round_start "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 1"
!system set default entity_line_format "{name} HP:{hp} sword:{inventory.sword.damage}"
!turn next
!store save savetest.json
!match delete m8
!store load savetest.json
!match use m8
!list
!ent info hero
!passive list hero
!gpassive list
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].hp"

Expected: After load, !list still uses the custom template. !ent info
shows the same data. Passives and global passives are restored. The
round_started flag was True after the first !turn next, so on the
loaded match the next !turn next runs the normal advance-and-fire cycle.


SCENARIO 9 — Error handling sanity checks
------------------------------------------

!match new m9 errors 8 8
!match use m9
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!eval "entity[hero].does_not_exist"
!eval "entity[ghost].hp"
!eval "[x for x in range(3)]"
!eval "__import__('os')"
!ent hp self 5
!passive add hero bad on_lunch_break "entity[self].hp = 1"
!passive add hero bad on_turn_start "entity[self].x[0]"
!passive add ghost x on_turn_start "1"
!passive add hero empty on_turn_start ""

Expected: every command in this block should respond with a clear error
message (most prefixed by an X-mark). None should crash or silently
succeed. Specifically: unknown var, unknown entity, list comprehension
not allowed, __import__ not allowed, "self" cannot be used at command
level, bad hook name, subscripting not allowed, ghost entity not found,
empty formula rejected.


SCENARIO 10 — Conditional flow in formulas (if/elif/else, ternary)
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m10 conds 8 8
!match use m10
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero resting yes
!ent set_var hero stamina 5
!eval "5 if entity[hero].hp > 10 else 99"
!eval "if entity[hero].resting == \"yes\":\n    entity[hero].stamina = (entity[hero].stamina + 10) * 2\nelse:\n    entity[hero].stamina = entity[hero].stamina + 2"
!eval "entity[hero].stamina"
!ent set_var hero resting no
!ent set_var hero stamina 5
!eval "if entity[hero].resting == \"yes\":\n    entity[hero].stamina = (entity[hero].stamina + 10) * 2\nelse:\n    entity[hero].stamina = entity[hero].stamina + 2"
!eval "entity[hero].stamina"
!ent set_var hero mode medium
!eval "if entity[hero].mode == \"easy\":\n    entity[hero].hp = 100\nelif entity[hero].mode == \"medium\":\n    entity[hero].hp = 50\nelse:\n    entity[hero].hp = 1"
!eval "entity[hero].hp"
!ent set_var hero revives 1
!eval "if entity[hero].hp <= 50 and entity[hero].revives > 0:\n    entity[hero].hp = entity[hero].max_hp\n    entity[hero].revives = entity[hero].revives - 1"
!eval "entity[hero].hp"
!eval "entity[hero].revives"
!passive add hero conditional_heal on_turn_start "if entity[self].hp < entity[self].max_hp:\n    entity[self].hp = min(entity[self].hp + 5, entity[self].max_hp)"
!ent set_var hero hp 10
!turn next
!eval "entity[hero].hp"
!ent set_var hero blessed 1
!ent set_var hero hp 10
!ent hp hero "$(15 if entity[self].blessed else 5)"
!eval "entity[hero].hp"

Expected: ternary returns 5; first if/else hits then-branch (stamina 5 ->
30); second hits else-branch (5 -> 7); elif chain picks middle branch (hp
-> 50); compound boolean fires revive (hp -> max_hp = 100, revives -> 0);
registered conditional passive fires on next turn (hp 10 -> 15); ternary
inside $() adds 15 to hp (10 -> 25). (hero's max_hp is set to 100 up front
so the hp branches aren't pinned by the default hp <= max_hp clamp — with
the auto-filled max_hp = starting-hp, every branch above 30 would clamp
back to 30.)


SCENARIO 11 — Rejections still hold
------------------------------------

!match new m11 rejects 8 8
!match use m11
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!eval "for x in entity[hero].hp:\n    entity[hero].hp = x"
!eval "while True:\n    entity[hero].hp = 0"
!eval "lambda: entity[hero].hp"
!eval "[x for x in range(3)]"
!eval "x = 5\nentity[hero].hp = x"
!eval "import os"
!passive add hero bad on_turn_start "if True:\n    for x in [1]: entity[self].hp = x"

Expected: every line should print an error (most with an X-mark).
A `for` over a non-loopable iterable (entity[hero].hp is not a
loopable builtin call) is rejected ("for-loop iterable must be a
direct call to one of {...}"); `while` loops, lambdas, list
comprehensions, local-variable assignment, imports, and disallowed
constructs nested inside an otherwise-valid if (the last line nests
a `for x in [1]` — a List iterable, rejected) are all rejected
clearly. None should crash or silently succeed. (Constrained
for-loops over the loopable builtins ARE allowed — see SCENARIO
246+; this scenario only covers the rejection cases.)


SCENARIO 12 — Var hooks: creation events fire at every level
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m12 varhooks 8 8
!match use m12
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!passive add hero log_creates on_var_created target=inventory scope=deep "entity[self].create_log = entity[self].create_log + \"|\" + changed_key"
!ent set_var hero create_log start
!ent set_var hero inventory.gold_pouch.coins 50
!ent set_var hero create_log

Expected: After the !ent set_var to inventory.gold_pouch.coins, the
create_log should read "start|inventory|inventory.gold_pouch|inventory.gold_pouch.coins"
- creation events fire at every newly-created level along the path,
top-down.


SCENARIO 13 — Var hooks: changed only when value differs; removed bottom-up
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m13 varhooks 8 8
!match use m13
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!passive add hero log_changes on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "entity[self].change_log = entity[self].change_log + \"|\" + str(old_value) + \"->\" + str(new_value)"
!ent set_var hero change_log start
!ent set_var hero hp 30
!ent set_var hero hp 20
!ent set_var hero hp 20
!ent set_var hero hp 5
!ent set_var hero change_log

Expected: change_log should be "start|30->20|20->5" — no change event
fires when the same value is written.

!ent set_var hero inventory.spell.fire 10
!ent set_var hero inventory.spell.ice 5
!passive add hero log_removes on_var_removed target=inventory scope=deep "entity[self].removal_log = entity[self].removal_log + \"|\" + changed_key"
!ent set_var hero removal_log start
!ent delete_var hero inventory.spell
!ent set_var hero removal_log

Expected: removal_log reads "start|inventory.spell.fire|inventory.spell.ice|inventory.spell"
- leaves first, then container (bottom-up).


SCENARIO 14 — Scope filtering: exact vs children vs deep
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new m14 scopes 8 8
!match use m14
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!passive add hero ex on_var_created target=inventory scope=exact "entity[self].ex_log = entity[self].ex_log + \"|\" + changed_key"
!passive add hero ch on_var_created target=inventory scope=children "entity[self].ch_log = entity[self].ch_log + \"|\" + changed_key"
!passive add hero dp on_var_created target=inventory scope=deep "entity[self].dp_log = entity[self].dp_log + \"|\" + changed_key"
!ent set_var hero ex_log start
!ent set_var hero ch_log start
!ent set_var hero dp_log start
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!ent set_var hero ex_log
!ent set_var hero ch_log
!ent set_var hero dp_log

Expected:
- ex_log = "start|inventory" (only the exact path)
- ch_log = "start|inventory.sword" (direct child only, not the leaf damage)
- dp_log = "start|inventory|inventory.sword|inventory.sword.damage" (all three)


SCENARIO 15 — on_var_written catch-all with hook_name discrimination
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m15 catchall 8 8
!match use m15
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!passive add hero audit on_var_written target=mood scope=exact "entity[self].audit_log = entity[self].audit_log + \"|\" + hook_name"
!ent set_var hero audit_log start
!ent set_var hero mood happy
!ent set_var hero mood angry
!ent delete_var hero mood
!ent set_var hero audit_log

Expected: audit_log reads "start|on_var_created|on_var_changed|on_var_removed"
- the catch-all on_var_written fires alongside each kind, and hook_name
inside the formula gives you which kind it was.


SCENARIO 16 — Silent removal bypasses hooks
--------------------------------------------

!match new m16 silent 8 8
!match use m16
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero secret 42
!passive add hero observer on_var_removed target=secret scope=exact "entity[self].observed = 1"
!ent delete_var_silent hero secret
!ent info hero

Expected: secret is gone from vars (silent delete worked) but `observed`
is NOT set on the entity — the silent variant bypasses the hook.


SCENARIO 17 — Recursion limit catches infinite loops
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new m17 recurse 8 8
!match use m17
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!system set default var_hook_recursion_limit 5
!ent set_var hero counter 0
!passive add hero loop on_var_changed target=counter scope=exact "entity[self].counter = entity[self].counter + 1"
!ent set_var hero counter 1

Expected: counter advances some number of times bounded by the limit (5),
and the response includes a warning line beginning with "var-hook
recursion limit (5) reached". The chain halts gracefully rather than
hanging the bot.

!system set default var_hook_recursion_limit 128


SCENARIO 18 — Reactive passive: poison drains hp on item removal
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m18 reactive 8 8
!match use m18
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero antidote 1
!passive add hero poison_kicks_in on_var_removed target=antidote scope=exact "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 10"
!ent info hero
!ent delete_var hero antidote
!ent info hero

Expected: Hero starts at HP 30. After deleting antidote, the passive
fires on_var_removed and reduces HP to 20. This is a complete reactive
mechanic written entirely in passives + var hooks — no engine code
changes needed for "thing removed -> consequence."


SCENARIO 19 — Save/load preserves target/scope
-----------------------------------------------

!match new m19 saveload 8 8
!match use m19
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!passive add hero spy on_var_created target=inventory scope=children "entity[self].spy_log = changed_key"
!passive info hero spy
!store save /tmp/m19_save.json
!match delete m19
!store load /tmp/m19_save.json
!match use m19
!passive info hero spy

Expected: !passive info before and after save/load shows the same Target
and Scope fields. The new fields round-trip correctly.


SCENARIO 20 — Property setters route through chokepoint (no more limitation)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m20 chokepoint 8 8
!match use m20
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!passive add hero hp_audit on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "entity[self].hp_audit_log = entity[self].hp_audit_log + \"|\" + str(old_value) + \"->\" + str(new_value)"
!ent set_var hero hp_audit_log start
!ent hp hero -5
!ent hp hero 10
!ent hp hero -8
!ent set_var hero hp_audit_log

Expected: hp_audit_log reads "start|30->25|25->30|30->22" — every !ent hp
command fires on_var_changed via the property setter, which now routes
through the same write_var chokepoint as !ent set_var. (The 25->30 jump
instead of 25->35 is because heal clamps at max_hp=30; not a hook issue.)
Previously these mutations bypassed hooks; now they don't.


SCENARIO 21 — Default soft clamp on hp via max_hp
--------------------------------------------------

!match new m21 clamps 8 8
!match use m21
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero hp 10
!ent hp hero 100
!ent info hero
!ent set_var hero hp 50
!ent set_var hero hp 80

Expected: Hero starts at hp=30/30. After !ent set_var hp 10, hp=10. The
huge heal !ent hp hero 100 raises hp from 10 toward 110 but the default
soft clamp engages (crossing from below max_hp=30), so hp lands at 30.
Then setting hp directly to 50 puts hp above max (since soft is dormant
when not crossing from below — but setting 50 is a write from below the
prior value 30, soft engages, lands at 30). Setting hp to 80 same thing,
soft engages from below, lands at 30.


SCENARIO 22 — Bypass clamp for overheal
----------------------------------------

!match new m22 overheal 8 8
!match use m22
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero hp 10
!ent hp hero 100 bypass_clamp=yes
!ent info hero
!ent set_var hero hp 999 bypass_clamp=yes
!ent info hero

Expected: hp goes from 10 → 110 (bypass lets it exceed max_hp=30), then
the !ent set_var with bypass sets hp=999. Both ack messages mention
"clamp bypassed".


SCENARIO 23 — Entity clamp overrides system clamp
--------------------------------------------------

!match new m23 entclamp 8 8
!match use m23
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!clamp add hero hp max=50 mode=hard
!clamp list hero
!ent set_var hero hp 999

Expected: Hero has an entity-level hard clamp on hp at literal 50, which
overrides the system-level soft clamp by max_hp=30. Writing hp=999 goes
through the entity clamp and lands at 50 (hard clamps always enforce).


SCENARIO 24 — System-level clamp via !gclamp commands
------------------------------------------------------

!match new m24 sysclamp 8 8
!match use m24
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!gclamp list
!gclamp add mana max=100 min=0 mode=soft
!gclamp list
!ent set_var hero mana 150
!ent info hero
!ent set_var hero mana -50
!ent info hero
!gclamp remove mana

Expected: !gclamp list initially shows the default hp clamp shipped in
DEFAULT_SYSTEM_SETTINGS. After adding the mana clamp, the list grows.
Writing mana=150 clamps to 100 (soft, from below). Then writing mana=-50
clamps to 0 (min bound, soft, from above). Removing the clamp shows
"refreshed 1 live match" indicating the active match's rules updated.


SCENARIO 25 — Overheal tracking passive via was_clamped/intended_value
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m25 overheal_track 8 8
!match use m25
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero hp 5
!ent set_var hero overheal_log 0
!passive add hero overheal_track on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "entity[self].overheal_log = entity[self].overheal_log + (intended_value - new_value) if was_clamped else entity[self].overheal_log"
!ent hp hero 100
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero 50

Expected: Hero hp goes from 5 toward 105 but clamps at max_hp=30, so the
overheal passive sees intended_value=105, new_value=30, was_clamped=True
and adds 75 to overheal_log. Second heal of 50: heal_entity computes
30+50=80, write_var clamps to 30. Since new_value=30 equals old_value=30,
no on_var_changed event fires at all (diff produces nothing for unchanged
scalars). So overheal_log stays at 75 — the overheal-as-event model
deliberately doesn't count "tried to heal at full hp" as overheal. If you
want that distinction, route through a separate command/passive that
inspects the heal attempt before it reaches write_var.


SCENARIO 26 — Overheal demo: full mechanic with on_var_write_attempt
---------------------------------------------------------------------

This scenario walks through the three-stage story of overheal tracking:

(A) The existing was_clamped + intended_value mechanism handles "heal
    from below into cap" correctly.
(B) That mechanism misses heals at full HP because they produce no diff.
(C) on_var_write_attempt closes the gap.

!match new m26 overheal_demo 8 8
!match use m26
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10

Setup: Hero has hp=30/30 by default.

Stage A: on_var_changed catches heal-from-below clamping

!ent set_var hero overheal_changed 0
!passive add hero track_changed on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "entity[self].overheal_changed = entity[self].overheal_changed + (intended_value - new_value) if was_clamped else entity[self].overheal_changed"
!ent set_var hero hp 5
!ent hp hero 100
!ent info hero

Expected: hp goes from 5 toward 105 but the default soft clamp engages at
max_hp=30. The on_var_changed event fires with intended_value=105 and
new_value=30, so overheal_changed = 75. This part works perfectly with
just the existing hooks.

Stage B: the gap — heal at full HP produces NO on_var_changed event

!ent hp hero 50
!ent info hero

Expected: hp stays at 30 (already at cap, soft clamp dormant from below
since old=30=cap, write 80 → clamped to 30 — but 30==30 means the diff is
empty and on_var_changed does NOT fire). overheal_changed is still 75
because the tracker never ran. So 50 wasted heal points went unrecorded.
This is the gap the user identified.

Stage C: on_var_write_attempt closes the gap

!ent set_var hero overheal_attempt 0
!passive add hero track_attempt on_var_write_attempt target=hp scope=exact "entity[self].overheal_attempt = entity[self].overheal_attempt + (intended_value - new_value) if intended_value > new_value else entity[self].overheal_attempt"
!ent set_var hero hp 5
!ent hp hero 100
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero 50
!ent info hero

Expected: overheal_attempt = 75 + 50 = 125. The attempt hook fires for
EVERY write to hp regardless of whether the diff produces a change event.
The first heal (5 → clamped to 30) contributes 75; the second heal (30 →
clamped to 30) contributes 50. The user sees the full 125 wasted points.

Why two hooks exist: on_var_changed says "the data actually changed,"
on_var_write_attempt says "a write was attempted." Most game mechanics
want one or the other:
  - HP regen tracking only cares about actual hp gains: on_var_changed
  - Damage taken: on_var_changed (only when hp actually goes down)
  - Overheal accounting: on_var_write_attempt (count all wasted heal)
  - "Audit every interaction with this var": on_var_write_attempt
The on_var_written catch-all subscribes to created/changed/removed but
NOT to attempts, so subscribe to both write_attempt AND written if you
want truly comprehensive auditing.


SCENARIO 27 — on_var_write_attempt fires on bypassed writes
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m27 bypass_attempt 8 8
!match use m27
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero attempt_log ""
!passive add hero audit on_var_write_attempt target=hp scope=exact "entity[self].attempt_log = entity[self].attempt_log + \"|\" + str(intended_value) + \"->\" + str(new_value)"
!ent set_var hero hp 25
!ent hp hero 100 bypass_clamp=yes
!ent set_var hero hp 5
!ent info hero

Expected: attempt_log contains three entries:
  |25->25  (normal write, value under cap, no clamp)
  |130->130  (bypass — was_clamped=False, intended==new)
  |5->5    (normal write)
The bypass write fires the attempt just like any other write — bypass
affects clamping, not observability.


SCENARIO 28 — on_var_write_attempt does NOT fire on removals
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m28 no_attempt_on_remove 8 8
!match use m28
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent set_var hero secret 42
!ent set_var hero remove_attempt_count 0
!passive add hero watch_secret on_var_write_attempt target=secret scope=exact "entity[self].remove_attempt_count = entity[self].remove_attempt_count + 1"
!ent set_var hero secret 99
!ent delete_var hero secret
!ent info hero

Expected: remove_attempt_count = 1 (only the set_var fired the attempt
hook; the delete_var does NOT). Removals have no "no-op gap" — they
either succeed (firing on_var_removed) or raise. There's no need for a
separate "remove attempt" hook, and adding one would be conceptually
muddled.

Expected: level is stored as int 5, title as string, stats as a dict
{str: 12, dex: 14, int: 18}. Auto-coercion turns numeric tokens into

SCENARIO 47 — Deleting a nested subtree drops everything inside it

keys). inventory.potion is unaffected.


SCENARIO 48 — Vital vars cannot be deleted
-------------------------------------------

!match new vital48 Vital 6 6
!match use vital48
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10

!ent delete_var hero max_hp
!ent delete_var hero initiative
!ent delete_var hero inventory

Expected: First three deletions fail with a clear error ("Cannot
delete… vital variable"). The fourth (inventory, not a vital var) would
succeed but doesn't exist, so it also fails — different reason. The
protection prevents accidental destruction of HP-tracking data.


SCENARIO 49 — Silent deletion bypasses hooks
---------------------------------------------

!match new sd49 SilentDel 6 6
!match use sd49
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero observed 0
!ent set_var hero junk 42
!passive add hero watch on_var_removed target=junk scope=exact "entity[self].observed = 1"
!ent delete_var_silent hero junk
!ent info hero

Expected: junk is removed from vars, but the watching passive does NOT
fire. observed stays at 0. The silent variant is for cleanup operations
where cascading effects would be unwanted.


SCENARIO 50 — Reading and writing inside formulas via $(...)
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new sub50 Subst 6 6
!match use sub50
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero strength 8
!ent hp hero "$(entity[this].strength * -2)"
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero "$(entity[this].strength)"
!ent info hero

Expected: First $() evaluates to strength*-2 = -16, applied as damage
(hp drops to 14). Second $() evaluates to strength = 8, applied as heal
(hp goes back up, clamping at max_hp=30 if it exceeds).

LIFECYCLE PASSIVE EXAMPLES

SCENARIO 55 — Stamina regen each turn
--------------------------------------

!match new sta55 Stamina 6 6
!match use sta55
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero stamina 10
!ent set_var hero max_stamina 50
!passive add hero stamina_regen on_turn_start "entity[self].stamina = min(entity[self].stamina + 8, entity[self].max_stamina)"
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: Each on_turn_start fires, stamina increases by 8 capped at 50.
After first turn: 18. After second: 26. (The first !turn next is the
round-1 init that fires on_turn_start without advancing.)


SCENARIO 56 — Poison damage over time
--------------------------------------

!match new pois56 Poison 6 6
!match use pois56
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero poison_stacks 3
!passive add hero poison_dot on_turn_start "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - entity[self].poison_stacks"
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: At the start of each turn, hero loses HP equal to poison_stacks
(3 per turn). Note this passive doesn't decrement stacks — that's a
separate concern, see scenario 57.


SCENARIO 57 — Poison with decaying stacks
------------------------------------------

!match new pois57 PoisonDecay 6 6
!match use pois57
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero poison_stacks 5
!passive add hero poison_tick on_turn_start "if entity[self].poison_stacks > 0:\n    entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - entity[self].poison_stacks\n    entity[self].poison_stacks = entity[self].poison_stacks - 1"
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: Each turn the dot ticks AND poison_stacks decrements by 1.
After three turns: 5+4+3 = 12 damage taken, stacks down to 2. After
poison_stacks hits 0 the conditional skips the body.


SCENARIO 58 — Regen that scales with missing HP (more powerful when wounded)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new heal58 ScaleHeal 6 6
!match use heal58
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero hp 10
!passive add hero adaptive_regen on_turn_start "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + max(2, (entity[self].max_hp - entity[self].hp) // 4)"
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: Heal amount is max(2, missing_hp / 4). At 10/30 (missing 20):
heal 5 → 15/30. At 15/30 (missing 15): heal 3 → 18/30. At 18/30 (missing
12): heal 3 → 21/30. Etc. Adaptive regen heals more when more wounded.


SCENARIO 59 — Round-start global passive: all entities get a small heal
------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new heal59 Hearth 6 6
!match use heal59
!ent add a1 Alpha 30 1 1 10
!ent add a2 Beta 30 2 2 8
!ent set_var a1 hp 15
!ent set_var a2 hp 20

!turn next
!ent info a1
!ent info a2

Expected: on_round_start fires once per entity in turn order. Both
entities heal by 2 at the start of round 1.


SCENARIO 60 — Decrementing duration counters
---------------------------------------------

!match new dur60 Duration 6 6
!match use dur60
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero buff_turns 3

!turn next

!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next

!turn next

there. After 3 !turn next cycles, buff_turns is 0.


SCENARIO 61 — On_entity_spawned: initialize entity-specific state

!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent info hero

Expected: When Hero is spawned, the global passive fires with self=hero
and initializes actions_remaining to 2.


SCENARIO 62 — Round-end cleanup
--------------------------------

!match new clean62 Cleanup 6 6
!match use clean62
!ent add a1 Alpha 30 1 1 10
!ent add a2 Beta 30 2 2 8

!ent set_var a1 actions_remaining 0
!ent set_var a2 actions_remaining 1
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!ent info a1
!ent info a2

Expected: After the round wraps (on_round_end fires), both entities have
actions_remaining reset to 2. The on_round_end fires once per entity in
turn order.


SCENARIO 63 — Turn-end vs turn-start: when to put each kind of tick
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tick63 Tick 6 6
!match use tick63
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero start_count 0
!ent set_var hero end_count 0
!passive add hero start_ticker on_turn_start "entity[self].start_count = entity[self].start_count + 1"
!passive add hero end_ticker on_turn_end "entity[self].end_count = entity[self].end_count + 1"
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: First !turn next: start_count goes 0→1, no advance. Second:
end_count 0→1, advance (only one entity so wraps), start_count 1→2.
Third: end_count 1→2, start_count 2→3.

Useful guidance: on_turn_start for "wake up" effects (regen, buff
refresh); on_turn_end for "end of day" effects (status decay, cooldown
ticks).


===============================================================================
REAL-WORLD GAME MECHANICS
===============================================================================


SCENARIO 64 — Life-to-mana conversion: damage taken refunds mana
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new l2m64 LifeToMana 6 6
!match use l2m64
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero mana 0
!ent set_var hero max_mana 100
!passive add hero blood_mage on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value < old_value:\n    entity[self].mana = min(entity[self].mana + (old_value - new_value) // 2, entity[self].max_mana)"
!ent hp hero -10
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -8
!ent info hero

Expected: First damage: 30→20, hero gains 5 mana. Second damage: 20→12,
hero gains 4 mana (8 damage / 2 = 4). Mana caps at max_mana.


SCENARIO 65 — Thorns: attacker takes damage equal to half what you took
------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new thorn65 Thorns 6 6
!match use thorn65
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 5 5 20
!turn next
!list
!passive add hero thorns on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value < old_value:\n    entity[this].hp = entity[this].hp - (old_value - new_value) // 2"
!ent hp hero -10
!ent info hero
!ent info foe

Expected: Foe has higher initiative so it's the current entity (this).
When hero takes 10 damage, the thorns passive runs with self=hero and
this=foe. Foe takes 5 damage in return (10/2). Note: this is a
simplistic model — a real "attacker" concept will come later with the
damage system.


SCENARIO 66 — Mana shield: damage drains mana first, hp only when mana=0
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new shield66 ManaShield 6 6
!match use shield66
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero mana 20
!ent set_var hero max_mana 50
!passive add hero mana_shield on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value < old_value:\n    entity[self].mana = max(0, entity[self].mana - (old_value - new_value))\n    entity[self].hp = old_value - max(0, (old_value - new_value) - old_mana_amount) if entity[self].mana > 0 else new_value"

This is getting complex. A simpler version:

!passive remove hero mana_shield
!passive add hero mana_absorbs on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value < old_value and entity[self].mana > 0:\n    entity[self].hp = old_value\n    entity[self].mana = max(0, entity[self].mana - (old_value - new_value))"
!ent hp hero -15
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -15
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -15
!ent info hero

Expected: When hp drops, mana absorbs the damage (hp is restored, mana
takes the hit). At mana=20, taking 15 damage restores hp and drops mana
to 5. Next 15 damage: hp would drop to 15, but mana>0 absorbs it (mana
to 0, hp restored). Once mana=0 the passive's condition fails and
damage applies normally.

Note: the mana_absorbs passive itself writes hp, which retriggers
on_var_changed. To avoid infinite loops, the condition mana > 0 must
become false before recursion reaches the limit.


SCENARIO 67 — Lifesteal: healing on every successful hp drop on opponents
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ls67 Lifesteal 6 6
!match use ls67
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 20
!ent add foe Foe 50 5 5 5
!gpassive add lifesteal_for_attacker on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value < old_value and entity[this].id != entity[self].id:\n    entity[this].hp = entity[this].hp + (old_value - new_value) // 2"
!turn next
!list
!ent hp foe -20
!ent info hero
!ent info foe

Expected: Hero is current (higher init). When foe takes 20 damage, the
global lifesteal passive fires with self=foe and this=hero. Since
this.id (hero) != self.id (foe), the conditional triggers and hero
heals for 10 (half of 20).

Note: comparison `entity[this].id != entity[self].id` uses the implicit
id var that gets exposed via the ctx; in your version of the engine,
this might be exposed differently. If `.id` doesn't resolve, store a
duplicate id var: `!ent set_var hero my_id "hero"` and compare those.


SCENARIO 68 — Berserker: damage output scales with missing HP
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ber68 Berserker 6 6
!match use ber68
!ent add hero Berserker 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero base_damage 5
!ent set_var hero hp 6
!eval "entity[hero].base_damage + (entity[hero].max_hp - entity[hero].hp) // 5"

Expected: Damage formula evaluates to base + missing_hp/5 = 5 + 24/5 =
5 + 4 = 9. At full HP it would be 5; at 6 HP it's 9. Use the result
as a damage value: !ent hp foe "$(...)".


SCENARIO 69 — Phase transition: boss changes state below 50% hp
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new boss69 Boss 8 8
!match use boss69
!ent add boss Boss 100 4 4 10
!ent set_var boss phase 1
!ent set_var boss base_attack 5
!passive add boss enrage on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value <= entity[self].max_hp // 2 and entity[self].phase == 1:\n    entity[self].phase = 2\n    entity[self].base_attack = entity[self].base_attack * 2"
!ent hp boss -40
!ent info boss
!ent hp boss -15
!ent info boss

Expected: First damage: hp 100→60, still above 50% (=50), phase stays
1. Second damage: hp 60→45, drops below 50% threshold. Phase becomes 2,
base_attack doubles to 10. The conditional `phase == 1` ensures this
only fires once.


SCENARIO 70 — Shield variable absorbs damage before hp
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new sh70 Shield 6 6
!match use sh70
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero shield 20
!passive add hero shield_absorb on_var_write_attempt target=hp scope=exact "if intended_value < old_value and entity[self].shield > 0:\n    entity[self].shield = max(0, entity[self].shield - (old_value - intended_value))"
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -15
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -15
!ent info hero

Expected: Note this uses on_var_write_attempt because we want to react
even when the resulting hp is unchanged. The passive doesn't actually
prevent hp loss (that would need write modification, deferred). It just
drains shield in parallel: first damage drops shield 20→5 and hp 30→15;
second damage drops shield 5→0 and hp 15→0. For full damage prevention,
wait for the damage system / write modification feature.


SCENARIO 71 — Cooldown timer on a special ability
--------------------------------------------------

!match new cd71 Cooldown 6 6
!match use cd71
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero ult_cooldown 0
!passive add hero cooldown_tick on_turn_end "if entity[self].ult_cooldown > 0:\n    entity[self].ult_cooldown = entity[self].ult_cooldown - 1"
!ent set_var hero ult_cooldown 3
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: ult_cooldown decrements each turn end until it hits 0. The
GM checks `ult_cooldown > 0` before letting the player use the ability,
and sets `ult_cooldown` back to its max value (e.g. 3) when it's used.


SCENARIO 72 — Death save: when hp hits 0, roll a save (counter)
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ds72 DeathSave 6 6
!match use ds72
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero death_saves 0
!ent set_var hero status_downed 0
!passive add hero on_dying on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value <= 0 and entity[self].status_downed == 0:\n    entity[self].status_downed = 1\n    entity[self].hp = 0"
!ent hp hero -50
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -5
!ent info hero

Expected: First massive damage brings hp to 0 (it would have gone
negative but the passive forces it to 0 and sets status_downed). Second
damage: hp is already 0, the conditional doesn't trigger again
(status_downed == 1). The GM can now adjudicate death-save rolls
externally and write back to hp/status_downed.


SCENARIO 73 — Mana cost validation via formula in $()
------------------------------------------------------

!match new mana73 ManaCost 6 6
!match use mana73
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero mana 20
!eval "entity[hero].mana >= 15"
!ent set_var hero mana "$(entity[hero].mana - 15)"
!ent info hero
!eval "entity[hero].mana >= 15"

Expected: First eval returns True (20 >= 15). Cast the spell: mana goes
to 5. Second eval returns False — the GM should reject a further cast.
This pattern lets the GM check resource availability before letting an
action go through.


SCENARIO 74 — Splash damage: write to multiple entities in sequence
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new aoe74 AOE 8 8
!match use aoe74
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe1 Foe1 20 3 3 8
!ent add foe2 Foe2 20 4 4 6
!ent add foe3 Foe3 20 5 5 4
!ent hp foe1 -10
!ent hp foe2 -10
!ent hp foe3 -10
!list

Expected: AOE damage is just multiple !ent hp commands in sequence. No
special machinery — the GM picks the targets. (Or define a passive on
"hp changed on any team-X entity → damage all team-X" using deep scope.)


SCENARIO 75 — Crit chance simulated by GM (manual roll, conditional damage)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new crit75 Crit 6 6
!match use crit75
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero crit_chance 25
!ent set_var hero last_roll 17
!eval "entity[hero].last_roll < entity[hero].crit_chance"
!eval "10 * 2 if entity[hero].last_roll < entity[hero].crit_chance else 10"

Expected: The GM rolls dice externally and writes the result to
last_roll. The eval shows whether a crit occurred, then computes the
final damage (doubled if crit). This pattern keeps the random source
outside the engine — the engine just computes consequences.


SCENARIO 76 — Buff with duration tied to round count
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new buf76 Buff 6 6
!match use buf76
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero rage_turns 0
!ent set_var hero damage_bonus 0
!passive add hero rage_tick on_turn_start "if entity[self].rage_turns > 0:\n    entity[self].rage_turns = entity[self].rage_turns - 1\n    entity[self].damage_bonus = 5\nelse:\n    entity[self].damage_bonus = 0"
!ent set_var hero rage_turns 3
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: When rage_turns is activated to 3, the next 3 turn_starts
keep damage_bonus at 5 and decrement rage_turns. On the 4th turn,
rage_turns is 0, so damage_bonus is set to 0 — buff has expired.


SCENARIO 77 — Aura: global passive applies to every entity each round
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new aura77 Aura 6 6
!match use aura77
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add ally Ally 25 2 2 8
!ent add enemy Enemy 30 5 5 12
!gpassive add inspiring_aura on_round_start "if entity[self].team == \"blue\":\n    entity[self].morale_bonus = 2\nelse:\n    entity[self].morale_bonus = 0"
!ent team hero blue
!ent team ally blue
!ent team enemy red
!turn next
!ent info hero
!ent info ally
!ent info enemy

Expected: At round start, the aura fires once per entity. Blue team
members (hero, ally) get morale_bonus=2; red team (enemy) gets
morale_bonus=0. Globals iterate over every entity in turn order.


SCENARIO 78 — XP gain tracked on entity, level-up via passive
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new xp78 XP 6 6
!match use xp78
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero level 1
!ent set_var hero xp 0
!ent set_var hero xp_to_next 100
!passive add hero level_up on_var_changed target=xp scope=exact "if new_value >= entity[self].xp_to_next:\n    entity[self].level = entity[self].level + 1\n    entity[self].xp = new_value - entity[self].xp_to_next\n    entity[self].xp_to_next = entity[self].xp_to_next + 50"
!ent set_var hero xp 60
!ent info hero
!ent set_var hero xp 110

Expected: First xp gain: 60 stays below threshold (100), level stays 1.
Second: xp=110 triggers level up. Level becomes 2, leftover xp = 110-100
= 10, threshold raises to 150. The level_up passive fires when xp
changes — recursion from the passive's own writes is contained because
the conditions stop triggering after the level-up.


SCENARIO 79 — Spell that costs mana AND has a duration
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new spell79 Spell 6 6
!match use spell79
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero mana 50
!ent set_var hero shield_turns 0
!ent set_var hero shield_active 0
!ent set_var hero mana "$(entity[this].mana - 20)"
!ent set_var hero shield_turns 3
!ent set_var hero shield_active 1
!passive add hero shield_decay on_turn_start "if entity[self].shield_turns > 0:\n    entity[self].shield_turns = entity[self].shield_turns - 1\nelse:\n    entity[self].shield_active = 0"
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: Casting the spell costs 20 mana (50→30) and sets shield_turns
to 3 + shield_active to 1. Each turn_start, the decay passive ticks
turns down. After 3 turns reach 0, shield_active goes to 0 on the next
turn_start where shield_turns is already 0.


SCENARIO 80 — Resistance: damage multiplier based on type
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new res80 Resist 6 6
!match use res80
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero resist_fire 50
!ent set_var hero resist_ice 0
!eval "20 * (100 - entity[hero].resist_fire) // 100"
!eval "20 * (100 - entity[hero].resist_ice) // 100"

Expected: Hero has 50% fire resistance and 0% ice resistance. Computed
damage: fire 20 * 50/100 = 10, ice 20 * 100/100 = 20. Apply via
!ent hp hero "$(...)" with the appropriate calculation.


SCENARIO 81 — Counter-attack: when you dodge, you hit back
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new ctr81 Counter 6 6
!match use ctr81
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 5 5 20
!turn next
!list
!ent set_var hero counter_damage 7
!passive add hero counter_strike on_var_changed target=last_dodge scope=exact "if new_value == 1:\n    entity[this].hp = entity[this].hp - entity[self].counter_damage\n    entity[self].last_dodge = 0"
!ent set_var hero last_dodge 1
!ent info foe

Expected: When the GM signals a dodge by setting last_dodge=1, the
passive fires: applies counter_damage to "this" (the current turn entity
= foe), then resets last_dodge so the passive doesn't loop. Foe takes 7
damage from the counter.


SCENARIO 82 — Status durations stored as a dict
------------------------------------------------

!match new sd82 StatusDict 6 6
!match use sd82
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero effects.burning.duration 3
!ent set_var hero effects.burning.damage 2
!ent set_var hero effects.frozen.duration 2
!ent dump hero

Expected: effects is a nested dict mapping status name → its parameters.
A passive could iterate (in pseudocode) but the formula language doesn't
support iteration — so the GM would write one passive per status or
hardcode the dotted paths. See scenario 83 for a workable pattern.


SCENARIO 83 — Multiple-status DOT with per-status passives
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdot83 MultiDot 6 6
!match use mdot83
!ent add hero Hero 50 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero burn_turns 3
!ent set_var hero poison_turns 2
!passive add hero burn_tick on_turn_start "if entity[self].burn_turns > 0:\n    entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 3\n    entity[self].burn_turns = entity[self].burn_turns - 1"
!passive add hero poison_tick on_turn_start "if entity[self].poison_turns > 0:\n    entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 2\n    entity[self].poison_turns = entity[self].poison_turns - 1"
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: Two passives fire on each turn_start. First turn: burn 3,
poison 2, hp 50→45. Burn_turns 2, poison_turns 1. Second turn: burn 3,
poison 2, hp 45→40. Burn_turns 1, poison_turns 0. Third turn: burn 3
only, hp 40→37. Burn_turns 0.

VAR HOOK ADVANCED EXAMPLES

SCENARIO 84 — On_var_created: trigger when first picked up
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new pickup84 Pickup 6 6
!match use pickup84
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero pickup_log ""
!passive add hero on_pickup on_var_created target=inventory scope=children "entity[self].pickup_log = entity[self].pickup_log + \"|\" + changed_key"
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!ent set_var hero inventory.potion.healing 20
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.weight 5
!ent info hero

Expected: pickup_log shows "|inventory.sword|inventory.potion" — both
were direct children of inventory and were newly created. The sword.weight
write doesn't fire the children-scope passive because weight is two
levels deep.


SCENARIO 85 — On_var_removed: clean up when an item leaves
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new rm85 RemoveItem 6 6
!match use rm85
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!ent set_var hero attuned_to "sword"
!passive add hero unattune on_var_removed target=inventory.sword scope=exact "if entity[self].attuned_to == \"sword\":\n    entity[self].attuned_to = \"\""
!ent delete_var hero inventory.sword
!ent info hero

Expected: When the sword is removed, the passive checks if the entity
was attuned to it. Since attuned_to == "sword", it gets cleared.


SCENARIO 86 — Deep watch: track every change inside an inventory subtree
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dw86 DeepWatch 6 6
!match use dw86
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero audit_log ""
!passive add hero inv_audit on_var_written target=inventory scope=deep "entity[self].audit_log = entity[self].audit_log + \"|\" + hook_name + \":\" + changed_key"
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 15
!ent delete_var hero inventory.sword
!ent info hero

Expected: audit_log accumulates created events for inventory, sword,
damage; one changed event for damage (12→15); removed events for damage
and sword (bottom-up). The catch-all on_var_written catches all of
created/changed/removed but NOT on_var_write_attempt.


SCENARIO 87 — Use intended_value to validate writes that would have been wasted
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new iv87 IntendedValue 6 6
!match use iv87
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero wasted_heal_log 0
!passive add hero heal_audit on_var_write_attempt target=hp scope=exact "if intended_value > old_value and intended_value > new_value:\n    entity[self].wasted_heal_log = entity[self].wasted_heal_log + (intended_value - new_value)"
!ent set_var hero hp 25
!ent hp hero 100
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero 30

Expected: First heal: intended=125, new=30, wasted=95. Counter += 95.
Second heal at full: intended=60, new=30, wasted=30. Counter += 30.
Final wasted_heal_log = 125. The passive catches both because it fires
on every write attempt, not just diff-producing ones.


SCENARIO 88 — Root-watch passive (target="" scope=deep): audit everything
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new root88 RootWatch 6 6
!match use root88
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero touches 0
!passive add hero touch_count on_var_changed target= scope=deep "entity[self].touches = entity[self].touches + 1"
!ent set_var hero mana 50
!ent set_var hero stamina 30
!ent set_var hero gold 100
!ent info hero

Expected: Empty target with deep scope catches every var change on the
entity. Note: writes to "touches" itself also count, which leads to
quick recursion — the formula increments touches, which fires another
on_var_changed, etc. The recursion limit catches it. To avoid: scope
narrower, or check `if changed_key != "touches"` in the formula.


SCENARIO 89 — Was_clamped flag distinguishes natural changes from clamped ones
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new wc89 WasClamped 6 6
!match use wc89
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero hp 5
!ent set_var hero clamped_count 0
!ent set_var hero unclamped_count 0
!passive add hero distinguish on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if was_clamped:\n    entity[self].clamped_count = entity[self].clamped_count + 1\nelse:\n    entity[self].unclamped_count = entity[self].unclamped_count + 1"
!ent hp hero 3
!ent hp hero 100
!ent hp hero -10
!ent info hero

Expected: First heal (+3): hp 5→8, no clamp, unclamped_count → 1.
Second heal (+100): hp 8→30 (clamped), clamped_count → 1.
Third damage (-10): hp 30→20, no clamp, unclamped_count → 2.


SCENARIO 90 — Hook_name discriminator inside on_var_written
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new hn90 HookName 6 6
!match use hn90
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero created_count 0
!ent set_var hero changed_count 0
!ent set_var hero removed_count 0
!passive add hero discriminator on_var_written target=mana scope=exact "if hook_name == \"on_var_created\":\n    entity[self].created_count = entity[self].created_count + 1\nelif hook_name == \"on_var_changed\":\n    entity[self].changed_count = entity[self].changed_count + 1\nelse:\n    entity[self].removed_count = entity[self].removed_count + 1"
!ent set_var hero mana 50
!ent set_var hero mana 30
!ent set_var hero mana 30
!ent delete_var hero mana
!ent info hero

Expected: created_count=1 (first set), changed_count=1 (50→30; same
value 30→30 fires nothing because no diff), removed_count=1 (delete).

CLAMP MECHANICS AND EDGE CASES

SCENARIO 91 — Multiple clamps on one entity
--------------------------------------------

!match new mc91 MultiClamp 6 6
!match use mc91
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!clamp add hero mana max=100 min=0 mode=soft
!clamp add hero stamina max=50 min=0 mode=hard
!clamp add hero rage max=10 mode=soft
!clamp list hero
!ent set_var hero mana 150
!ent set_var hero stamina -10
!ent set_var hero rage 20
!ent info hero

Expected: mana clamps to 100, stamina to 0 (hard min), rage to 10.


SCENARIO 92 — Cross-variable clamp: damage clamped by armor
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cv92 CrossVarClamp 6 6
!match use cv92
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero max_focus 50
!clamp add hero focus max=max_focus min=0 mode=soft
!ent set_var hero focus 100
!ent info hero
!ent set_var hero max_focus 30
!ent set_var hero focus 100

Expected: First write of focus=100 clamps to 50. Lowering max_focus to
30 doesn't retroactively clamp the existing focus value (still 50 due
to soft semantics — "no retroactive"). But the next write attempt uses
the new max: focus=100 clamps to 30.


SCENARIO 93 — Hard clamp pulls a value down when it's already over
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new hc93 HardClamp 6 6
!match use hc93
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero hp 999 bypass_clamp=yes
!ent info hero
!clamp add hero hp max=max_hp mode=hard
!ent hp hero -1
!ent info hero

Expected: Hp is 999 (bypassed). Adding a hard clamp. The next hp
adjustment (heal/damage) goes through write_var, which engages the
clamp on the NEW value (999 - 1 = 998, clamped to 30 because hard
always enforces).


SCENARIO 94 — Soft clamp DOES NOT pull a value down when it's already over
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new sc94 SoftClamp 6 6
!match use sc94
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero hp 999 bypass_clamp=yes
!ent hp hero -1
!ent info hero

Expected: hp is 999 (bypassed). Hp loss of 1 brings it to 998. The
default soft clamp doesn't engage because the prior value (999) was
already over the cap — soft is dormant in this direction.


SCENARIO 95 — Bypass clamp for overheal scaling
------------------------------------------------

!match new oh95 Overheal 6 6
!match use oh95
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero hp 25
!ent hp hero 50 bypass_clamp=yes
!ent info hero

Expected: Heal 25→75, bypassing the max_hp=30 clamp. Useful for
characters with explicit overheal mechanics where the normal cap
doesn't apply (e.g. a paladin's overheal-as-shield).


SCENARIO 96 — System-level clamp via !gclamp commands
------------------------------------------------------

!match new syscl96 SysClamp 6 6
!match use syscl96
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!gclamp list
!gclamp add stamina max=50 min=0 mode=soft
!gclamp list
!ent set_var hero stamina 999
!ent info hero
!ent set_var hero stamina -5
!ent info hero
!gclamp remove stamina

Expected: gclamp shows the default hp clamp and the new stamina clamp.
Stamina writes get clamped per the rule: 999→50, -5→0.


SCENARIO 97 — Removing the default hp clamp lets hp go free
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new free97 FreeHp 6 6
!match use free97
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!gclamp remove hp
!ent hp hero 100
!ent info hero
!gclamp add hp max=max_hp mode=soft

Expected: Without the hp clamp, hp goes to 130 freely after a +100 heal.
(Reminder: re-add the clamp for normal use — most game systems want it
on by default.)


SCENARIO 98 — Min-only clamp (floor without ceiling)
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new floor98 MinOnly 6 6
!match use floor98
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!clamp add hero debt min=0 mode=hard
!ent set_var hero debt 100
!ent set_var hero debt -50
!ent info hero

Expected: Setting debt to 100 succeeds (no max). Setting it to -50 hits
the hard min and clamps to 0.


SCENARIO 99 — Min > max at config time → fails fast
----------------------------------------------------

!match new bad99 BadClamp 6 6
!match use bad99
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!clamp add hero x min=10 max=5 mode=hard

Expected: Error message about min > max. The clamp is NOT added; !clamp
list shows nothing.


SCENARIO 100 — Non-numeric writes bypass clamps
------------------------------------------------

!match new str100 StringWrite 6 6
!match use str100
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!clamp add hero status max=10 mode=hard
!ent set_var hero status "knocked_out"
!ent info hero

Expected: status is a string. The clamp only applies to numeric writes,
so the string passes through unchanged.

SCENARIO 108 — Full match round-trip
-------------------------------------

!match new save108 SaveTest 6 6
!match use save108
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10

!clamp add hero mana max=100 mode=soft
!turn next
!store save /tmp/save108.json
!match delete save108
!store load /tmp/save108.json
!match use save108
!list
!ent info hero
!passive list hero
!clamp list hero

Expected: All state survives the round-trip: entity vars including
nested inventory, the regen passive, the mana clamp, the current turn
state (round_started=True).

SCENARIO 112 — $() with self binding
-------------------------------------

!match new arg112 ArgSelf 6 6
!match use arg112
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10

!ent hp hero "$(entity[self].atk * -1)"
!ent info hero

Expected: $() evaluates with self=hero (the entity in arg[1] of !ent hp).
entity[self].atk * -1 = -8, applied as damage. Hp: 30→22.


SCENARIO 113 — $() with this binding (current-turn entity)

Expected: Foe is current (init=20). $() resolves this=foe. Foe's
weapon_dmg=12 becomes -12 damage to hero. Hero hp: 30→18.

SCENARIO 118 — If/elif/else statement
--------------------------------------

!match new if118 IfElif 6 6
!match use if118
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero mode normal
!eval "if entity[hero].mode == \"easy\":\n    entity[hero].score = 100\nelif entity[hero].mode == \"normal\":\n    entity[hero].score = 50\nelse:\n    entity[hero].score = 10"
!ent info hero

Expected: mode=normal hits elif, score=50.


SCENARIO 119 — Compound boolean conditions
-------------------------------------------

!match new bool119 Bool 6 6
!match use bool119
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero level 5
!ent set_var hero quest_done 1
!eval "entity[hero].level >= 5 and entity[hero].quest_done == 1"
!eval "entity[hero].level >= 10 or entity[hero].quest_done == 1"
!eval "not (entity[hero].level < 3)"

Expected: True, True, True. Standard Python boolean ops work in formulas.


SCENARIO 120 — Built-in functions
----------------------------------

!match new fn120 Funcs 6 6
!match use fn120
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!eval "min(5, 10)"
!eval "max(5, 10, 8)"
!eval "abs(-7)"
!eval "round(3.6)"
!eval "int(3.9)"
!eval "float(5)"

Expected: 5, 10, 7, 4, 3, 5.0. Whitelisted: min, max, abs, round, int,
float, str.


SCENARIO 121 — Loops are constrained, not blanket-disallowed
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rej121 Reject 6 6
!match use rej121
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!eval "for x in range(3): entity[hero].hp = x"
!eval "for x in entity[hero].hp: entity[hero].hp = x"
!eval "while True: entity[hero].hp = 0"

Expected: `while` loops are still fully disallowed ("Disallowed
syntax: While"). `for` loops ARE allowed, but only over a direct
call to one of the loopable builtins (entities_within,
group_members, cells_in_burst, cells_in_line, cells_in_cone) — so
`for x in range(3)` is rejected because `range` isn't an allowed
function, and `for x in entity[hero].hp` is rejected because the
iterable isn't a loopable call ("for-loop iterable must be a
direct call to one of {...}"). See SCENARIO 246+ for the legal
for-loop forms.


SCENARIO 122 — Disallowed: lambdas, comprehensions, imports
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rej122 Reject 6 6
!match use rej122
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!eval "(lambda x: x)(5)"
!eval "[x for x in range(3)]"
!eval "import os"

Expected: All three rejected.


SCENARIO 123 — Disallowed: subscripting non-entity values
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new rej123 Reject 6 6
!match use rej123
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!eval "entity[hero].x[0]"

Expected: Rejected. The only allowed subscript is `entity[X]`.


SCENARIO 124 — Disallowed: attribute access on non-entity
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new rej124 Reject 6 6
!match use rej124
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!eval "min.foo"

Expected: Rejected. Attribute access is only valid on `entity[X].path`.


SCENARIO 125 — Self unbound at command level
---------------------------------------------

!match use self125
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent hp self 5
!eval "entity[self].hp"

Expected: Both fail. `self` is only bound inside passive formulas and
as the implicit "target entity" in $() arg substitution.

the var first or use a ternary.

SCENARIO 130 — Conditional damage tier (rage-based)
----------------------------------------------------

Expected: 5 (rage<30), 10 (30<=rage<70), 20 (rage>=70). Nested ternaries
let the GM tier damage by a resource level.


SCENARIO 131 — Curse mark that triggers when crossed
-----------------------------------------------------

!ent hp hero -10
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -8
!ent info hero
!ent hp hero -1
!ent info hero

Expected: First damage 25→15, not yet below 10. Second damage 15→7,
crosses below 10, curse triggers — extra -5 → hp=2. curse_triggered=1
so subsequent damage doesn't retrigger. Third damage 2→1.


SCENARIO 132 — Counter-attack damage based on enemy's missing HP
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ca132 ExecCounter 6 6
!match use ca132
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 100 5 5 20
!turn next
!ent set_var foe hp 20
!ent hp hero "$((entity[this].max_hp - entity[this].hp) // 5)"
!ent info hero

Expected: Foe (this) is at 20/100, missing 80. Execute heal scales with
foe's wound: 80/5 = 16 heal for hero. Hero hp 30 + 16 = 46, but clamps
to max_hp=30 due to default soft clamp. Hero info shows 30.

Expected: First, foe takes 25 damage (50→25, well within max). Second,
the GM uses bypass_clamp to force hp to 5 (simulating "true damage" or
a debug override that ignores clamps).


SCENARIO 134 — Multi-stage boss with health gates
--------------------------------------------------

!match new boss134 BossGates 8 8
!match use boss134
!ent add boss Boss 200 4 4 10
!ent set_var boss phase 1
!ent set_var boss enraged 0
!passive add boss phase_2_gate on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value <= entity[self].max_hp * 3 // 4 and entity[self].phase < 2:\n    entity[self].phase = 2"
!passive add boss phase_3_gate on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value <= entity[self].max_hp // 2 and entity[self].phase < 3:\n    entity[self].phase = 3"
!passive add boss enrage_gate on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value <= entity[self].max_hp // 4 and entity[self].enraged == 0:\n    entity[self].enraged = 1"
!ent hp boss -60
!ent info boss
!ent hp boss -50
!ent info boss
!ent hp boss -60
!ent info boss

Expected: Phase advances as hp crosses 75%, 50%, 25% thresholds.
Damage 60→140: phase 2 triggers (140 <= 150). Damage 50→90: phase 3
triggers (90 <= 100). Damage 60→30: enraged triggers (30 <= 50).
Multiple passives on the same hook all fire; conditions ensure each
transition runs exactly once.


SCENARIO 135 — Heal-on-kill: when enemy hp hits 0, allies heal
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new hok135 HealKill 6 6
!match use hok135
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent team hero blue
!ent add foe Foe 20 5 5 20
!ent team foe red
!gpassive add heal_on_kill on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value <= 0 and entity[self].team != entity[this].team and entity[this].team == \"blue\":\n    entity[this].hp = entity[this].hp + 5"
!turn next
!ent set_var hero hp 15
!ent hp foe -25
!ent info hero
!ent info foe

Expected: Foe is current (init=20). Hero damages foe; foe.hp drops to
-5 (or 0 depending on min clamp). The heal_on_kill global fires with
self=foe and this=foe (since on_var_changed fires for the entity whose
var changed, "this" is the current-turn entity)... actually wait, the
intent here is to heal the OPPOSING team's ally. The model would need
an attacker concept. For now this scenario demonstrates the conditional
syntax but the actual mechanic needs the future damage system.

SCENARIO 138 — Mirror match: copy stats from another entity

hero.atk changes later, mirror.atk won't update.


SCENARIO 139 — Aggregate damage check across multiple sources
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new agg139 Aggregate 6 6
!match use agg139
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero turn_damage 0
!passive add hero start_turn on_turn_start "entity[self].turn_damage = 0"
!passive add hero accumulate on_var_changed target=hp scope=exact "if new_value < old_value:\n    entity[self].turn_damage = entity[self].turn_damage + (old_value - new_value)"
!turn next
!ent hp hero -3
!ent hp hero -5
!ent hp hero -2
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero

Expected: Across the turn, hero takes 3+5+2=10 damage, turn_damage=10.
At the next turn_start, turn_damage resets to 0. Useful for "if you
took more than 15 damage this turn, X happens" mechanics.


SCENARIO 140 — Channeled ability: must stay still
--------------------------------------------------

!match new ch140 Channel 6 6
!match use ch140
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero channeling 1
!ent set_var hero channel_x 3
!ent set_var hero channel_y 3

!ent info hero
!ent tp hero 4 3
!ent info hero

Expected: Hero starts channeling at (3,3). Teleporting to (4,3) changes
x from 3 to 4. The passive sees x changed and channel_x is still 3, so
it sets channeling=0. Note: this requires var hooks on x, which depends
on x being routed through write_var — that's outside this commit's
scope. The scenario demonstrates the pattern; if x isn't watched, the
mechanic won't trigger.

SCENARIO 144 — Periodic event: every 3 turns, something happens

1,2,3→0+pulse,1,2,3→0+pulse,1,2... after 8 starts pulse_count = 2.


SCENARIO 145 — Variable type-coercion gotcha: number vs string
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tc145 TypeCoerce 6 6
!match use tc145
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero count 5
!ent set_var hero label "5"
!eval "entity[hero].count == 5"
!eval "entity[hero].label == \"5\""
!eval "entity[hero].count == entity[hero].label"

Expected: True, True, False. !ent set_var auto-coerces "5" to int 5
when the value is bare; quoted "5" stays a string. The third comparison
shows int 5 != string "5".

entity. Entity card shows the full character sheet.

SCENARIO 150 — Demonstration of two scopes interacting
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new sc150 ScopeMix 6 6
!match use sc150
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero direct_hits 0
!ent set_var hero deep_hits 0
!passive add hero direct on_var_changed target=loadout scope=children "entity[self].direct_hits = entity[self].direct_hits + 1"
!passive add hero deep on_var_changed target=loadout scope=deep "entity[self].deep_hits = entity[self].deep_hits + 1"
!ent set_var hero loadout.weapon "sword"
!ent set_var hero loadout.weapon "axe"
!ent set_var hero loadout.gear.boots "leather"
!ent set_var hero loadout.gear.boots "iron"
!ent info hero

Expected: First write: creates loadout, loadout.weapon (children + deep
both watching at their respective paths fire creation NOT change so
counters stay 0). Second write changes loadout.weapon (sword→axe):
direct fires (children of loadout), deep fires. Counters: direct=1,
deep=1 — wait, deep also matches loadout itself but the changed event
fires on loadout.weapon. So deep_hits=1. Third write creates
loadout.gear and loadout.gear.boots (no change event). Fourth changes
loadout.gear.boots: deep matches (boots is descendant of loadout),
direct does NOT (boots is two levels deep, not a direct child).
Final: direct=1 (just the weapon change), deep=2 (weapon and boots
changes).

Note: this scenario tests the precise scope semantics. Verify by
inspecting both counters in !ent info.


SCENARIO 151 — Demonstration of save/load equivalence
------------------------------------------------------

!match new eq151 Equiv 6 6
!match use eq151
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero mana 50
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 12
!passive add hero regen on_turn_start "entity[self].mana = entity[self].mana + 5"
!clamp add hero mana max=100 mode=soft
!turn next
!turn next
!ent info hero
!store save /tmp/eq151_before.json
!store load /tmp/eq151_before.json
!ent info hero

Expected: !ent info before save and after load show identical state.
This is the strongest validation that serialization is complete and
lossless — including round count, current entity, turn_started flag,
passives, clamps, and nested vars.

!turn next

registered (insertion order in the dict).

SCENARIO 156 — Buggy passive doesn't crash siblings

log shows a "CRASHED" line for it. The good passive still fires
normally; good_tick=1. Per-passive errors don't abort other passives.


SCENARIO 157 — Diagonal directions rejected by default
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new m29 cardinal_only 8 8
!match use m29
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent face hero up
!map
!ent move hero ne
!ent face hero up_left
!ent face hero nw
!ent move hero up_right
!ent move hero u
!map

Expected: Hero renders as ^ on the first map (single-cell ASCII glyph,
unambiguous for cardinals). Both diagonal move attempts (ne, up_right)
and both diagonal face attempts (up_left, nw) are rejected with
"Diagonal ... not allowed" errors, since allow_diagonal_movement and
allow_diagonal_facing both default to False. The cardinal move 'u'
still works, leaving Hero at (4,3) facing ^ on the second map.


SCENARIO 158 — Enabling diagonal movement and facing
----------------------------------------------------

!match new m30 eight_way 8 8
!match use m30
!system set default allow_diagonal_movement true
!system set default allow_diagonal_facing true
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent move hero ne
!ent move hero 2 down_right
!ent face hero ul
!ent face hero south-east
!map
!ent dump hero

Expected: After enabling both diagonal rules and refreshing the live
match, Hero starts at (4,4). 'ne' moves to (5,3) facing up_right;
'2 down_right' moves to (7,5) facing down_right. The face commands
accept compact ('ul' → up_left), hyphenated ('south-east' →
down_right), and any other alias forms. The map renders Hero as a
diagonal slash glyph — '/' for up_right/down_left, '\\' for
up_left/down_right (ambiguous within each pair; check !ent dump for
exact facing). Reset the rules afterward with
  !system set default allow_diagonal_movement false
  !system set default allow_diagonal_facing false
if you plan to run other scenarios in the same session.


SCENARIO 159 — Rotation via !ent face <cw|ccw> (4-way and 8-way)
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m31 rotation 8 8
!match use m31
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent face hero up
!ent face hero cw
!ent face hero clockwise
!ent face hero ccw
!ent face hero counterclockwise
!ent face hero ccw
!system set default allow_diagonal_facing true
!ent face hero up
!ent face hero cw
!ent face hero cw
!ent face hero cw
!ent face hero turn_right
!ent face hero turn_left

Expected: In cardinal-only mode the 4-step cw cycle is up → right →
down (the 'clockwise' alias is identical to 'cw'). The two ccw
rotations then walk back: down → right → up. One more ccw goes
up → left. After enabling diagonal facing and resetting to up, the
8-step ring runs up → up_right → right → down_right (the turn_right
alias steps it once more to down), and turn_left rotates one step
back to down_right.


SCENARIO 160 — Rotation snap when current facing is off the rotation ring
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new m32 rotation_snap 8 8
!match use m32
!system set default allow_diagonal_facing true
!ent add hero Hero 30 4 4 10
!ent face hero up_right
!system set default allow_diagonal_facing false
!ent face hero cw
!system set default allow_diagonal_facing true
!ent face hero up_right
!system set default allow_diagonal_facing false
!ent face hero ccw

Expected: Enable diagonal facing, set facing to up_right, then disable
the rule. The entity's facing is now "off-ring" relative to the active
4-cardinal rotation order. !ent face hero cw snaps forward a single
step to the next cardinal in the clockwise direction: right. Re-enable
diagonals just long enough to reset facing back to up_right, then
disable again and rotate ccw — snaps back the other way to up. Off-ring
rotation always resolves in one step, never spinning through directions
the current system has disallowed.


SCENARIO 161 — Group registry: create, add, info, remove, delete
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mgrp1 GroupRegistry 8 8

!ent add b B 30 2 1 11
!ent add c C 30 3 1 12
!ent group new swarm

!ent group add swarm a b

!ent group add swarm c

!ent group list

!ent group add elite a

!ent group info swarm

!ent group list
!ent group info elite

Expected: 'new swarm' creates an empty group; 'list' shows it with

SCENARIO 162 — Iterating !ent subcommands across a group
---------------------------------------------------------

!ent add c C 30 3 1 12

Expected: '!ent hp group:mooks -5' damages each of a, b, c by 5
(three separate ack lines, one per member). 'set_var group:mooks

SCENARIO 163 — Atomic group movement with self-passthrough
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new mgrp3 GroupMove 10 6
!match use mgrp3
!ent add a A 30 2 3 10
!ent add b B 30 3 3 11
!ent add c C 30 4 3 12
!ent add obstacle_entity obstacle_entity 30 7 3 1
!ent group new line
!ent group add line a b c
!map
!ent move group:line right
!map
!ent move group:line right right
!map
!ent move group:line right
!map
!ent remove obstacle_entity
!ent move group:line right right
!map

Expected: The line {a,b,c} sits at x=2,3,4 on row 3 with a obstacle_entity at
x=7. First 'move right' shifts to x=3,4,5 — fellow members are
transparent so a "moves into" b's old cell with no false collision.
'move right right' would put c on (7,3) which is the obstacle_entity: abort,
the map is unchanged, none of a/b/c moved (atomic). 'move right'
alone shifts to x=4,5,6 — fine, c stops short of the obstacle_entity. After
removing the obstacle_entity, 'move right right' completes; the group lands at
x=6,7,8.


SCENARIO 164 — group: target rejected for incompatible subcommands
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mgrp4 GroupReject 8 8
!match use mgrp4
!ent add a A 30 1 1 10
!ent add b B 30 2 1 11
!ent group new pair
!ent group add pair a b
!ent tp group:pair 3 3
!ent rename group:pair Renamed
!ent clone group:pair clone 5 5
!ent add group:newentity New 30 1 4

Expected: All four commands return errors. tp/rename/clone all need
a single per-call target (a unique destination cell, a single new
name, a single new id) — they can't sensibly fan out across a group.
'!ent add group:newentity' fails too: a creation command takes a
NEW id, not a group target. None of these commands silently iterate
or partially apply.
