!eval "len(clip_cells(cells_in_burst(1, 1, 2)))"
!eval "clip_cells(cells_in_rect(4, 4, 9, 9))"

Expected: `cells_in_rect(x1, y1, x2, y2)` returns every cell in
the axis-aligned rectangle between the two corners, inclusive,
sorted in (x,y) order — the rectangular twin of cells_in_burst.
(2,2)-(4,3) is a 3x2 block = 6 cells; (2,2)-(4,4) is 3x3 = 9.
Corner order doesn't matter, so (4,3,2,2) gives the same cells as
(2,2,4,3). Like the other cells_in_* helpers it isn't clipped to
the grid: cells_in_burst(1,1,2) yields 25 cells (a 5x5 block
centered on the corner), many off-grid. `clip_cells(cells)` drops
the off-grid ones — here 25 -> 9 (the on-grid quarter). The final
rect (4,4)-(9,9) on a 6x6 grid clips to the (4..6, 4..6) corner =
9 cells.


SCENARIO 376 — entities_in_line / _cone / _rect: entity-returning area twins
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ment EntArea 6 6
!match use ment
!ent add a A 10 2 2 9
!ent add b B 10 3 3 9
!ent add c C 10 4 4 9
!ent add d D 10 6 6 9
!ent add off O 10 3 1 9
!eval "entities_in_rect(2, 2, 4, 4)"
!eval "entities_in_line_ignorelos(2, 2, 4, 4)"
!eval "entities_in_cone(1, 1, 'down_right', 10, 30)"

Expected: the entity-returning twins of the cells_in_* shapes —
each returns the ALIVE entity ids standing on the shape's cells
(entities_in_area already covers the burst/radius case). With a,b,c
on the (2,2)->(4,4) diagonal, d at (6,6), and off at (3,1):
entities_in_rect(2,2,4,4) = [a, b, c] (d and off are outside the
rectangle). entities_in_line_ignorelos(2,2,4,4) walks the beam
start->end and returns [a, b, c] in that order (nearest first;
endpoints included, walls ignored). entities_in_cone
from (1,1) down the down-right diagonal with a narrow 30° half-angle
catches the whole diagonal — [a, b, c, d] sorted by distance — while
off (90° off the centerline) is excluded. Filter by team/relation
inside a `for` loop; all three are loopable, e.g. an AoE action does
`for eid in entities_in_rect(...): entity[eid].hp = entity[eid].hp - dmg`.


SCENARIO 229 — Spatial helpers compose with passives and functions
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mgeo6 SpatialCompose 12 12
!match use mgeo6
!ent add mage Mage 30 5 5 10
!ent set_var mage team blue
!ent add foe1 Foe1 20 5 6 8
!ent set_var foe1 team red
!ent add foe2 Foe2 20 6 5 7
!ent set_var foe2 team red
!ent add bystander Bystander 30 5 4 6
!ent set_var bystander team blue
!func def foes_adjacent eid "len(entities_within(eid, 1, 'square_radius_distance', 'hostile'))"
!eval "foes_adjacent('mage')"
!passive add mage threat_check on_turn_start "entity[self].threatened = foes_adjacent('mage')"
!turn next
!ent dump mage

Expected: The spatial helpers compose with user-defined functions
and passives. `foes_adjacent(eid)` wraps
`len(entities_within(eid, 1, ..., 'hostile'))` into a reusable
function. The mage at (5,5) has two adjacent hostiles (foe1 at
(5,6), foe2 at (6,5)) and one adjacent ally (bystander), so
`foes_adjacent('mage')` = 2. A passive can call the function and
store the result: after `!turn next` fires the on_turn_start
passive, `mage.threatened` = 2, confirmed by `!ent dump`. This is
the headline composition win — "count of adjacent enemies" is now
a one-liner usable anywhere a formula runs.
SCENARIO 236 — !ent clone: multiple coordinate pairs auto-number copies
------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mclone1 CloneMulti 10 10
!match use mclone1
!ent add gob Goblin 20 1 1 5
!ent set_var gob atk 7
!ent clone gob gobcopy 3 3
!ent clone gob minion 5 5 6 6 7 7
!list
!ent dump minion2
!ent clone gob bad 2 2 3
!ent clone gob onself 5 5

Expected: `!ent clone` now accepts multiple `x y` pairs. A single pair
keeps the original behavior: `!ent clone gob gobcopy 3 3` makes one
copy with id "gobcopy" at (3,3). Multiple pairs make one copy per
cell, auto-numbering the ids from the base: `!ent clone gob minion
5 5 6 6 7 7` creates minion1@(5,5), minion2@(6,6), minion3@(7,7).
Each copy is a full clone (vars included — `!ent dump minion2` shows
atk=7 inherited). All-or-nothing validation: an odd number of
coordinate values ("2 2 3") is rejected as not forming pairs, and a
target cell already occupied (5,5 is taken by minion1) is rejected
before any copy in that batch is made.


SCENARIO 237 — !ent status: add / remove / list / clear
--------------------------------------------------------

!match new mstat1 StatusCmd 6 6
!match use mstat1
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent status hero list
!ent status hero add stunned
!ent status hero add poisoned
!ent status hero list
!ent status hero remove poisoned
!ent status hero list
!ent status hero clear
!ent status hero list

Expected: `!ent status <id> <action> [name]` manages the entity's
statuses. `add` creates a status with no data, `remove` drops it,
`list` shows them all (sorted, "(none)" when empty), `clear` wipes
the lot. After adding stunned + poisoned, list shows
"poisoned (no data), stunned (no data)"; after removing poisoned,
just stunned; after clear, "(none)". Statuses can also carry data —
see SCENARIO 241 for the set/del/info subcommands and SCENARIO 242
for the per-status `skips_turn` field.


SCENARIO 238 — !eval --as binds self for testing passive bodies
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new meval1 EvalAs 6 6
!match use meval1
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero atk 12
!ent set_var hero max_hp 50
!eval "entity[self].atk"
!eval --as hero "entity[self].atk"
!eval --as hero "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 5"
!ent dump hero

Expected: `!eval` normally leaves `self` unbound, so a formula using
`entity[self]` errors ("'self' is unbound in this context") — useful
but inconvenient when prototyping a passive body. The new
`!eval --as <eid> "<formula>"` prefix binds `self` to that entity for
the evaluation. `!eval --as hero "entity[self].atk"` returns 12, and
`!eval --as hero "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 5"` actually
heals hero from 30 to 35 (confirmed by `!ent dump`) — letting a GM
test a passive's effect interactively without attaching it and
advancing a turn.


SCENARIO 239 — !system delete with safety guards
-------------------------------------------------

!system new homebrew
!system new throwaway
!system delete throwaway
!system list
!system delete default
!match new msys1 SysMatch 6 6 --system homebrew
!system delete homebrew
!system delete nonexistent

Expected: `!system delete <name>` removes a GameSystem, with guards
against breaking the manager. Deleting the unused "throwaway" system
succeeds and `!system list` no longer shows it. The guards then
reject: deleting "default" (it's the global default — must reassign
first); deleting "homebrew" while a match is bound to it (the match
must be rebound or deleted first); and deleting a nonexistent system.
Each guard produces a clear error rather than corrupting state. (The
match msys1 is created ON the homebrew system specifically to
exercise the in-use guard.)


SCENARIO 240 — Status skips_turn: per-status, not a gamerule list
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mskip1 SkipTurn 8 8
!match use mskip1
!ent add alice Alice 30 1 1 30
!ent add bob Bob 30 2 2 20
!ent add carol Carol 30 3 3 10
!ent status bob add stunned
!ent status bob set stunned skips_turn true
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next

Expected: "What X does" is stored inside X — there is no
skip-list gamerule any more. A status causes its bearer's turn to
be skipped when the status's data dict carries `skips_turn: True`.
With Bob carrying stunned ({skips_turn: True}) and the order
alice(30), bob(20), carol(10), the first `!turn next` opens on
alice. The second advances past alice — would land on bob, but
bob's stunned.skips_turn is True, so it skips to carol (a
"⏭️ `bob`'s turn skipped (stunned)" line is logged and bob's
on_turn_start does NOT fire). The third wraps to alice. A status
WITHOUT skips_turn (or with skips_turn explicitly False) doesn't
skip — adding "poisoned" to bob wouldn't matter unless poisoned
also had skips_turn:true. SCENARIO 245 covers auto-clear of a
skips_turn status via the status_tick mechanism.
SCENARIO 232 — Dynamic entity[<expr>]: literal still works, expressions resolve
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdyn1 DynAccess 12 12
!match use mdyn1
!ent add hero Hero 30 5 5 10
!ent set_var hero focus gob2
!ent add gob1 Gob1 20 5 6 5
!ent add gob2 Gob2 25 8 8 4
!ent set_var gob2 max_hp 25
!eval "entity[gob1].hp"
!eval "entity[\"gob2\"].hp"
!eval "entity[entity[hero].focus].hp"
!eval "entity[5].hp"

Expected: The `entity[X]` accessor now accepts dynamic indices while
keeping the old literal forms working. `entity[gob1].hp` (bare
identifier) still means the entity with id "gob1" = 20 — backward
compatible, because at top level no identifier is a "known
parameter". A string literal `entity["gob2"].hp` = 25. The new
power: `entity[entity[hero].focus].hp` evaluates the inner read
(hero.focus = "gob2") and uses it as the id, giving gob2's hp = 25.
A non-string index like `entity[5]` errors clearly ("index must be
an entity id string, got int") instead of a confusing downstream
failure.


SCENARIO 233 — Dynamic entity[<param>]: the function-parameter fix
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdyn2 DynParam 12 12
!match use mdyn2
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent add ally Ally 40 2 2 9
!ent set_var ally max_hp 100
!func def target_hp eid "entity[eid].hp"
!func def heal eid,amount "entity[eid].hp = entity[eid].hp + amount"
!eval "target_hp('hero')"
!eval "target_hp('ally')"
!eval "heal('hero', 15)"
!ent dump hero
!eval "heal('ally', 20)"
!ent dump ally

Expected: Inside a function body, a parameter used as an entity index
(`entity[eid]`) now resolves to the parameter's VALUE — the
limitation called out in PR16's scenario 219 is fixed. `target_hp`
reads any passed entity's hp: `target_hp('hero')` = 30,
`target_hp('ally')` = 40. `heal` writes to the passed entity:
`heal('hero', 15)` raises hero to 45 (room under max_hp 100),
`heal('ally', 20)` raises ally to 60. `!ent dump` confirms both.
This makes functions genuinely reusable across entities passed by
id, not just `self`/`this`. (The distinction is unambiguous: bare
identifiers that are NOT parameters stay literal ids, so existing
`entity[goblin]` references are unaffected.)


SCENARIO 234 — Seedable RNG: reproducible roll sequences
---------------------------------------------------------

!system set default random_seed encounter42
!match new mseed1 Seeded1 8 8
!match use mseed1
!eval "random_int(1, 1000)"
!eval "random_int(1, 1000)"
!eval "random_int(1, 1000)"
!match new mseed2 Seeded2 8 8
!match use mseed2
!eval "random_int(1, 1000)"
!eval "random_int(1, 1000)"
!eval "random_int(1, 1000)"
!system set default random_seed

Expected: With the `random_seed` rule set to a non-empty value, the
match's formula RNG becomes deterministic — each match seeded with
the same value produces the SAME sequence of rolls. So the three
rolls in Seeded1 exactly match the three rolls in Seeded2
(same seed "encounter42", same call order). The RNG advances across
calls (the three rolls within a match differ from each other — it's
a reproducible SEQUENCE, not a stuck value). The trailing
`!system set default random_seed` with no value clears the seed
back to unseeded (independent rolls) so later scenarios aren't
affected. (Test note: because the two matches share the same seed
and the same number of prior rolls, their roll lists are equal —
that equality is the deterministic assertion; the exact numbers
depend on the seed.)


SCENARIO 235 — Seedable RNG: random_string and reseeding on change
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!system set default random_seed alpha
!match new mseed3 Seeded3 8 8
!match use mseed3
!eval "random_string('n', 's', 'e', 'w')"
!eval "random_string('n', 's', 'e', 'w')"
!match new mseed4 Seeded4 8 8
!match use mseed4
!eval "random_string('n', 's', 'e', 'w')"
!eval "random_string('n', 's', 'e', 'w')"
!system set default random_seed

Expected: Seeding applies to `random_string` too — Seeded3 and
Seeded4 (same seed "alpha", same call order) draw the same two
direction strings in the same order. This is the basis for
reproducible "random scatter" or "wandering monster" tables a GM
can replay. The trailing empty `random_seed` restores unseeded
behavior. (As in 234, the assertion is that the two matches'
draw sequences are equal; the specific letters depend on the seed.)
SCENARIO 230 — !tile place_random: scatter instances across empty cells
------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mtr1 PlaceRandom 4 4
!match use mtr1
!tile def new flame
!tile def data flame burn 5
!tile place_random flame 5
!tile find flame
!tile place_random flame 3 burn=20
!tile find flame
!tile place_random flame 100
!tile place_random flame 0

Expected: `!tile place_random <template> <count>` scatters `count`
instances across random cells that have no existing tile data
(entity-occupied cells are still eligible — tiles and entities
coexist). On a 4x4 grid (16 cells), placing 5 flames then listing
shows exactly 5 placed cells (the exact coordinates are random, so
this test asserts the COUNT, not positions). A second
`place_random flame 3 burn=20` adds 3 more (now 8 total); the
`burn=20` override applies to those 3. Asking for 100 on a grid
with only 8 empty cells left fails all-or-nothing: "only 8 empty
cell(s) available; cannot place 100" — nothing is placed. A count
of 0 (or negative) is rejected. Because placement is random, the
deterministic assertions are: count after first call = 5, count
after second = 8, the over-count and zero-count calls both error
and leave the total unchanged.


SCENARIO 231 — !tile fill_pattern: paint an ASCII stencil
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new mtr2 FillPattern 8 8
!match use mtr2
!tile def new wall
!tile def data wall glyph #
!tile def new water
!tile def data water glyph ~
!tile fill_pattern 2 2 "#=wall,~=water" "##~" "#.~" "~~~"
!tile find wall
!tile find water
!tile info 3 3
!tile fill_pattern 7 7 "#=wall" "###" "###"
!tile fill_pattern 1 1 "#=nope" "#"
!tile fill_pattern 1 1 "##=wall" "#"

Expected: `!tile fill_pattern <x> <y> <legend> <rows...>` paints a
multi-row stencil with its top-left at (x, y). The legend maps
single characters to templates; each row places one template per
character at (x + column, y + row). Characters not in the legend
are skipped (left untouched) — '.' is the conventional hole.

The 3x3 stencil at (2,2):
  row "##~" → (2,2) wall, (3,2) wall, (4,2) water
  row "#.~" → (2,3) wall, (3,3) SKIP,  (4,3) water
  row "~~~" → (2,4) water,(3,4) water, (4,4) water
So `!tile find wall` shows 3 cells, `!tile find water` shows 5,
and `!tile info 3 3` reports "no data" (the '.' left it empty).

The remaining calls demonstrate all-or-nothing validation: a
stencil at (7,7) that would spill off the 8x8 grid fails with an
out-of-bounds cell error (placing nothing); a legend referencing
an undefined template (`nope`) fails up front; a multi-character
legend key (`##`) is rejected.


SCENARIO 241 — Status data: !ent status set / del / info
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst1 StatusData 6 6
!match use mst1
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent status hero add stunned
!ent status hero set stunned skips_turn true
!ent status hero set stunned remaining 3
!ent status hero set stunned source.spell "thunder_shock"
!ent status hero info stunned
!ent status hero list
!ent status hero del stunned source.spell
!ent status hero info stunned
!ent status hero del stunned remaining
!ent status hero info stunned

Expected: Statuses carry their own data dicts (the "what X does is
stored in X" rule). `!ent status hero set stunned skips_turn true`
stores the literal bool True (case-sensitive: "true" / "false" are
coerced; "yes" / "no" stay strings). Numeric values like
`remaining 3` parse as int. Dotted paths like `source.spell
"thunder_shock"` create intermediate dicts. `info` prints the full
data as JSON. `list` shows each status's fields inline. `del` with
a dotted path removes one field and prunes the now-empty parent
dict (so after `del stunned source.spell`, the `source` subdict is
gone, not left as `{}`). Removing the LAST field leaves the status
with no data — `info` reports "(no data)" — but the status itself
persists until `!ent status hero remove stunned`.


SCENARIO 242 — Status data: !ent status remove vs. clear
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst2 StatusRC 6 6
!match use mst2
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent status hero add stunned
!ent status hero set stunned remaining 2
!ent status hero add poisoned
!ent status hero set poisoned damage 5
!ent status hero list
!ent status hero remove stunned
!ent status hero list
!ent status hero clear
!ent status hero list

Expected: `remove <name>` drops one status entirely (data and all);
`clear` wipes every status. After remove-stunned, only poisoned
remains (with its damage field intact). After clear, the list is
"(none)". Removing a status that doesn't exist reports a friendly
"`hero` has no status `<name>`" line rather than erroring — the
remove is idempotent. (Removing a status field, vs. removing the
whole status, is the del vs. remove distinction shown in 241/242.)


SCENARIO 243 — status_* formula functions: read, write, branch
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst3 StatusFn 6 6
!match use mst3
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent status hero add stunned
!ent status hero set stunned remaining 5
!eval --as hero "status_has(self, 'stunned')"
!eval --as hero "status_has(self, 'absent')"
!eval --as hero "status_has_path(self, 'stunned', 'remaining')"
!eval --as hero "status_has_path(self, 'stunned', 'nope')"
!eval --as hero "status_get(self, 'stunned', 'remaining')"
!eval --as hero "status_set(self, 'stunned', 'remaining', 99)"
!eval --as hero "status_get(self, 'stunned', 'remaining')"
!eval --as hero "status_del(self, 'stunned', 'remaining')"
!eval --as hero "status_has_path(self, 'stunned', 'remaining')"
!eval --as hero "status_add(self, 'poisoned')"
!eval --as hero "status_add(self, 'poisoned')"
!eval --as hero "status_remove(self, 'poisoned')"
!eval --as hero "status_remove(self, 'poisoned')"

Expected: The status_* formula functions parallel tile_*:
`status_has(eid, name)` → bool (status present);
`status_has_path(eid, name, "path")` → bool (status present AND
path resolves); `status_get` raises on missing path; `status_set`
writes (creating intermediates); `status_del` returns True iff the
path existed; `status_add` returns True only on a fresh insert
(False if already present); `status_remove` returns True only on
an actual removal (False if absent). Bare `self` (allowed via the
new entity-token identifier set) evaluates to the !eval --as
binding. So the calls thread through:
- has stunned → True; absent → False
- has_path remaining → True; nope → False
- get remaining → 5
- set remaining 99 → returns 99
- get remaining → 99
- del remaining → True
- has_path remaining → False
- add poisoned → True (newly added); second call → False (already)
- remove poisoned → True; second call → False (already gone)


SCENARIO 244 — Status auto-tick (round_end): "remaining" decay
---------------------------------------------------------------

!system set default status_tick_when round_end
!system set default status_tick_formula "if status_has_path(self, status_name, 'remaining'):\n    status_set(self, status_name, 'remaining', status_get(self, status_name, 'remaining') - 1)\n    if status_get(self, status_name, 'remaining') <= 0:\n        status_remove(self, status_name)"
!match new mst4 StatusTick 6 6
!match use mst4
!ent add alice Alice 30 1 1 30
!ent add bob Bob 30 2 2 20
!ent status alice add bleeding
!ent status alice set bleeding remaining 2
!ent status bob add poisoned
!ent status bob set poisoned remaining 3
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!ent status alice list
!ent status bob list
!turn next
!turn next
!ent status alice list
!ent status bob list
!turn next
!turn next
!ent status alice list
!ent status bob list
!system set default status_tick_when never
!system set default status_tick_formula ""

Expected: With `status_tick_when=round_end` and the canonical
decay formula, EACH (entity, status) ticks once per round wrap.
The formula is GM-defined — there is no hardcoded "remaining"
field; the formula chooses what to decrement and when to remove.

Initial: alice has bleeding(remaining=2), bob has
poisoned(remaining=3). Each round_end fires the tick once per
(entity, status). With turn_order [alice, bob], a round wrap
happens once every 2 `!turn next` calls (after the initial
opener). So:

  After 1st `!turn next`: opens R1 (no round_end yet).
  After 2nd: alice→bob, no wrap. State unchanged.
  After 3rd: bob→alice WRAP — tick #1 fires:
    bleeding 2→1, poisoned 3→2.
  After 4th-5th: another wrap — tick #2 fires:
    bleeding 1→0 → AUTO-REMOVE, poisoned 2→1.
  After 6th-7th: another wrap — tick #3 fires:
    poisoned 1→0 → AUTO-REMOVE.

Final state: both statuses gone. The two trailing `!system set`
calls restore `never`/`""` so later scenarios run without ticks.


SCENARIO 245 — Status auto-tick on a skips_turn status
-------------------------------------------------------

!system set default status_tick_when round_end
!system set default status_tick_formula "if status_has_path(self, status_name, 'remaining'):\n    status_set(self, status_name, 'remaining', status_get(self, status_name, 'remaining') - 1)\n    if status_get(self, status_name, 'remaining') <= 0:\n        status_remove(self, status_name)"
!match new mst5 StatusSkipDecay 6 6
!match use mst5
!ent add alice Alice 30 1 1 30
!ent add bob Bob 30 2 2 20
!ent status bob add stunned
!ent status bob set stunned skips_turn true
!ent status bob set stunned remaining 2
!turn next
!ent status bob list
!turn next
!ent status bob list
!turn next
!ent status bob list
!system set default status_tick_when never
!system set default status_tick_formula ""

Expected: skips_turn and the tick decay work together. Bob has
stunned({skips_turn:true, remaining:2}). On each round wrap the
tick decrements remaining. When remaining hits 0 the status
auto-removes — and bob stops being skipped.

Trace:
  R1 opens on alice. Bob is stunned, so when his turn comes he
  is skipped (no on_turn_start).
  Wrap to R2: tick fires. bob.stunned.remaining 2→1.
  R2 bob.status: stunned(r=1, skips_turn=true). Still skipped.
  Wrap to R3: tick fires. remaining 1→0 → auto-remove.
  R3 bob.status: (none). Now bob acts normally; his on_turn_start
  fires.

This is the headline modularity win: "stunned skips turns AND
lasts N rounds" is fully described by the status's own data,
not by external rules.


SCENARIO 246 — Formula for-loop over entities_within: AOE damage
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mfor1 ForLoop 10 10
!match use mfor1
!ent add wizard Wizard 30 5 5 10
!ent set_var wizard team blue
!ent add gob1 Gob1 20 5 6 5
!ent set_var gob1 team red
!ent set_var gob1 max_hp 100
!ent add gob2 Gob2 25 6 5 4
!ent set_var gob2 team red
!ent set_var gob2 max_hp 100
!ent add gob3 Gob3 30 4 5 3
!ent set_var gob3 team red
!ent set_var gob3 max_hp 100
!ent add ally Ally 40 5 4 9
!ent set_var ally team blue
!ent set_var ally max_hp 100
!eval --as wizard "for eid in entities_within(self, 2, 'square_radius_distance', 'hostile'): entity[eid].hp = entity[eid].hp - 7"
!ent dump gob1
!ent dump gob2
!ent dump gob3
!ent dump ally

Expected: The for-loop over `entities_within(...)` makes "damage
every adjacent enemy" a one-liner. The wizard at (5,5) sees three
hostiles (gob1@(5,6), gob2@(6,5), gob3@(4,5)) within distance 2
plus an ally at (5,4). The relation filter "hostile" keeps only
the three goblins. The loop body applies -7 hp to each. After:
gob1.hp = 13, gob2.hp = 18, gob3.hp = 23, ally.hp UNCHANGED at
40. The dynamic-accessor (PR 20) makes `entity[eid]` resolve at
runtime to each loop iteration's id; combined with the relation
filter that's the whole "single-target spell becomes AOE" recipe.


SCENARIO 247 — for-loop iterable validation + loop bound
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new mfor2 ForLimits 10 10
!match use mfor2
!ent add hero Hero 30 5 5 10
!eval "for x in range(5): entity[x].hp = 0"
!eval "for x in my_list: entity[x].hp = 0"
!eval "for [a, b] in cells_in_burst(5, 5, 1): tile_set(a, b, 'foo', 1)"
!tile def new mark
!system set default formula_loop_limit 5
!eval "for (cx, cy) in cells_in_burst(5, 5, 3): tile_set(cx, cy, 'foo', 1)"
!system set default formula_loop_limit 10000

Expected: For-loops are validated up front. The iterable MUST be
a direct call to one of: entities_within, group_members,
cells_in_burst, cells_in_line, cells_in_cone. So `range(5)`
errors with "iterable must be a direct call to one of {...}" and
`my_list` errors as an unknown identifier. A loop target that's
neither a single name nor a tuple of names ("for [a, b] in ..."
uses a List, not Tuple) is also rejected.

The formula_loop_limit rule caps TOTAL iterations across all
loops in one evaluation. With it set to 5, looping a 7x7=49-cell
square-radius burst would tick 49 times — the runtime raises
"formula for-loop iteration limit (5) exceeded" once the 6th
iteration runs. The default 10000 is restored at the end so
later scenarios run with the normal cap.


SCENARIO 248 — group_members and tuple-unpack for-loop
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new mfor3 GroupAndCoords 10 10
!match use mfor3
!ent add a A 30 1 1 10
!ent add b B 30 2 2 9
!ent add c C 30 3 3 8
!ent group new party
!ent group add party a b c
!eval "for eid in group_members('party'): entity[eid].hp = entity[eid].hp - 1"
!ent dump a
!ent dump b
!ent dump c
!tile def new mark
!tile def data mark glyph X
!eval "for (cx, cy) in cells_in_line(2, 2, 5, 2): tile_set(cx, cy, 'marked', 1)"
!eval "for (cx, cy) in cells_in_burst(7, 7, 1, 'manhattan_distance'): tile_set(cx, cy, 'flame', 1)"

Expected: `group_members(name)` returns the member list in
insertion order and is loopable. The loop applies -1 hp to every
party member: a/b/c all drop from 30 to 29. The tuple-unpack form
`for (cx, cy) in cells_in_*` works on coord-list returns: a line
from (2,2) to (5,2) marks four cells; a manhattan-burst of radius
1 at (7,7) marks the diamond {(6,7),(7,6),(7,7),(7,8),(8,7)}.
The transformer treats cx/cy as dynamic identifiers inside the
body (PR 20's accessor logic), so they pass straight through as
runtime values to tile_set.


SCENARIO 249 — status_names: iterate a status set without hardcoding
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mintro1 StatusNames 6 6
!match use mintro1
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent status hero add stunned
!ent status hero set stunned remaining 2
!ent status hero add poisoned
!ent status hero set poisoned damage 5
!ent status hero add blessed
!eval --as hero "status_names(self)"
!eval --as hero "len(status_names(self))"
!eval --as hero "for s in status_names(self): status_set(self, s, 'audited', 1)"
!ent status hero info stunned
!ent status hero info poisoned
!ent status hero info blessed

Expected: `status_names(eid)` returns the active status names in
insertion order. Hero starts with [stunned, poisoned, blessed].
`len(status_names(self))` = 3. The for-loop iterates whatever
statuses exist (no hardcoded names) and stamps each with an
`audited: 1` field — `info` on every status now shows that field
alongside its existing data. This is the headline composition win:
"do X to every status the entity has" is now a one-liner without
naming any specific status.


SCENARIO 250 — var_keys + the runtime-path var_* accessors
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mintro2 VarIntrospect 6 6
!match use mintro2
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero team blue
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.potion.heal 12
!eval --as hero "var_keys(self)"
!eval --as hero "var_keys(self, 'inventory')"
!eval --as hero "var_has(self, 'inventory.sword.damage')"
!eval --as hero "var_has(self, 'inventory.spear.damage')"
!eval --as hero "var_get(self, 'inventory.sword.damage')"
!eval --as hero "var_set(self, 'inventory.sword.damage', 99)"
!eval --as hero "var_get(self, 'inventory.sword.damage')"
!eval --as hero "var_del(self, 'inventory.bow.damage')"
!eval --as hero "var_has(self, 'inventory.bow.damage')"
!eval --as hero "var_del(self, 'inventory.bow.damage')"
!eval --as hero "for item in var_keys(self, 'inventory'): var_set(self, 'audit.' + item, 1)"
!ent dump hero

Expected: `var_keys(eid, path)` lists keys at a vars path
(empty/omitted path = top level). `entity[X].path` requires a
STATIC path at parse time; the runtime-path companions
`var_get/var_has/var_set/var_del` accept a string path computed
at runtime — which is what makes `var_keys` useful (you can
iterate whatever exists and touch it without naming names).

Top-level keys for hero: hp, max_hp, initiative, team, inventory.
Inventory keys: sword, bow, potion. `var_has` returns True/False
without raising; `var_get` raises on a missing path (same as
entity[X].path reads). `var_set` writes (routing through
write_var so var hooks still fire); `var_del` returns True iff
the path existed (False second time — idempotent).

The trailing for-loop demonstrates iteration over `var_keys`: it
stamps every inventory item's name as an `audit.<item> = 1` flag
on the entity. After the loop, the dump shows the new audit
subtree alongside the existing inventory.


SCENARIO 251 — tile_keys + entity_groups + rule_get
----------------------------------------------------

!match new mintro3 MiscIntro 8 8
!match use mintro3
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent add ally Ally 30 3 3 9
!ent add mage Mage 30 4 4 8
!ent group new heroes
!ent group add heroes hero ally
!ent group new mages
!ent group add mages mage hero
!tile def new flame
!tile def data flame burn 5
!tile def data flame glyph F
!tile place flame 5 5
!eval "tile_keys(5, 5)"
!eval "tile_keys(7, 7)"
!eval --as hero "entity_groups(self)"
!eval "entity_groups('mage')"
!eval "entity_groups('ally')"
!eval "rule_get('turnorder_direction')"
!eval "rule_get('friendlyfire')"
!eval "rule_get('nonexistent_rule')"

Expected: `tile_keys(x, y)` lists the top-level keys in a tile's
data dict. The placed flame instance shows the placement keys
(burn, glyph, _template). An empty tile (7,7) returns [].

`entity_groups(eid)` is the reverse index of `group_members`: it
lists every group containing the entity. hero is in both `heroes`
and `mages`; mage is in only `mages`; ally is in only `heroes`.
Insertion order over Match.groups so results are stable.

`rule_get(name)` returns the rule's current value or None for
unknown rules. Defaults are returned when the rule hasn't been
set — turnorder_direction = 'highest_first', friendlyfire = False.


SCENARIO 252 — Match-wide entity queries: all_entities / with_status / with_var / in_area
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mintro4 AllQueries 12 12
!match use mintro4
!ent add a A 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var a team blue
!ent set_var a inventory.sword 1
!ent add b B 30 2 2 9
!ent set_var b team red
!ent set_var b inventory.bow 1
!ent add c C 30 5 5 8
!ent set_var c team red
!ent add d D 30 10 10 7
!ent set_var d team blue
!ent set_var d inventory.staff 1
!ent status b add poisoned
!ent status c add poisoned
!ent status c add stunned
!eval "all_entities()"
!eval "entities_with_status('poisoned')"
!eval "entities_with_status('stunned')"
!eval "entities_with_status('absent')"
!eval "entities_with_var('inventory')"
!eval "entities_with_var('inventory.sword')"
!eval "entities_in_area(5, 5, 2)"
!eval "entities_in_area(5, 5, 2, 'manhattan_distance')"
!eval "for eid in entities_with_status('poisoned'): var_set(eid, 'hp', var_get(eid, 'hp') - 3)"
!ent dump b
!ent dump c

Expected: The match-wide query family doesn't need a reference
entity — handy when the "originator" of an effect is a tile or a
GM command, not another entity.

`all_entities()` returns every alive entity id in insertion order:
[a, b, c, d]. `entities_with_status(name)` filters to those
carrying the named status: poisoned → [b, c]; stunned → [c];
absent → []. `entities_with_var(path)` does the same for var
paths: 'inventory' → [a, b, d]; 'inventory.sword' → [a] only.

`entities_in_area(x, y, n, mode)` is the coord-rooted twin of
`entities_within`. Centered on (5,5) with r=2 Chebyshev: c
(distance 0), all others farther — [c]. Switching to manhattan
keeps the same result here (c at distance 0). Use this when an
AOE is rooted at a tile/explosion point, not an entity.

The trailing for-loop is the headline composition pattern: damage
every poisoned entity by 3 in one line, via `var_set` /
`var_get` (the runtime-path var accessors needed because `eid`
is a loop variable). After: b.hp = 27, c.hp = 27, others
unchanged.


SCENARIO 253 — eval reports affected entities for side-effect formulas
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mintro5 AffectedOut 12 12
!match use mintro5
!ent add wizard Wizard 30 5 5 10
!ent set_var wizard team blue
!ent set_var wizard max_hp 100
!ent add gob1 Gob1 20 5 6 5
!ent set_var gob1 team red
!ent set_var gob1 max_hp 100
!ent add gob2 Gob2 25 6 5 4
!ent set_var gob2 team red
!ent set_var gob2 max_hp 100
!ent add gob3 Gob3 30 4 5 3
!ent set_var gob3 team red
!ent set_var gob3 max_hp 100
!eval --as wizard "for eid in entities_within(self, 2, 'square_radius_distance', 'hostile'): entity[eid].hp = entity[eid].hp - 7"
!eval --as wizard "entity[gob1].hp = entity[gob1].hp - 1"
!eval --as wizard "status_add(self, 'casting')"
!eval "entity[wizard].hp"
!eval "entity[wizard].max_hp + 0"

Expected: A formula that mutates entity vars or status now
reports "Affected N entit(y|ies): a, b, c" instead of the
confusing "= None" that a trailing assignment naturally produces.

The first eval (the user's exact reported case) damages three
hostiles in a loop; the trailing assignment makes the return
value None, but the engine tracked the three writes and the
command-layer summary reports "Affected 3 entities: `gob1`,
`gob2`, `gob3`". A single-target side-effect eval reports
"Affected 1 entity: `gob1`" (singular form).

When the formula DOES return a value, that value wins — the
"Affected" report only fires when the result is None AND at
least one entity was mutated. So `status_add(self, 'casting')`
prints `= \`True\`` (the bool the call returned), even though
status_add affected an entity under the hood. `entity[wizard].hp`
prints `= \`30\`` and `max_hp + 0` prints its arithmetic result
the same way they always have. Use a trailing expression in a
formula to get its value; omit one to get the affected-entities
summary.


SCENARIO 254 — Composition: data-driven debuff purge
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new mintro6 Purge 6 6
!match use mintro6
!ent add cleric Cleric 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var cleric team blue
!ent add ally1 Ally1 30 2 2 9
!ent set_var ally1 team blue
!ent status ally1 add poisoned
!ent status ally1 add bleeding
!ent status ally1 add blessed
!ent set_var ally1 'status_meta.poisoned.bad' 1
!ent set_var ally1 'status_meta.bleeding.bad' 1
!ent add ally2 Ally2 30 3 3 8
!ent set_var ally2 team blue
!ent status ally2 add poisoned
!ent set_var ally2 'status_meta.poisoned.bad' 1
!eval --as cleric "for tgt in entities_within(self, 5, 'square_radius_distance', 'ally'):\n    for s in status_names(tgt):\n        if var_has(tgt, 'status_meta.' + s + '.bad'):\n            status_remove(tgt, s)"
!ent status ally1 list
!ent status ally2 list

Expected: A "mass debuff purge" passive becomes ~one nested loop
when both iteration primitives exist. The cleric iterates every
ally in range; for each, she iterates that ally's active
statuses; for each, she checks whether the status is flagged as
"bad" via a convention var (`status_meta.<name>.bad = 1`) and
removes it if so.

This is the design philosophy in action: the engine doesn't know
what "bad" means — the GM defines the convention by setting
`status_meta.<name>.bad`. ally1 had poisoned + bleeding + blessed;
the bleeding and poisoned were flagged bad → removed; blessed
was not flagged → kept. ally2 had only poisoned (flagged bad)
→ removed. Final ally1: blessed only. ally2: (none).

(The formula uses the multi-line `\n` form because Python doesn't
allow `for x in a: for y in b: ...` on a single physical line —
the SCENARIO file's `\n` escape is interpreted by the harness
the same way Discord/CLI receive real newlines.)


SCENARIO 255 — on_entity_moved fires once per tp / move
--------------------------------------------------------

!match new mev1 EntityMoved 10 10
!match use mev1
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero move_count 0
!ent set_var hero last_from 0
!ent set_var hero last_to 0
!passive add hero mover on_entity_moved "entity[self].move_count = entity[self].move_count + 1\nentity[self].last_from = from_x\nentity[self].last_to = to_x"
!ent tp hero 5 5
!ent dump hero
!ent move hero 2 right
!ent dump hero
!ent tp hero 5 5

Expected: `on_entity_moved` fires once per position-changing command,
with `from_x`/`from_y`/`to_x`/`to_y` bound to the move's endpoints.
The hook is the entity-side complement to tile on_enter/on_exit —
a passive can react to "any move" without caring which tiles are
involved.

After `!ent tp hero 5 5` (from (3,3)): move_count = 1, last_from = 3,
last_to = 5. After `!ent move hero 2 right` (from (5,5) to (7,5)):
move_count = 2, last_from = 5, last_to = 7. The final
`!ent tp hero 5 5` from (7,5) IS a real move, so count = 3.

For a stepwise move the hook fires ONCE at the end with from/to as
the endpoints (per-step observation is via tile on_enter/on_exit).
For group moves it fires once per moving member. The TP-to-current-
cell case is a no-op (no actual move) and does NOT fire.


SCENARIO 256 — Status lifecycle events: added / removed / changed
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mev2 StatusEvents 8 8
!match use mev2
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero status_log ""
!passive add hero saw_added on_status_added "entity[self].status_log = entity[self].status_log + '+' + status_name"
!passive add hero saw_removed on_status_removed "entity[self].status_log = entity[self].status_log + '-' + status_name"
!passive add hero saw_changed on_status_changed "entity[self].status_log = entity[self].status_log + '~' + status_name"
!ent status hero add poisoned
!ent status hero set poisoned damage 5
!ent status hero set poisoned damage 5
!ent status hero set poisoned damage 7
!ent status hero remove poisoned
!ent dump hero

Expected: Three new hook event types complete the status surface:
on_status_added (fired when a status appears), on_status_removed
(when it goes away), on_status_changed (when a field inside an
already-present status changes). All three bind `status_name`,
plus old_value/new_value with the whole pre/post status data dict.

The trace: add poisoned → "+poisoned"; set damage=5 first time
(status data goes from {} to {damage:5}) → "~poisoned"; set
damage=5 AGAIN with the same value → NO FIRE (the diff helper
compares before vs after and only fires when they differ); set
damage=7 → "~poisoned"; remove → "-poisoned". Final
status_log = "+poisoned~poisoned~poisoned-poisoned" (4 markers
for the 4 actual transitions, not 5).

Same diff-comparison logic applies whether the mutation came from
the !ent status command or from the status_* formula functions —
both paths route through Match._emit_status_diff to keep the
firing semantics consistent.


SCENARIO 257 — Tile time hooks fire at round/turn lifecycle
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mev3 TileTimeHooks 6 6
!match use mev3
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero beacon_count 0
!tile def new beacon
!tile def data beacon glyph B
!tile def hook beacon on_round_end "entity[this].beacon_count = entity[this].beacon_count + 1"
!tile place beacon 5 5
!ent dump hero
!turn next
!ent dump hero
!turn next
!ent dump hero
!turn next
!ent dump hero

Expected: Tile hooks now include time hooks (on_round_start /
on_round_end / on_turn_start / on_turn_end) in addition to the
movement hooks (on_enter / on_exit / on_stop). Time hooks fire on
the tile itself at the round/turn lifecycle moment, without
requiring an entity transit. Each registered tile fires once per
matching tick — useful for "beacon pulses every round end",
"trap rearms at turn start", terrain-driven effects in general.

The first `!turn next` opens round 1; no round_end yet, so
beacon_count = 0. With only hero in turn_order, every subsequent
`!turn next` immediately wraps the round, firing on_round_end on
every relevant tile (just (5,5) here). After 2nd turn next:
beacon_count = 1. After 3rd: 2.

`self` inside a time hook resolves to the current-turn entity at
the moment of fire (hero here); for round_* hooks during a wrap
when active_index sits at 0, that's whoever is at index 0 of the
new order.


SCENARIO 258 — !tile test fires a tile hook manually
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new mev4 TileTest 6 6
!match use mev4
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero touched 0
!tile def new spike
!tile def hook spike on_enter "entity[self].touched = entity[self].touched + 1"
!tile place spike 4 4
!tile test 4 4 on_enter --as hero
!tile test 4 4 on_enter --as hero
!ent dump hero
!tile test 4 4 on_exit --as hero
!tile test 9 9 on_enter --as hero
!tile test 4 4 not_a_hook
!tile test 4 4 on_enter

Expected: `!tile test <x> <y> <hook_name> [--as <eid>]` fires the
named tile hook immediately, without requiring an entity to walk
onto the cell. Pure debugging UX — you can verify a hook formula
works in isolation, fire it for testing without spawning a phantom
entity, or use it as the "trigger this trap manually" admin
command.

Two `!tile test 4 4 on_enter --as hero` fires bump `touched` to 2.
A test for a hook that's not registered (`on_exit` on a tile with
only on_enter) reports "no hook to fire" and doesn't error. Off-
grid coords error before firing. An unknown hook name errors with
the allowed list. Omitting --as leaves self unbound — fine for
hooks that don't reference it; a hook that DOES reference self
would surface the standard "'self' is unbound" error.


SCENARIO 259 — fire_tile_hook from formulas (chained tile effects)
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mev5 ChainedTiles 8 8
!match use mev5
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero burned 0
!tile def new flame
!tile def hook flame on_enter "entity[self].burned = entity[self].burned + 1"
!tile place flame 3 3
!tile place flame 4 3
!tile place flame 5 3
!eval --as hero "fire_tile_hook(3, 3, 'on_enter')"
!eval --as hero "for (cx, cy) in cells_in_line(3, 3, 5, 3): fire_tile_hook(cx, cy, 'on_enter')"
!ent dump hero
!eval --as hero "fire_tile_hook(9, 9, 'on_enter')"
!eval --as hero "fire_tile_hook(3, 3, 'not_a_hook')"

Expected: `fire_tile_hook(x, y, hook_name, eid=None)` triggers a
tile hook from a formula. Returns the number of log lines emitted
(>0 means the hook ran, 0 means no hook of that name on this
tile). Defaults `self` to the caller's ctx.target; pass an
explicit eid as the fourth arg to override.

The first call fires flame on (3,3) once → burned = 1. The
for-loop over cells_in_line iterates (3,3)→(5,3) and fires
each of the three flames → burned += 3 → burned = 4. Off-grid
(9,9) returns 0 (no tile data, no hook to fire). An unknown
hook name errors with the allowed-list message.

This is the "chained effects" primitive: a tile's own on_enter
hook could call `fire_tile_hook(cx, cy, 'on_enter')` on
neighbors to spread fire, propagate damage, etc. — without the
GM scripting the propagation manually.


SCENARIO 260 — move_entity / move_step from formulas
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new mev6 FormulaMove 8 8
!match use mev6
!ent add a A 30 3 3 10
!ent add b B 30 7 5 9
!ent add c C 30 2 2 8
!ent set_var a moves 0
!passive add a count_moves on_entity_moved "entity[self].moves = entity[self].moves + 1"
!eval "move_entity('a', 5, 5)"
!ent dump a
!eval "move_step('a', 'right')"
!ent dump a
!eval "move_step('a', 'right')"
!ent dump a
!ent tp a 8 5
!eval "move_step('a', 'right')"
!ent dump a
!ent tp a 6 5
!eval "move_step('a', 'right')"

Expected: `move_entity(eid, x, y)` teleports the entity with full
tp() semantics (bounds + occupancy validated, tile hooks +
on_entity_moved fire). Returns (x, y) on success; raises
FormulaError on validation failure.

`move_step(eid, direction)` is the single-cell-toward-a-direction
companion. Returns True if the step succeeded, False if blocked
(off-grid or destination occupied) — so formulas can branch on
the result without try-equivalent patterns.

Trace: move_entity to (5,5) succeeds → a at (5,5), moves = 1
(on_entity_moved fired). move_step right → a at (6,5), moves = 2.
move_step right → would land on (7,5) but b is there → False,
a still at (6,5), moves still 2. After tp a 8 5 (the grid edge),
move_step right → False (off-grid), a unchanged. After tp a 6 5,
move_step right → True, lands on (7,5) — wait, b is there. So
False. The point: move_step honors the same bounds/occupancy
rules !ent move does, and is observationally identical (tile
hooks fire, on_entity_moved fires) when the step succeeds.


SCENARIO 261 — Composition: status event triggers cleanup passive
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mev7 EventComposition 6 6
!match use mev7
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!ent set_var hero max_hp 100
!ent set_var hero blessing_count 0
!passive add hero bless_log on_status_added "if status_name == 'blessed':\n    entity[self].blessing_count = entity[self].blessing_count + 1"
!passive add hero curse_purge on_status_added "if status_name == 'cursed':\n    status_remove(self, 'cursed')\n    entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 5"
!ent status hero add blessed
!ent dump hero
!ent status hero add cursed
!ent dump hero
!ent status hero add blessed
!ent dump hero

Expected: Status events compose with the formula side-effect
toolkit. A "blessing counter" passive watches on_status_added
and bumps a var when a status named "blessed" appears. A
"curse purge" passive intercepts the same event for "cursed"
and immediately removes it while applying a cost (-5 hp).

Trace:
  add blessed   → bless_log fires → blessing_count = 1.
                  curse_purge fires too but `status_name !=
                  cursed`, so the if-branch doesn't run; blessed
                  remains.
  add cursed    → curse_purge fires → status_remove(self, 'cursed')
                  → hp drops to 25 → cursed is gone immediately.
                  This produces an on_status_removed event for
                  cursed — observable by a separate passive if
                  registered (none here).
  add blessed   → bless_log fires → blessing_count = 2.

The hp clamp respects the default `hp <= max_hp` rule (set max_hp
= 100 up front so the -5 lands cleanly). The "added a status →
immediately remove it" pattern is the foundation for things like
"this entity is immune to debuffs", "fire-resistant entity
removes burning on apply", etc. — all GM-built via this PR's
event hooks.


SCENARIO 262 — !alias define / list / info / use / overwrite / delete
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ma1 AliasBasics 6 6
!match use ma1
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 10
!alias list
!alias def dmg "ent hp this"
!alias def heal "ent hp this"
!alias list
!alias info dmg
!dmg -5
!ent dump hero
!heal 7
!ent dump hero
!alias def dmg "ent set_var this"
!alias info dmg
!dmg poked yes
!ent dump hero
!alias del dmg
!alias list
!dmg -1

Expected:
`!alias list` initially reports "No aliases defined.". After
`!alias def dmg "ent hp this"` and `!alias def heal "ent hp this"`,
list shows both with their expansions. `!alias info dmg` shows
`!dmg` -> `!ent hp this`. `!dmg -5` expands to `!ent hp this -5`,
damaging hero to 25; `!heal 7` heals back to 32 (capped at 30
unless max_hp differs — depending on default clamp behaviour the
final HP may be 30). Redefining `dmg` to `ent set_var this` shows
the before/after in the response, then `!dmg poked yes` sets the
hero's `poked` var to "yes". After `!alias del dmg`, list shows
only `heal`, and `!dmg -1` falls through to the unknown-command
path with a did-you-mean hint pointing at `heal` (or similar).


SCENARIO 263 — !alias rejects unknown target and empty expansion
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ma2 AliasReject 6 6
!match use ma2
!ent add a A 30 2 2 10
!alias def foo nosuchcommand
!alias def bar ""
!alias def "spaced name" "ent hp this"
!alias list

Expected: Each `!alias def` rejects with a specific error.
`foo` -> "alias expansion must start with a real command;
`nosuchcommand` is not a registered command." `bar` -> "alias
expansion cannot be empty." `"spaced name"` -> "invalid alias
name `spaced name`: names must be a single whitespace-free token."
List ends empty.


SCENARIO 264 — !batch groups commands under a single undo
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new mb1 BatchUndo 6 6
!match use mb1
!ent add a A 30 2 2 10
!ent add b B 30 4 4 9
!batch ent hp a -5 ; ent hp b -7 ; ent set_var a marked true
!ent dump a
!ent dump b
!history list commands
!history undo command 1 confirm
!ent dump a
!ent dump b

Expected: After `!batch`, A has hp 25 and `marked=true`; B has
hp 23. The batch produces ONE command snapshot (label starts with
`!batch ent hp a ...`) — `!history list commands` shows a single
entry from this batch. After `!history undo command 1 confirm`,
both entities revert: A back to hp 30 (no `marked` var), B back
to hp 30 — proving the snapshot was taken BEFORE any subcommand
ran.


SCENARIO 265 — !history diff between two command snapshots
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new mhd1 HistoryDiff 6 6
!match use mhd1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent add foe Foe 30 4 4 9
!history save start
!ent hp hero -10
!ent set_var hero blessed true
!ent add ally Ally 30 1 1 8
!ent remove foe
!history save end
!history diff manual:start manual:end

Expected: The diff names the two selectors and lists:
entities added (ally), entities removed (foe), and entity changes
for hero — vars.hp moved 30 -> 20 and vars.blessed was added
(+ true). Round/active_index unchanged so those lines do not
appear. Direction is `start -> end`; swapping the args would
flip adds/removes.


SCENARIO 266 — !find predicate AND queries (vars, status, group)
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mf1 FindQueries 6 6
!match use mf1
!ent add a A 30 1 1 10
!ent add b B 15 2 2 9
!ent add c C 8 3 3 8
!ent set_var a team red
!ent set_var b team red
!ent set_var c team blue
!ent status b add bleeding
!ent status c add bleeding
!ent group new wounded
!ent group add wounded b
!ent group add wounded c
!find team=red
!find team=red hp<20
!find status:bleeding group:wounded
!find hp>=10 team!=blue
!find nosuchvar=1

Expected:
- `team=red`        -> a, b
- `team=red hp<20`  -> b only (a has hp 30)
- `status:bleeding group:wounded` -> b, c
- `hp>=10 team!=blue` -> a, b (c is hp 8, excluded; also team=blue
  would have excluded it)
- `nosuchvar=1`     -> "No entities match." (missing vars never
  satisfy any operator, even `!=`)

SCENARIO 268 — Did-you-mean hints (unknown command, rule, identifier)
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdym1 DidYouMean 6 6
!match use mdym1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!enitty
!system set DidYouMean teem_var team
!eval "entitty"
!eval "minn(1,2)"

Expected: `!enitty` triggers the unknown-command suggester with
a did-you-mean pointing at `ent`. `!system set ... teem_var ...`
fails with "Unknown setting 'teem_var'. Did you mean: 'team_var'?".
`!eval "entitty"` fails with "Unknown identifier 'entitty'. Did
you mean: ..." (close-matches drawn from allowed funcs, hook
context names, entity tokens, and user-defined function names —
e.g. 'move_entity', 'entity_groups'). `!eval "minn(1,2)"` fails

SCENARIO 269 — !system alias library inherits into new matches
---------------------------------------------------------------

!system new SysAlias
!system alias list SysAlias
!system alias def SysAlias dmg "ent hp this"
!system alias def SysAlias heal "ent hp this"
!system alias list SysAlias
!match new msa1 SysAliasMatch1 6 6 --system SysAlias
!match use msa1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!alias list
!dmg -7
!ent dump hero
!alias def heal "ent set_var this"
!alias list
!system alias list SysAlias

!match use msa2
!ent add ally Ally 20 1 1 8
!alias list
!system alias del SysAlias dmg
!system alias list SysAlias

Expected: Initially `!system alias list SysAlias` is empty. After

shows the same two and `!dmg -7` works directly. Editing
`heal` match-side and listing the system afterwards STILL shows
the ORIGINAL system-side expansions — the inherit is snapshot,
not link. The second match (msa2) also inherits both aliases at
creation. Deleting `dmg` system-side does NOT affect already-
created matches: `!system alias list SysAlias` shows only `heal`
afterwards, but msa2's `!alias list` still shows both.


SCENARIO 270 — push_entity and swap_entities formula primitives
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mpush PushSwap 8 8
!match use mpush
!ent add a A 30 1 3 10
!ent add b B 30 3 3 9
!ent add c C 30 5 3 8
!eval "push_entity('a', 'right', 3)"
!ent dump a
!eval "push_entity('a', 'right', 5)"
!ent dump a
!eval "push_entity('a', 'right', 10)"
!ent dump a
!eval "swap_entities('a', 'b')"
!ent dump a
!ent dump b
!eval "swap_entities('a', 'a')"
!eval "swap_entities('a', 'nosuch')"

Expected:
- `push_entity('a','right',3)` -> a goes from x=1 to x=2 (one
  cell, then b blocks at x=3). Returns 1.
- `push_entity('a','right',5)` -> a is still at x=2, b still at
  x=3 -> returns 0 (immediately blocked). a unchanged.
- `push_entity('a','right',10)` after first batch -> 0 again.
- Then `swap_entities('a','b')` -> a at (3,3), b at (2,3).
  Returns True.
- `swap_entities('a','a')` -> no-op, returns False (no error).
- `swap_entities('a','nosuch')` -> raises "swap_entities:
  unknown entity id 'nosuch'." surfaced as ❌.


SCENARIO 271 — on_entity_step fires per cell of stepwise movement
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mstep StepHook 8 8
!match use mstep
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 4 10
!ent set_var hero step_count 0
!ent set_var hero move_count 0
!passive add hero step_counter on_entity_step "entity[self].step_count = entity[self].step_count + 1"
!passive add hero move_counter on_entity_moved "entity[self].move_count = entity[self].move_count + 1"
!ent move hero 3 right
!ent dump hero
!ent tp hero 1 4
!ent dump hero

Expected: After the stepwise move (`!ent move hero 3 right`),
`step_count` increments to 3 (one per cell) while `move_count`
increments to 1 (one for the whole command). After `!ent tp hero
1 4` (single-tp), `step_count` is STILL 3 (tp doesn't fire
per-step) but `move_count` is 2 (tp fires on_entity_moved once).
This confirms on_entity_step is the per-cell event and
on_entity_moved is the once-per-command event.


SCENARIO 272 — Container primitives: var_has_key, var_count, var_sum
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mvc1 VarContainer 6 6
!match use mvc1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword 1
!ent set_var hero inventory.arrows 12
!ent set_var hero inventory.potion 3
!ent set_var hero inventory.broken_flag true
!eval "var_has_key('hero', 'inventory', 'sword')"
!eval "var_has_key('hero', 'inventory', 'shield')"
!eval "var_has_key('hero', 'nosuch', 'anything')"
!eval "var_count('hero', 'inventory')"
!eval "var_count('hero', 'nosuch')"
!eval "var_count('hero', '')"
!eval "var_sum('hero', 'inventory')"
!eval "var_sum('hero', 'nosuch')"

Expected:
- `var_has_key('hero','inventory','sword')` -> True
- `var_has_key('hero','inventory','shield')` -> False
- `var_has_key('hero','nosuch','anything')` -> False (tolerant)
- `var_count('hero','inventory')` -> 4 (sword, arrows, potion,
  broken_flag)
- `var_count('hero','nosuch')` -> 0 (tolerant)
- `var_count('hero','')` -> the entity's top-level var count
  (inventory + the vital vars set by !ent add: hp, max_hp,
  initiative — exact number depends on defaults; >= 4)
- `var_sum('hero','inventory')` -> 16 (1 + 12 + 3; the
  `broken_flag` True is a bool and is skipped explicitly)
- `var_sum('hero','nosuch')` -> 0

!eval "var_pick_random('hero', 'inv')"

  insertion order, so the tie breaks to bow)

SCENARIO 274 — var_clear drops children and fires on_var_removed
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mvc3 VarClear 6 6
!match use mvc3
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword 1
!ent set_var hero inventory.arrows 12
!ent set_var hero loot.gold 50
!ent set_var hero notes "draft"
!ent set_var hero drop_count 0
!passive add hero loss_counter on_var_removed "entity[self].drop_count = entity[self].drop_count + 1"
!eval "var_clear('hero', 'inventory')"
!ent dump hero
!eval "var_has('hero', 'inventory')"
!eval "var_count('hero', 'inventory')"
!eval "var_clear('hero', 'notes')"
!ent dump hero
!eval "var_has('hero', 'notes')"
!eval "var_clear('hero', 'nosuch')"

Expected:
- `var_clear('hero','inventory')` -> 2 (sword and arrows removed).
  The container `inventory` is still present as an empty dict, so
  `var_has('hero','inventory')` stays True and
  `var_count('hero','inventory')` returns 0. The on_var_removed
  passive fired for each removed child: drop_count is now 2.
- `var_clear('hero','notes')` -> 1 (leaf scalar removed entirely).
  `var_has('hero','notes')` is now False. drop_count is 3.
- `var_clear('hero','nosuch')` -> 0 (missing is a no-op, no error).
  drop_count stays at 3.


SCENARIO 275 — Container primitives compose for an inventory pattern
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mvc4 VarComposition 6 6
!match use mvc4
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var hero pack.rations 5
!ent set_var hero pack.torch 3
!ent set_var hero pack.rope 1
!ent set_var hero weight 0
!eval --as hero "for item in var_keys('hero', 'pack'):\n    entity[self].weight = entity[self].weight + var_get('hero', 'pack.' + item)"
!eval "var_sum('hero', 'pack')"
!ent dump hero

Expected: The explicit for-loop over `var_keys` reads each
child via `var_get` and accumulates into `entity[hero].weight`,
which ends up at 9 (5+3+1). The shorthand `var_sum('hero','pack')`
returns 9 too. The composition demonstrates that var_keys +
var_get covers the same ground as the dedicated `var_sum`; the
latter is purely a convenience. This is the canonical "carry-
weight summing" pattern without a hardcoded inventory: pack
contents are just numeric vars under a GM-chosen path.


SCENARIO 276 — Basic action: source proxy + entity target
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac1 ActionBasic 6 6
!match use mac1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent add goblin Goblin 20 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.description "Slice with the sword"
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!action hero slice goblin
!ent dump goblin
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 8
!action hero slice goblin
!ent dump goblin

Expected: First !action runs the body with source.damage = 5;
goblin's hp drops from 20 to 15. After bumping inventory.sword
.damage to 8, a second invocation reads through the source
proxy and subtracts 8 — goblin hp 15 -> 7. The reply line is
`hero used action slice.` in both cases. This proves the
self-reference pattern: copying the same action body to a
"dagger" with damage=3 would automatically use 3 with no body
change.


SCENARIO 277 — fail() rolls back to pre-action state
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new mac2 ActionRollback 6 6
!match use mac2
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var hero mana 6
!ent set_var hero blast_count 0
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.cost 10
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.power 12
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.actions.cast.target none
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.actions.cast.body "entity[self].blast_count = entity[self].blast_count + 1\nif entity[self].mana < source.cost:\n    fail('not enough mana (need ' + str(source.cost) + ', have ' + str(entity[self].mana) + ')')\nentity[self].mana = entity[self].mana - source.cost"
!action hero cast
!ent dump hero
!ent set_var hero mana 15
!action hero cast
!ent dump hero

Expected: First !action fails because mana (6) < cost (10).
The body's first statement BUMPED blast_count to 1, but the
fail() triggers a rollback — so blast_count stays at 0 and mana
stays at 6. The reply is `❌ action cast: not enough mana (need
10, have 6)`. After topping mana to 15, the second invocation
succeeds: blast_count goes to 1, mana drops to 5. This proves
transactional rollback: mid-body writes that came before the
fail() are reverted, not persisted.


SCENARIO 278 — cmd() dispatches an allowed entity command
----------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac3 ActionCmd 6 6
!match use mac3
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero spells.zap.damage 4
!ent set_var hero spells.zap.actions.cast.target entity
!ent set_var hero spells.zap.actions.cast.body "cmd('ent hp ' + target + ' -' + str(source.damage))"
!action hero cast foe
!ent dump foe
!system set default action_cmd_allowlist ""
!action hero cast foe
!ent dump foe

Expected: With the default allowlist (`ent` only), the first
!action runs cmd("ent hp foe -4") and foe's hp drops from 25
to 21. After clearing the allowlist, the second invocation
fails — `❌ action cast: cmd(): command `ent` is not on this
system's action_cmd_allowlist. Allowed: (none).` — and foe's
hp stays at 21 (rollback). This proves the allowlist
enforcement and that cmd() is the bridge between the action
body and the wider command surface.


SCENARIO 279 — Disambiguation menu for two same-named actions
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac4 ActionDisamb 6 6
!match use mac4
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.strike.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.strike.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!ent set_var hero inventory.dagger.damage 3
!ent set_var hero inventory.dagger.actions.strike.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.dagger.actions.strike.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!action hero strike foe
!action hero inventory.sword.actions.strike foe
!ent dump foe
!action hero inventory.dagger.actions.strike foe
!ent dump foe

Expected: The first !action with just `strike` triggers the
disambiguation menu listing both `inventory.sword.actions.
strike` and `inventory.dagger.actions.strike`, instructing the
user to re-issue with a full path. The next call uses the
sword path; foe loses 5 hp (25 -> 20). The dagger path then
loses 3 more (20 -> 17). This proves both that ambiguity is
detected and that the full-path form is the unambiguous
selector.


SCENARIO 280 — Recursion limit guards an action chain
------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac5 ActionRecursion 6 6
!match use mac5
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!system set default action_recursion_limit 3
!ent set_var hero actions.bounce.target none
!ent set_var hero actions.bounce.body "use_action(self, 'bounce')"
!action hero bounce

Expected: The action recursively calls itself via use_action.
With action_recursion_limit=3, the third nested call refuses;
the runner returns False with the message "action recursion
limit reached (3). ..." which the use_action() formula
primitive bubbles up as a FormulaError, surfaced by the OUTER
!action as `❌ action bounce: Runtime error: ...recursion
limit...`. All mid-chain writes are rolled back. The limit
acts as the backstop against accidentally cyclic actions.


SCENARIO 281 — on_action_used fires after successful actions
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac6 ActionHook 6 6
!match use mac6
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var hero used_count 0
!ent set_var hero last_action ""
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.target none
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[self].used_count = entity[self].used_count"
!passive add hero log_action on_action_used "entity[self].used_count = entity[self].used_count + 1\nentity[self].last_action = action_name"
!action hero slice
!ent dump hero
!action hero slice
!ent dump hero

Expected: Each successful !action fires on_action_used once.
used_count goes from 0 -> 1 -> 2 across the two invocations
and last_action is set to "slice" by the passive. The action's
own body is a deliberate no-op (reads but doesn't change a
var) — the hook fires regardless because the action completed
without fail().


SCENARIO 282 — Action body locals + control flow + args proxy
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac7 ActionLocals 6 6
!match use mac7
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 10
!ent add target1 T1 20 3 3 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.base 4
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.body "raw = source.base + 3\nif args.crit:\n    raw = raw * 2\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - raw"
!action hero shoot target1 crit=false
!ent dump target1
!action hero shoot target1 crit=true
!ent dump target1

Expected: First call: raw = 4 + 3 = 7, no crit branch -> hp
drops 20 -> 13. Second call: raw = 7, crit branch doubles to
14 -> hp drops 13 -> -1. This proves locals (`raw = ...`)
work, control flow (`if args.crit: ...`) routes correctly, and
args.<key> attribute access reads through the ArgsProxy.


SCENARIO 283 — target=location uses the Coord proxy
----------------------------------------------------

!match new mac8 ActionLocTarget 6 6
!match use mac8
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero spells.blink.actions.cast.target location
!ent set_var hero spells.blink.actions.cast.body "cmd('ent tp ' + self + ' ' + str(target.x) + ' ' + str(target.y))"
!action hero cast 4 5
!ent dump hero
!action hero cast 2 3
!ent dump hero

Expected: Each !action consumes the next two tokens as x and y
ints and binds them onto the Coord proxy that becomes
`target`. The body reads `target.x` and `target.y` and passes
them to `!ent tp <id> <x> <y>` via cmd(). First call teleports
hero to (4,5); second to (2,3). This proves the Coord proxy
makes location targets usable from formula bodies even though
subscript is banned in the sandbox.


SCENARIO 284 — target=entity_list iterates every target
--------------------------------------------------------

!ent dump g3

Expected: Body uses `for eid in target:` — `_ACTION_LOOPABLE_NAMES`
lets the loop iterate the entity_list directly (without

goblins lose 4 hp: g1 11, g2 11, g3 11. The chain.damage proxy
read is constant across the loop body.


SCENARIO 285 — target=location_list iterates Coord proxies

Expected: The three (x,y) pairs after `cast` parse as a

SCENARIO 286 — Top-level action: source binds to entity vars root
------------------------------------------------------------------

!action hero rest
!ent dump hero
!action hero rest
!ent dump hero

Expected: `actions.rest` is a top-level action (entity.vars
.actions.rest, no enclosing container). Per the spec, `source`
binds to the entity's vars ROOT, so `source.stamina` reads /
writes `entity.vars.stamina` (equivalent to entity[self].stamina).
First call: stamina 5 -> 15, hp 30 -> 30 (default clamp keeps
at max). Second call: stamina 15 -> 25, hp stays.


SCENARIO 287 — Deeply nested container is discovered
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new mac12 ActionDeep 6 6
!match use mac12
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero inventory.bag.bottle.charges 3
!ent set_var hero inventory.bag.bottle.actions.drink.target none
!ent set_var hero inventory.bag.bottle.actions.drink.body "source.charges = source.charges - 1\nentity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 5"
!eval "has_action('hero', 'drink')"
!eval "entity_actions('hero')"
!action hero drink
!ent dump hero
!action hero drink
!ent dump hero

Expected: Discovery walks four levels deep (inventory ->
bag -> bottle -> actions -> drink) and surfaces `drink` as an
available action. `has_action('hero','drink')` returns True;
`entity_actions('hero')` returns `['drink']`. Each !action
reads source.charges (= the bottle's own charges) and
decrements it via source.charges = source.charges - 1.
charges goes 3 -> 2 -> 1; hp clamps at max.


SCENARIO 288 — has_action / entity_actions primitives
------------------------------------------------------

!ent add wiz Wizard 30 4 4 9

!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 5"
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 3"
!ent set_var wiz spells.fireball.actions.cast.target entity
!ent set_var wiz spells.fireball.actions.cast.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 7"
!eval "has_action('hero', 'slice')"
!eval "has_action('hero', 'shoot')"
!eval "has_action('hero', 'cast')"
!eval "has_action('wiz', 'cast')"
!eval "entity_actions('hero')"
!eval "entity_actions('wiz')"

Expected:
- has_action('hero','slice') -> True
- has_action('hero','shoot') -> True
- has_action('hero','cast') -> False (cast is wiz's)
- has_action('wiz','cast') -> True
- entity_actions('hero') -> ['slice', 'shoot'] (insertion order
  via the vars walk)
- entity_actions('wiz') -> ['cast']


SCENARIO 289 — use_action() composition
----------------------------------------

!match new mac14 ActionUseAct 6 6
!match use mac14

!ent add goblin Goblin 20 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero used_inner 0
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 4
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage\nentity[self].used_inner = entity[self].used_inner + 1"
!ent set_var hero actions.flurry.target entity

!ent dump hero

Expected: `flurry` calls `slice` three times, each on the same
target. Goblin loses 4 hp three times: 20 -> 16 -> 12 -> 8.
`used_inner` increments three times: 0 -> 3. Each nested
use_action() succeeds (returns True). The outer flurry then
fires on_action_used once for itself. Recursion stays well
below the limit (depth 2 max).

SCENARIO 295 — args.<missing> error and `in args` guard
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac20 ActionArgsGuard 6 6
!match use mac20
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 30 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero spells.zap.actions.cast.target entity
!ent set_var hero spells.zap.actions.cast.body "amount = 5\nif 'boost' in args:\n    amount = amount + args.boost\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - amount"
!action hero cast foe
!ent dump foe
!action hero cast foe boost=3
!ent dump foe
!action hero cast foe boost=10

Expected: First call passes no args; `"boost" in args` is
False so amount stays 5. Foe hp 30 -> 25. Second call passes
boost=3; amount becomes 8, foe 25 -> 17. Third call passes
boost=10; amount becomes 15, foe 17 -> 2. This proves the
`in args` membership guard works for optional args, and that
args.<key> reads through ArgsProxy when the key exists.


SCENARIO 296 — Action is a single history entry
-------------------------------------------------

!match new mac21 ActionHistory 6 6
!match use mac21
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!action hero slice foe
!ent dump foe
!history list commands
!history undo command 1 confirm
!ent dump foe

Expected: The body does three hp writes via three statements.
Per the design (action depth suspends per-command snapshots),
the WHOLE action shows up as ONE entry in `!history list
commands` (labeled with the !action line). After
`!history undo command 1 confirm`, foe goes back to hp=25
(all three writes reverted in one step). This proves the
transactional snapshot model.

!action hero cast foe
!ent dump foe

Expected: The body builds the command string via local string
concatenation (msg = ...), then dispatches via cmd. Foe loses
6 hp: 30 -> 24. Demonstrates that cmd's argument can be a
runtime-computed string (the body assembles `!ent hp foe -6`
from constants + the target binding + the source proxy
read).

crit(4) returns 8; foe loses 8 hp from 25 to 17. Demonstrates

SCENARIO 303 — Source proxy writes propagate to vars
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new mac28 ActionSourceWrite 6 6
!match use mac28
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero inventory.wand.charges 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.wand.actions.zap.target none
!ent set_var hero inventory.wand.actions.zap.body "if source.charges <= 0:\n    fail('wand is empty')\nsource.charges = source.charges - 1\nentity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 1"
!action hero zap

!action hero zap

!action hero zap
