!ent dump hero

Expected: Each zap decrements wand.charges via the source
proxy. After 5 successful zaps (charges 5 -> 0), the 6th
call's body sees source.charges == 0, hits the `if <= 0:
fail(...)` branch, rolls back, and surfaces `❌ action zap:
wand is empty`. Final state: charges = 0. The proxy writes
have all persisted (one history entry per successful
action).


SCENARIO 304 — Action iterates a container with var_keys
---------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac29 ActionIterVars 6 6
!match use mac29
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero pack.gold 10
!ent set_var hero pack.silver 25
!ent set_var hero pack.copper 40
!ent set_var hero actions.dump_pack.target none
!ent set_var hero actions.dump_pack.body "for item in var_keys(self, 'pack'):\n    cmd('ent delete_var ' + self + ' pack.' + item)"
!action hero dump_pack
!ent dump hero

Expected: The action iterates `var_keys(self, 'pack')` and
dispatches `!ent delete_var hero pack.<item>` for each. All
three pack entries are removed in a single transactional
unit. The body uses cmd() because deleting an entity var via
formula isn't available as a sandbox primitive on this code
path (var_del is the formula-side equivalent — see scenario
269 in the var_clear PR; this scenario chose cmd to show that
delete_var dispatches under an action's umbrella too).




SCENARIO 305 — Action with a range gate (bow, range 4)
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac30 ActionBowRange 8 8
!match use mac30
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 4 4 8
!ent add far Far 25 1 8 7
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.range 4
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.damage 6
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.description "Fire the bow (range 4)"
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.body "dist = distance(entity[self].x, entity[self].y, entity[target].x, entity[target].y)\nif dist > source.range:\n    fail(\"target is outside this action's range!\")\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!action hero shoot foe
!ent dump foe
!action hero shoot far
!ent dump far

Expected: The bow body computes the grid (Chebyshev /
square_radius) distance from the wielder to the target and
gates on `source.range`. `foe` is at (4,4), distance 3 from
hero at (1,1) — 3 <= 4, so the shot lands and foe drops from
25 to 19 (-6). `far` is at (1,8), distance 7 — 7 > 4, so the
body hits the `fail(...)` branch, the action rolls back, and
the reply is `❌ action shoot: target is outside this action's
range!`. far stays at 25. Range is read through the source
proxy, so the same body works for any weapon container that
defines `range` and `damage`.


SCENARIO 306 — Artillery with a min AND max range band (3..7)
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac31 ActionArtillery 10 10
!match use mac31
!ent add gun Cannon 40 1 1 10
!ent add tooclose Grunt 20 2 2 9
!ent add inband Tank 30 1 5 8
!ent add toofar Scout 20 1 10 7
!ent set_var gun artillery.min_range 3
!ent set_var gun artillery.max_range 7
!ent set_var gun artillery.damage 12
!ent set_var gun artillery.actions.fire.target entity
!ent set_var gun artillery.actions.fire.description "Lob a shell (range 3-7)"
!ent set_var gun artillery.actions.fire.body "dist = distance(entity[self].x, entity[self].y, entity[target].x, entity[target].y)\nif dist < source.min_range:\n    fail(\"target is too close (min range \" + str(source.min_range) + \")\")\nif dist > source.max_range:\n    fail(\"target is out of range (max range \" + str(source.max_range) + \")\")\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!action gun fire tooclose
!ent dump tooclose
!action gun fire inband
!ent dump inband
!action gun fire toofar
!ent dump toofar

Expected: Artillery enforces BOTH a minimum and a maximum
range with two `fail()` gates in sequence. Distances from gun
at (1,1) (Chebyshev): tooclose at (2,2) = 1, inband at (1,5)
= 4, toofar at (1,10) = 9.
- fire tooclose: 1 < 3 -> `❌ action fire: target is too close
  (min range 3)`; tooclose stays at 20.
- fire inband: 4 is in [3,7] -> hits, Tank drops 30 -> 18 (-12).
- fire toofar: 9 > 7 -> `❌ action fire: target is out of range
  (max range 7)`; toofar stays at 20.
Demonstrates layered requirement checks: an action body can
chain multiple fail() guards before applying its effect, each
with a specific message.


SCENARIO 307 — Range threshold scales through the source proxy
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac32 ActionRangeScale 10 10
!match use mac32
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add target1 T1 30 1 6 8
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.range 4
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.actions.shoot.body "dist = distance(entity[self].x, entity[self].y, entity[target].x, entity[target].y)\nif dist > source.range:\n    fail(\"out of range\")\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!action hero shoot target1
!ent dump target1
!ent set_var hero inventory.bow.range 6
!action hero shoot target1
!ent dump target1

Expected: target1 is at (1,6), distance 5 from hero at (1,1).
With `inventory.bow.range` = 4, the first shot fails (5 > 4):
`❌ action shoot: out of range`, target1 stays at 30. After
bumping `inventory.bow.range` to 6, the SAME body now reads
source.range = 6 and 5 <= 6, so the shot lands: target1 drops
30 -> 25 (-5). This is the range analogue of scenario 276's
damage scaling — the gate threshold lives in vars and the
body reads it live through the source proxy, so upgrading a
weapon's range needs no body edit.


SCENARIO 308 — !action list / !action info introspect available actions

!ent set_var hero actions.rest.body "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 1"
!action list hero

!action info hero nosuch

Expected:

    - rest (target: none, at (entity root)) — Catch your breath
    - slice (target: entity, at inventory.sword) — Slash

  container = `(entity root)`, target = none, description, and
  the body block.
- `!action info hero slice` shows path = `inventory.sword.actions
  .slice`, container = `inventory.sword`, and the body.
- `!action info hero nosuch` -> "❌ no action `nosuch` on `hero`.
  Available: `rest`, `slice`."

SCENARIO 310 — !find action:NAME predicate

SCENARIO 311 — fail(reason, message): reason tag in error output + on_action_failed binding
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac36 ActionFailReason 6 6
!match use mac36
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 25 4 4 8
!ent set_var hero last_reason "init"
!ent set_var hero last_msg "init"
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.cost 50
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.actions.cast.target entity
!ent set_var hero spells.fireball.actions.cast.body "if entity[self].hp < source.cost:\n    fail('cost', 'need ' + str(source.cost) + ' hp, have ' + str(entity[self].hp))\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 20"
!passive add hero log_fail on_action_failed "entity[self].last_reason = fail_reason\nentity[self].last_msg = fail_message"
!action hero cast foe
!ent dump hero
!ent dump foe

Expected: hero's hp (30) is BELOW the cost (50), so the body
hits `fail('cost', 'need 50 hp, have 30')`. The reply is
`❌ action cast: [cost] need 50 hp, have 30`. The
on_action_failed passive fires (since this is a clean fail(),
not an engine fault), and hero's vars record
`last_reason = "cost"` and `last_msg = "need 50 hp, have 30"`.
Foe stays at hp 25 — the body's damage line never ran;
rollback restored pre-state. This is the canonical
"requirement check + reactive logging" pattern enabled by
the fail-with-reason + on_action_failed pair.


SCENARIO 312 — on_action_used_on_target: defender reacts to attacker
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac37 ActionTargetHook 6 6
!match use mac37
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 30 4 4 8
!ent set_var foe hits_taken 0
!ent set_var foe last_attacker ""
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!passive add foe react on_action_used_on_target "entity[self].hits_taken = entity[self].hits_taken + 1\nentity[self].last_attacker = actor"
!action hero slice foe
!ent dump foe
!action hero slice foe
!ent dump foe

Expected: After each !action, foe's `hits_taken` increments by
1 and `last_attacker` is set to `"hero"`. The passive runs with
`self` = foe (the defender) and `actor` = hero. Foe's hp drops
5 each time (30 -> 25 -> 20) from the action body's write,
which happens BEFORE on_action_used_on_target fires.


SCENARIO 313 — on_action_used_on_target fires once per entity_list target
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac38 ActionTargetList 6 6
!match use mac38
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add g1 G1 30 3 3 8
!ent add g2 G2 30 4 4 7
!ent add g3 G3 30 5 5 6
!ent set_var g1 reactions 0
!ent set_var g2 reactions 0
!ent set_var g3 reactions 0
!ent set_var hero spells.chain.actions.zap.target entity_list
!ent set_var hero spells.chain.actions.zap.body "for eid in target:\n    entity[eid].hp = entity[eid].hp - 3"
!passive add g1 r1 on_action_used_on_target "entity[self].reactions = entity[self].reactions + 1"
!passive add g2 r2 on_action_used_on_target "entity[self].reactions = entity[self].reactions + 1"
!passive add g3 r3 on_action_used_on_target "entity[self].reactions = entity[self].reactions + 1"
!action hero zap g1 g2 g3
!ent dump g1
!ent dump g2
!ent dump g3

Expected: Each goblin's `reactions` is now 1 (the hook fires
ONCE per entity in the entity_list). All three lose 3 hp from
the body's loop. Insertion order matters for the firing order
(g1, then g2, then g3) — visible if you check log lines.


SCENARIO 314 — Retaliation pattern: target-side hook deals damage back to attacker
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac39 ActionRetaliate 6 6
!match use mac39
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add thorn Thorn 30 4 4 8
!ent set_var thorn thorns 4
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.damage 5
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.target entity
!ent set_var hero inventory.sword.actions.slice.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - source.damage"
!passive add thorn retaliate on_action_used_on_target "entity[actor].hp = entity[actor].hp - entity[self].thorns"
!action hero slice thorn
!ent dump hero
!ent dump thorn

Expected: Hero slashes thorn for 5 damage (thorn: 30 -> 25).
The target-side hook then fires on thorn — `self` = thorn,
`actor` = hero — and writes `entity[actor].hp = entity[actor]
.hp - 4`. Hero: 30 -> 26. This is the canonical "thorns"
pattern, built entirely from the new on_action_used_on_target
hook and the existing entity[X].path write — no hardcoded
retaliation system. Note: passives can't dispatch `!commands`
via cmd() (that's an action-mode-only binding); direct vars
writes are the passive-side mutation surface.


SCENARIO 315 — on_action_failed doesn't fire on engine faults (recursion limit)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mac40 ActionFailedEngineFault 6 6
!match use mac40

!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent set_var hero engine_fault_count 0
!ent set_var hero actions.bounce.target none
!ent set_var hero actions.bounce.body "use_action(self, 'bounce')"
!passive add hero log on_action_failed "entity[self].engine_fault_count = entity[self].engine_fault_count + 1"
!action hero bounce
!ent dump hero

Expected: The recursion-limit engine fault aborts the chain
and surfaces as `❌ action bounce: action recursion limit
reached (3). ...`. The on_action_failed passive does NOT fire
(engine faults are bugs, not GM-controlled outcomes), so
`engine_fault_count` stays at 0.

SCENARIO 317 — Summon: capture a template, then summon from it
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msm1 SummonBasic 8 8
!match use msm1
!ent add mage Mage 30 2 2 12
!ent add elem_proto FireElemental 18 1 1 7
!ent set_var elem_proto atk 6
!ent set_var elem_proto element fire
!ent store_entity_into_var elem_proto mage conjure.fire_elemental
!ent remove elem_proto
!ent set_var mage conjure.actions.summon_fire.target location
!ent set_var mage conjure.actions.summon_fire.body "summon(source.fire_elemental, target.x, target.y)"
!ent action mage summon_fire 4 5
!ent dump fireelemental
!list

Expected: `!ent store_entity_into_var elem_proto mage
conjure.fire_elemental` snapshots the configured FireElemental
into mage's vars at `conjure.fire_elemental` (id/position
stripped). The action lives at `conjure.actions.summon_fire`,
so its `source` proxy is bound to the `conjure` container —
`source.fire_elemental` reaches the stored template. After
deleting the prototype, invoking the action with a location
target summons a live entity at (4,5) with id `fireelemental`
(minted from the template's name), carrying atk=6 and
element=fire. The takeaway: a captured entity is just data the
summon primitive instantiates.

SCENARIO 319 — Boss passive summons a minion adjacent every turn
-----------------------------------------------------------------

passive summons an Imp in a free cell within radius 2 of the

SCENARIO 320 — Graveyard tile summons a skeleton on a countdown
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msm4 SummonTile 8 8
!match use msm4
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add skel_proto Skeleton 8 7 7 5
!ent set_var skel_proto undead true
!eval "tile_set(4, 4, 'minion', entity_snapshot('skel_proto'))"
!eval "tile_set(4, 4, 'countdown', 2)"
!ent remove skel_proto
!tile hook add 4 4 on_round_start "tile_set(tile_x, tile_y, 'countdown', tile_get(tile_x, tile_y, 'countdown') - 1)\nif tile_get(tile_x, tile_y, 'countdown') <= 0:\n    summon_near(tile_get(tile_x, tile_y, 'minion'), tile_x, tile_y, 3)\n    tile_set(tile_x, tile_y, 'countdown', 2)"
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!list

Expected: The graveyard tile at (4,4) stores a Skeleton
template plus a countdown in its own data. Each round start
decrements the countdown; when it hits 0 the tile summons a
skeleton near (4,4) and resets the countdown to 2. Over four
turn advances (each a fresh round, since hero is the only
turn-order member initially) the countdown reaches 0 twice, so
two skeletons (`skeleton`, `skeleton2`) appear near the
graveyard. The cadence lives entirely in the tile's data — no
round-number primitive needed.


SCENARIO 321 — Strict summon fails on occupied; summon_near searches
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msm5 SummonOccupied 8 8
!match use msm5
!ent add boss Boss 40 4 4 12
!ent add blocker Blocker 10 4 6 8
!ent add proto Proto 5 1 1 5
!ent store_entity_into_var proto boss minion
!ent remove proto
!ent set_var boss actions.strict.target none
!ent set_var boss actions.strict.body "summon(var_get('boss','minion'), 4, 6)"
!ent action boss strict
!ent set_var boss actions.flex.target none
!ent set_var boss actions.flex.body "summon_near(var_get('boss','minion'), 4, 6, 2)"
!ent action boss flex
!list

Expected: `summon(... 4 6)` targets the cell occupied by
`blocker`, so the strict summon raises — the action fails and
rolls back: `❌ action strict: summon: cell (4,6) is
occupied. Use summon_near to search for a free cell.` No entity
is added. Then `summon_near(... 4 6 2)` ring-searches outward
from (4,6), finds a free adjacent cell, and summons `proto`
there successfully. Final roster: boss, blocker, proto.


SCENARIO 322 — remove_entity despawns a summoned minion
--------------------------------------------------------

!match new msm6 SummonDespawn 8 8
!match use msm6
!ent add boss Boss 40 4 4 12
!ent add proto Proto 5 1 1 5
!ent store_entity_into_var proto boss minion
!ent remove proto
!ent set_var boss actions.raise.target none
!ent set_var boss actions.raise.body "summon(var_get('boss','minion'), 4, 6)"
!ent action boss raise
!list
!ent set_var boss actions.banish.target entity
!ent set_var boss actions.banish.body "remove_entity(target)"
!ent action boss banish proto
!list

Expected: The raise action summons `proto` at (4,6). The banish
action then `remove_entity(target)` despawns it — removed from
the match, turn order, and any groups. Final roster after
banish: just boss. remove_entity is the despawn complement of
summon; "minion vanishes after N turns" is built by calling it
from a passive/action.


SCENARIO 323 — summon_event_limit caps summons within one command
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msm7 SummonRunaway 12 12
!match use msm7
!system set default summon_event_limit 4
!ent add boss Boss 40 6 6 12
!ent add proto Proto 5 1 1 5
!ent store_entity_into_var proto boss minion
!ent remove proto
!ent set_var boss actions.mass_summon.target none
!ent set_var boss actions.mass_summon.body "summon_near(var_get('boss','minion'), 6, 6, 5)\nsummon_near(var_get('boss','minion'), 6, 6, 5)\nsummon_near(var_get('boss','minion'), 6, 6, 5)\nsummon_near(var_get('boss','minion'), 6, 6, 5)\nsummon_near(var_get('boss','minion'), 6, 6, 5)"
!ent action boss mass_summon
!list

Expected: The action body tries to summon 5 minions, but
`summon_event_limit` is 4. The 5th summon raises
"summon_event_limit reached (4) ..." — a FormulaError that
propagates out of the action body, which rolls back the WHOLE
transaction. So NONE of the 4 already-summoned minions persist:
final roster is boss only. The cap + transactional rollback
make a misconfigured mass-summon safe inside an action — it
fails loudly and changes nothing. (Note: when the cap is hit
inside a PASSIVE cascade instead — e.g. an on_entity_spawned
that summons — the passive-error swallow means the cascade
just STOPS at the cap with the partial wave intact, rather
than rolling back; either way the hang is prevented.)


SCENARIO 324 — entity_snapshot + var_set + summon(value form); blueprint independence
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msm8 SummonSnapshot 8 8
!match use msm8
!ent add wizard Wizard 30 2 2 12
!ent add golem_proto Golem 40 1 1 6
!ent set_var golem_proto armor 5
!ent set_var wizard actions.capture_and_summon.target location
!ent set_var wizard actions.capture_and_summon.body "var_set('wizard', 'blueprint', entity_snapshot('golem_proto'))\nsummon(var_get('wizard','blueprint'), target.x, target.y)"
!ent action wizard capture_and_summon 4 4
!ent dump golem
!ent set_var golem armor 99
!ent action wizard capture_and_summon 5 5
!ent dump golem2

Expected: The action snapshots golem_proto into wizard's
`blueprint` var (via entity_snapshot + var_set), then summons
from that stored value (`summon(var_get(...), target.x,
target.y)`) — first at (4,4), minting `golem` with armor=5.
After bumping the SUMMONED golem's armor to 99, a second
capture_and_summon at (5,5) re-snapshots the PROTOTYPE (still
armor=5) and summons `golem2` with armor=5 — proving the
summoned copy is independent of both the prototype and the
stored blueprint (deep-copied at summon time). The two summons
use distinct cells so neither hits the other's occupancy.


SCENARIO 325 — round_number() / turn_index() match-clock primitives
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mrn1 RoundClock 6 6
!match use mrn1
!ent add a A 30 1 1 10
!ent add b B 30 2 2 9
!eval "round_number()"
!ent set_var a pulse 0
!passive add a clock on_round_start "if round_number() % 2 == 0:\n    entity[self].pulse = round_number()"
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!ent dump a
!eval "round_number()"
!eval "turn_index()"

Expected: `round_number()` is 1 at match start. The passive on
`a` watches on_round_start and, only on EVEN rounds, records
the current round into `pulse`. The first `turn next` BEGINS
round 1 (fires the round-start hook for round 1 — odd, so pulse
stays 0). With two entities, the round wraps to 2 on the third
`turn next` (a comes round again), firing on_round_start with
round_number() == 2 — even, so `pulse` is set to 2. The fourth
advance moves to b's turn, still round 2. So after four
advances: `a.pulse` == 2, `round_number()` returns 2, and
`turn_index()` returns 1 (b is at position 1 in turn order).
These are the cadence primitives for "every N rounds" effects,
round-measured cooldowns, and "first turn of the round" checks
— no need to hand-track a counter in vars.


SCENARIO 326 — Natural death by hp damage; corpse stored in tile data
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdc1 DeathBasic 8 8
!match use mdc1
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 8 4 4 8
!list
!ent hp foe -12
!list
!ent dump hero

Expected: Initial !list shows both entities, no Dead: section.
After `!ent hp foe -12` drops foe's hp from 8 to -4, the death
chokepoint in write_var fires the default death condition
(hp <= 0) — true. The death pipeline runs on_death (no
passives here), stores foe as a corpse at (4,4), and removes
foe from the match + turn order. The second !list shows only
hero in Entities: and a Dead: section with foe at HP -4/8
X,Y: 4,4 (corpse). Hero is unaffected.

SCENARIO 329 — Per-entity __death_condition (additive): non-hp death gate

+ Dead: construct. `has_corpse('construct')` returns True.

SCENARIO 330 — on_death and on_revive hooks fire

write triggers the chokepoint — `deaths` is bumped from 0 to 1
(observed AFTER the snapshot is taken, so the corpse carries
deaths=1). On revive, the entity is restored from the snapshot
(so deaths starts at 1) and on_revive fires, bumping revivals
from 0 to 1. Final dump shows deaths=1, revivals=1.

SCENARIO 334 — corpse_id_uniqueness: corpse id blocks reuse by default
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mui1 IdUniqDefault 8 8
!match use mui1
!ent add goblin Goblin 5 3 3 8
!ent hp goblin -10
!ent add goblin Goblin 5 4 4 8
!list

Expected: After the lethal damage, goblin becomes a corpse at
(3,3). The second `!ent add goblin ...` is REJECTED under the
default `corpse_id_uniqueness=true` rule with `❌ Entity id
'goblin' already exists in this match (as a live entity or a
corpse — see the corpse_id_uniqueness rule).`. !list shows
nothing in Entities: (no live goblin) and the corpse goblin in
the Dead: section. The id stays reserved for the corpse, so a
later `revive('goblin')` brings back THIS goblin specifically.


SCENARIO 335 — corpse_id_uniqueness=false: id reuse is allowed

is permitted at (4,4) sharing the id with the corpse at (3,3).
!list shows the new goblin in Entities: and a goblin entry in
Dead:. has_corpse('goblin') returns True. Note that under this
setting revive('goblin') would refuse to spawn (id collision
with the live goblin) — this is exactly the breakage the
default rule prevents.

SCENARIO 337 — __cell_stackable mover can enter occupied cells
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst1 StackableMover 6 6
!match use mst1
!ent add big Big 20 3 3 10
!ent add small Small 5 1 1 5
!ent set_var small __cell_stackable true
!ent tp small 3 3
!ent dump small

Expected: `small` has `__cell_stackable=true`. The tp onto big's
cell (3,3) SUCCEEDS — both entities now occupy (3,3). The dump
confirms small.x = 3, small.y = 3 (stacked on big). Without the
flag the tp would have raised "Cell (3,3) already occupied".


SCENARIO 338 — __cell_stackable resident doesn't block other movers
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst2 StackableResident 6 6
!match use mst2
!ent add scout Scout 5 3 3 10
!ent set_var scout __cell_stackable true
!ent add knight Knight 25 1 1 8
!ent tp knight 3 3
!ent dump knight
!eval "is_occupied = 'cant call directly, but the tp succeeded so cell wasnt occupying'"

Expected: `scout` is stackable and sits at (3,3). When normal
knight tps onto (3,3), is_occupied returns FALSE (the only
resident is stackable) so the move succeeds. Both entities are
now at (3,3). Knight is non-stackable; further entities tping
to (3,3) would now be blocked by knight (since knight DOES
count as occupying).


SCENARIO 339 — Stackable + non-stackable interaction (full matrix)
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst3 StackableMatrix 6 6
!match use mst3
!ent add wall Wall 100 3 3 1
!ent add ghost Ghost 10 1 1 5
!ent set_var ghost __cell_stackable true
!ent add mouse Mouse 1 5 5 12
!ent set_var mouse __cell_stackable true
!ent tp ghost 3 3
!ent tp mouse 3 3
!ent dump ghost
!ent dump mouse
!ent add normal Normal 10 2 2 7
!ent tp normal 3 3

Expected: Stackable ghost tps onto wall (3,3) — succeeds (ghost
bypasses occupancy as a mover). Stackable mouse also tps onto
(3,3) — also succeeds (mouse bypasses occupancy too; even
though wall is there, mouse doesn't care). Three entities now
at (3,3): wall + ghost + mouse. When normal tries to tp onto
(3,3), the cell IS occupied (wall is non-stackable), so the
move is REJECTED with `❌ Cell (3,3) already occupied`. The
rule is: occupancy fails ONLY when a non-stackable mover
enters a cell holding a non-stackable resident.


SCENARIO 340 — summon respects __cell_stackable on the template
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mst4 StackableSummon 6 6
!match use mst4
!ent add altar Altar 50 3 3 1
!ent add wisp_proto Wisp 3 1 1 7
!ent set_var wisp_proto __cell_stackable true

!ent remove wisp_proto
!ent set_var altar actions.summon_wisp.target none
!ent set_var altar actions.summon_wisp.body "summon(source.wisp, 3, 3)"
!ent action altar summon_wisp
!ent dump wisp
!list

Expected: The wisp template has `__cell_stackable=true`. The
altar's action summons a wisp DIRECTLY onto the altar's own
cell (3,3) — a non-stackable resident — and SUCCEEDS because
the summoned template is stackable (summon_entity bypasses
occupancy for stackable templates). The wisp ends up at (3,3),
stacked on the altar. List shows altar + wisp at the same
cell.


SCENARIO 341 — default_kill_function_effects: kill leaves a sensible corpse hp
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdk1 KillEffects 6 6
!match use mdk1
!ent add tough Tough 99 4 4 8
!eval "kill('tough')"
!state
!system set default default_kill_function_effects ""
!ent add unscathed Unscathed 50 2 2 7
!eval "kill('unscathed')"
!state

Expected: With the default rule (`entity[self].hp = 0`), the
`kill('tough')` writes hp to 0 before the death pipeline fires,
so the corpse renders `Tough (tough): HP: 0/99 X,Y: 4,4
(corpse)` — no more weird "99/99 corpse". After clearing the
rule, the next kill skips the pre-death effect; the corpse for
`unscathed` keeps the entity's original hp (50/50). The rule is
the configurable knob you reach for to tune what a corpse looks
like for a given system (negative hp for overkill tracking,
status_add for "dead but doesn't decompose", etc.).


SCENARIO 342 — default_revive_function_effects: configurable revive hp
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdr1 ReviveEffects 6 6
!match use mdr1
!ent add cleric Cleric 30 1 1 12
!ent add fighter Fighter 20 3 3 10
!eval "kill('fighter')"
!eval "revive('fighter')"
!ent dump fighter
!eval "kill('fighter')"
!system set default default_revive_function_effects "entity[self].hp = 1"
!eval "revive('fighter')"
!ent dump fighter
!eval "kill('fighter')"
!system set default default_revive_function_effects ""
!eval "revive('fighter')"
!ent dump fighter

Expected: First revive uses the default formula (`entity[self]
.hp = entity[self].max_hp`) — fighter comes back at 20/20.
Second revive uses the GM-set rule `entity[self].hp = 1` —
fighter comes back at 1/20 (the "Revive Lite" cleric pattern).
Third revive has the rule empty — no effect runs; fighter
comes back with WHATEVER hp was in the corpse snapshot (0,
from the kill's effect), which means the death check
immediately re-fires and fighter dies again. This is the
"foot-gun if you forget the rule" path; the docstring warns
about it. The point: no hardcoded revive policy — the GM
owns it.


SCENARIO 343 — corpse_line_format: GM customizes the Dead: section
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mcf1 CorpseFormat 6 6
!match use mcf1
