!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 10
!ent add foe Foe 8 4 4 8
!ent hp foe -10
!state

Expected: The Dead: section renders foe via the new template:
`🪦 Foe [foe] — fell at (4,4) on round 1` instead of the
default "HP: ... X,Y: ..." line. Hero stays in the live
Entities: section under the unchanged entity_line_format.
This proves the corpse line is a fully configurable template,
parallel to entity_line_format — `died_round` is exposed as a
placeholder, and the tile coords are authoritative (not the
embedded snapshot's x/y).


SCENARIO 344 — !ent kill / !ent revive: command equivalents of the formula primitives
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mck1 KillCmd 6 6
!match use mck1
!ent add victim Victim 20 2 2 7
!ent kill victim
!list
!ent revive victim
!ent dump victim

Expected: `!ent kill victim` routes through the same
Match.kill_entity used by the kill() formula primitive: it runs
default_kill_function_effects (hp -> 0), fires the death
pipeline, and replies "Killed `victim`.". `!list` then shows
victim in the Dead: section (a corpse at 2,2), gone from the
live roster. `!ent revive victim` wraps Match.revive_corpse and
replies "Revived corpse `victim` as `victim`."; the default
revive effects restore hp to max, so `!ent dump victim` shows a
live entity back at (2,2) with hp 20/20.


SCENARIO 345 — !ent push: forced movement stops at walls and occupants
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mph1 PushCmd 6 6
!match use mph1
!ent add boulder Boulder 10 1 1 5
!ent push boulder right 2
!ent add wall Wall 10 5 1 4
!ent push boulder right 10
!ent dump boulder
!ent push boulder right 5
!ent push boulder up_left 1

Expected: `!ent push boulder right 2` shoves it two cells to
(3,1) — "Pushed `boulder` 2 cell(s) to (3,1)." With a wall
placed at (5,1), `!ent push boulder right 10` walks east but
stops in front of the blocker at (4,1): "Pushed `boulder` 1
cell(s) to (4,1)." `!ent dump boulder` confirms (4,1). A
further `!ent push boulder right 5` is blocked immediately
(wall is adjacent) — "Pushed `boulder` 0 cell(s) to (4,1)." The
diagonal push fails the rule gate: with allow_diagonal_movement
off, `!ent push boulder up_left 1` replies "❌ push: diagonal
direction 'up_left' requires allow_diagonal_movement=True."
This is the !ent command equivalent of the push_entity()
formula primitive, sharing Match.push_entity.


SCENARIO 346 — !ent swap: atomic position exchange
--------------------------------------------------

!match new msw1 SwapCmd 6 6
!match use msw1
!ent add aa Aaa 10 1 1 5
!ent add bb Bbb 10 6 6 4
!ent swap aa bb
!ent dump aa
!ent dump bb
!ent swap aa aa

Expected: `!ent swap aa bb` exchanges positions atomically
(bypassing the occupancy check) and replies "Swapped `aa` ↔
`bb`; now at (6,6) and (1,1)." `!ent dump aa` shows aa at
(6,6); `!ent dump bb` shows bb at (1,1). Swapping an entity
with itself is a no-op: `!ent swap aa aa` replies "No swap:
`aa` and `aa` are the same entity or already share a cell."
This is the !ent command equivalent of the swap_entities()
formula primitive, sharing Match.swap_entities.


SCENARIO 347 — command/formula parity: !ent kill and kill() reach the same end-state
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mpar1 Parity 6 6
!match use mpar1
!ent add cmdkill CmdKill 30 1 1 8
!ent add fmlkill FmlKill 30 4 4 7
!ent kill cmdkill
!eval "kill('fmlkill')"
!list

Expected: Both entities end up as corpses with identical
treatment because the command and the formula primitive share
Match.kill_entity. `!ent kill cmdkill` and `!eval
"kill('fmlkill')"` each run default_kill_function_effects (hp
-> 0) then the death pipeline; `!list` shows BOTH cmdkill (at
1,1) and fmlkill (at 4,4) in the Dead: section, with no live
entities remaining. This is the DRY guarantee: one shared
implementation, two surfaces.


SCENARIO 348 — !ent pull: forced movement toward a point, stops at walls/occupants
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mpull1 PullCmd 8 6
!match use mpull1
!ent add anchor Anchor 10 4 3 5
!ent add draggee Draggee 10 8 3 4
!ent pull draggee 1 3 3
!ent dump draggee
!ent pull draggee 1 3 5

Expected: `!ent pull` is the point-directed twin of `!ent
push` — it drags an entity TOWARD a point instead of along a
fixed direction. draggee starts at (8,3); `!ent pull draggee 1
3 3` recomputes a heading toward (1,3) each step and walks 3
cells, replying "Pulled `draggee` 3 cell(s) toward (1,3) to
(5,3)." `!ent dump draggee` confirms it at (5, 3). The second
pull `!ent pull draggee 1 3 5` is blocked immediately: the
next cell toward (1,3) is (4,3), occupied by anchor, so it
stops with "Pulled `draggee` 0 cell(s) toward (1,3) to (5,3)"
— forced movement can't drag a body THROUGH another, matching
push's "stops at the first blocker" rule. This is the command
equivalent of the pull_entity() formula primitive, sharing
Match.pull_entity.


SCENARIO 349 — match-level vars: !match var command surface + match.* formula root
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mmv1 MatchVars 6 6
!match use mmv1
!match var set alarm 3
!eval "match.alarm = match.alarm + 10"
!match var get alarm
!eval 'match.weather.kind = "storm"'
!match var list
!eval "match_var_has('weather.kind')"
!match var del weather
!eval "match_var_has('weather.kind')"

Expected: Match-level vars are a free-form scratchpad that
belongs to the MATCH, not any entity — global GM state like an
alarm counter or the weather. `!match var set alarm 3` stores
it; the reserved `match` formula root reads and writes it, so
`!eval "match.alarm = match.alarm + 10"` bumps it and `!match
var get alarm` shows 13. Dotted paths nest: `!eval
'match.weather.kind = "storm"'` creates {'kind': 'storm'},
visible in `!match var list`. The match_var_* functions are
the runtime-path twins of the static `match.<path>` root, so
`match_var_has('weather.kind')` returns True. `!match var del
weather` removes the subtree and the final check returns
False. Match vars persist with the match (to_dict/from_dict)
and do NOT fire var hooks (no per-entity owner).


SCENARIO 350 — roll(): standard dice notation through the seeded RNG
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mroll1 Roll 6 6
!match use mroll1
!system set default random_seed dicetest
!eval "roll('4d1+2')"
!eval "roll('2d6')"
!eval "roll('2d6')"
!eval "roll('d20+5')"
!eval "roll('oops')"

Expected: roll() evaluates standard dice notation and returns
the integer total, routed through the same RNG random_int uses
(so the random_seed rule makes it reproducible). `roll('4d1+2')`
is deterministic — four 1-sided dice plus 2 — and always
returns 6. Under random_seed=dicetest the seeded rolls are
reproducible across replays: `roll('2d6')` yields a value in
[2,12] (4, then 7 on the next call as the RNG advances),
`roll('d20+5')` a value in [6,25] (the leading count defaults
to 1). A malformed spec is a clean user error, not a crash:
`roll('oops')` replies "❌ roll(spec): malformed term 'oops'
... expected NdM or a flat integer." Grammar: terms joined by
+/-, each either NdM (N optional) or a flat integer.


SCENARIO 351 — default_entity_passives: injected at every entity creation (add + summon)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdp1 DefPass 8 8
!match use mdp1
!defpassive add regen on_turn_start "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp + 1"
!defpassive add mark on_entity_spawned "entity[self].marked = 1"
!defpassive list
!ent add hero Hero 10 2 2 5
!ent dump hero
!eval 'summon({"name": "imp", "vars": {"hp": 5, "max_hp": 5}}, 4, 4)'
!passive list imp

Expected: The `default_entity_passives` rule (edited via
!defpassive, the passive analog of !gclamp for default_clamps)
copies passives onto every entity at creation. After adding
two defaults, `!ent add hero ...` injects BOTH onto hero —
`!ent dump hero` shows `regen` and `mark` in its passives, and
because the injection happens BEFORE on_entity_spawned fires,
the `mark` passive's spawn formula already ran (vars include
marked=1). Summoning routes through the same Entity.spawn
chokepoint, so the summoned `imp` also carries both defaults:
`!passive list imp` shows `regen` and `mark`. This is injection,
not enforcement — the copies are independent Passive instances
the GM can remove per-entity afterward.


SCENARIO 352 — default passive survives revive (death-suppression during respawn)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mdr1 DefRevive 6 6
!match use mdr1
!defpassive add mark on_entity_spawned "entity[self].marked = 1"
!ent add ghost Ghost 10 2 2 5
!ent kill ghost
!ent revive ghost
!list
!ent dump ghost

Expected: A revived entity respawns from its corpse snapshot,
which carries the DEATH-state hp (0 from the kill). Death
checks are suppressed across the revive's spawn + revive-effects
window, so the `mark` default passive's on_entity_spawned
write (marked=1) can't re-trigger the death condition before
default_revive_function_effects restores hp -> max_hp. After
`!ent revive ghost`, `!list` shows ghost ALIVE at HP 10/10 (not
in a Dead: section), and `!ent dump ghost` shows hp=10,
marked=1, and a single `mark` passive (the spawn-time injection
is skipped when the entity already carries that id, keeping
revive idempotent for kept passives).


SCENARIO 353 — scheduled effects: match-level (round) and entity-attached (turn) fire at their boundaries
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msch1 Schedule 6 6
!match use msch1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 9
!ent add foe Foe 30 5 5 5
!schedule round 1 "match.alarm = 1"
!schedule turn hero 1 "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 5"
!schedule list
!turn next
!ent dump hero
!turn next
!turn next
!match var get alarm

Expected: Scheduled effects queue a formula body to run later.
`!schedule round 1 ...` is MATCH-level: at round 1 it reports
"for round 2" (delay 1 = next round) and fires at that round's
on_round_start. `!schedule turn hero 1 ...` is ENTITY-attached:
it fires at hero's turn-start after 1 of hero's turns, with
`self`=hero. `!schedule list` shows both pending. The first
`!turn next` begins round 1 on hero's turn — the turn schedule
fires immediately ("⏰ scheduled effect ... fired") and `!ent
dump hero` shows hp 25 (30 - 5). It is then removed (one-shot).
Two more `!turn next` calls advance through foe and wrap into
round 2, whose on_round_start fires the match schedule, so
`!match var get alarm` shows 1. Round schedules fire alongside
the on_round_start status-tick boundary; turn schedules
alongside on_turn_start.


SCENARIO 354 — scheduled effects: entity-attached dropped on death; cancel by name
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new msch2 SchedDrop 6 6
!match use msch2
!ent add doomed Doomed 10 2 2 9
!schedule turn doomed 3 "match.never = 1"
!eval 'schedule(5, "match.late = 1", "bomb")'
!schedule list
!ent kill doomed
!schedule list
!schedule cancel bomb
!schedule list

Expected: An entity-attached schedule is bound to its entity's
life. `!schedule turn doomed 3 ...` queues a body on `doomed`;
the formula `schedule(5, ..., "bomb")` queues a named match-level
one. `!schedule list` shows both. `!ent kill doomed` removes the
entity, and the next `!schedule list` shows ONLY `bomb` — the
doomed-bound schedule was pruned (the "dropped if the entity
dies/despawns" contract; it never fires). `!schedule cancel
bomb` removes the named match schedule (replying "Cancelled 1
scheduled effect(s) named `bomb`"), leaving "No scheduled
effects pending." cancel_schedule / `!schedule cancel` match by
name and remove every entry carrying it.


SCENARIO 355 — event log: the engine records a combat sequence and renders it via per-type templates
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mlog1 CombatLog 8 8
!match use mlog1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 9
!ent add foe Foe 20 5 5 5
!ent set_var hero kit.actions.zap.target entity
!ent set_var hero kit.actions.zap.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 8"
!log clear
!action hero zap foe
!ent status foe add poison
!ent kill foe
!log

Expected: The structured event log records curated combat
events at the engine's chokepoints, rendered at read time by
each type's template. `!log clear` empties it (here it drops
the two spawn entries from the !ent adds). `!action hero zap
foe` runs an action that subtracts 8 hp: the log captures both
the hp change as a `damage` event ("🩸 Foe (`foe`) took 8
damage (hp 20→12)") and the `action_used` event ("⚔️ Hero
(`hero`) used `zap` → foe") — damage first (it happens inside
the body) then action_used (fired after the body settles).
`!ent status foe add poison` logs a `status_added` event.
`!ent kill foe` runs default_kill_function_effects (hp→0,
logged as a second `damage` of 12) then the death pipeline (a
`death` event "💀 Foe (`foe`) died at (5,5)"). `!log` shows all
five in order. The log is a separate store — it never changes
the command replies themselves.


SCENARIO 356 — event log: custom log(), per-type filtering, format override, and retention cap
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mlog2 LogCfg 8 8
!match use mlog2
!ent add a A 10 1 1 5
!system set default event_log_events "spawn,custom"
!log clear
!ent tp a 3 3
!eval 'log("the bell tolls")'
!log format custom ">> {message}"
!log
!system set default event_log_retention 2
!log clear
!eval 'log("x1")'
!eval 'log("x2")'
!eval 'log("x3")'
!log

Expected: `event_log_events` controls which AUTO event types
are recorded. Setting it to "spawn,custom" means `!ent tp a 3
3` (a `move`) is NOT logged, but the `log("the bell tolls")`
formula primitive IS — the `custom` type is always allowed
when logging is enabled, bypassing the events filter. `!log
format custom ">> {message}"` overrides the custom template,
so `!log` renders ">> the bell tolls". `event_log_retention 2`
caps the log: after clearing and appending x1/x2/x3, only the
two most recent (x2, x3) remain — the oldest is dropped. The
log() primitive returns True when an entry was recorded. Both
the events filter and the format override persist on the game
system.


SCENARIO 357 — zones: footprint (fill/add/remove/shift), data, glyph rendering, and membership queries
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mzone1 Zones 8 8
!match use mzone1
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 5
!zone fill gas 2 2 4 4
!zone remove gas 2 2
!zone add gas 5 5
!zone set gas dmg 4
!zone glyph gas ~
!eval 'zone_size("gas")'
!eval 'in_zone("hero", "gas")'
!eval 'zone_get("gas", "dmg")'
!eval 'zones_at(3, 3)'
!eval 'entities_in_zone("gas")'
!zone shift gas 1 0
!eval 'in_zone("hero", "gas")'
!eval 'cell_in_zone(2, 3, "gas")'
!zone list
!map

Expected: A zone is a named set of cells. `!zone fill gas 2 2
4 4` paints the 3x3 block (9 cells); `remove` drops (2,2) and
`add` adds (5,5), leaving 9 cells. `!zone set gas dmg 4` stores
free-form data read back by `zone_get("gas", "dmg")` → 4.
`zone_size` is 9; the hero at (2,2) is NOT in the zone (we
removed that cell) so `in_zone("hero","gas")` is False;
(3,3) is covered so `zones_at(3,3)` → ['gas']. With the hero
off the zone, `entities_in_zone("gas")` is []. `!zone shift gas
1 0` translates every cell east by one — now (3,3) moved to
(4,3), and the hero at (2,2) is still outside, while
`cell_in_zone(2,3,"gas")` is False (that column shifted away).
`!zone list` shows gas with its cell count, data key, and
glyph. `!map` renders the zone's `~` glyph on every gas cell
that has no entity on top (the hero's own glyph wins on (2,2)).


SCENARIO 358 — zones: boundary hooks fire once on edge crossing, per-cell hooks fire every cell, time hook drifts the cloud
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mzone2 ZoneHooks 8 8
!match use mzone2
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 5
!zone fill gas 3 1 5 1
!zone set gas dmg 4
!zone hook add gas on_cell_enter "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - zone_get(zone_name, 'dmg')"
!zone hook add gas on_enter "log(self + ' entered ' + zone_name)"
!zone hook add gas on_exit "log(self + ' left ' + zone_name)"
!zone hook add gas on_round_start "zone_shift(zone_name, 0, 1)"
!log clear
!ent move hero 5 e
!eval 'entity[hero].hp'
!log
!zone cells gas
!turn next
!zone cells gas

Expected: The gas zone covers (3,1),(4,1),(5,1). Moving the
hero east 5 steps from (1,1) walks it through all three gas
cells and out the far side. The BOUNDARY on_enter fires exactly
ONCE (crossing into the zone at (3,1)) and on_exit ONCE
(leaving at (6,1)) — the log shows "hero entered gas" and "hero
left gas". The PER-CELL on_cell_enter fires for every gas cell
stepped onto — three times — so the hero loses 4 hp x3 and ends
at hp 18. `!zone cells gas` lists the three cells. `!turn next`
is the first turn advance, which begins round 1 and fires the
zone's on_round_start time hook: `zone_shift(zone_name, 0, 1)`
drifts the whole cloud one cell south, so `!zone cells gas` now
shows (3,2),(4,2),(5,2).


SCENARIO 359 — host system: owner runs freely, co-hosts run freely, players are held for approval; approve/deny
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new arena Arena 6 6
!match use arena
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 5
!host add alice
!match hosts
!as player alice
!ent move hero 1 e
!as player pleb
!ent move hero 1 e
!ent move hero 1 s
!as host
!pending
!approve r1
!deny r2
!pending
!as player alice
!host add carol

Expected: The creator of a match becomes its OWNER (here the
harness identity `cli`, set because `!match new` records the
sender). `!host add alice` appoints a co-host; `!match hosts`
shows owner `cli` and co-host `alice`. `!as <role>` is the
CLI/harness identity switch used to preview each role. As
co-host `alice`, `!ent move` runs DIRECTLY — co-hosts share full
command privileges. As `pleb` (no host role) the same two moves
are NOT executed: each is held as a pending request (`r1`, `r2`)
with a "needs host approval" reply; the hero does not move.
`!pending` as a player is refused ("Only a host can do that").
Back as the owner, `!pending` lists r1 and r2; `!approve r1`
runs the held command with host authority (the hero finally
moves east to (4,2)); `!deny r2` drops the other without
running it; `!pending` is then empty. Finally, co-host `alice`
trying `!host add carol` is refused — host MANAGEMENT is
owner-only, even though co-hosts can run every other command.


SCENARIO 360 — channel binding + per-match access overrides (fog-of-war read restriction)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new fog Fog 6 6
!match use fog
!ent add spy Spy 20 1 1 9
!match bind label=host-room
!match channels
!as player watcher
!ent info spy
!ent dump spy
!as host
!host access set "ent dump" all
!host access list
!as player watcher
!ent dump spy
!as host
!host access clear "ent dump"
!as player watcher
!ent dump spy

Expected: Channels bind to a match as a first-class set
(multiple channels can bind one match — a host channel plus a
players channel, or one per team — though the harness only has
the single CLI channel). `!match use` already bound CLI, so
`!match bind label=host-room` UPDATES that binding, attaching
the label reserved for upcoming per-team / fog-of-war views;
`!match channels` lists it. `!ent info` (a summary read) runs
for anyone, so `watcher` (a player) sees it. But `!ent dump`
reveals the entity's FULL var tree, so it is host-gated BY
DEFAULT — `watcher`'s `!ent dump spy` is held for approval
(request `r1`) rather than leaking everything. `!host access set
"ent dump" all` is the owner LOOSENING that read for this match
(e.g. an open-information game): now `watcher`'s `!ent dump spy`
runs and shows the vars. `!host access clear "ent dump"` drops
the override, so dump reverts to its gated default — `watcher`'s
final `!ent dump spy` is held again (request `r2`). These
overrides are per-match host state (they also survive a system
rule refresh, per scenario 361).


SCENARIO 361 — system-wide access policy + per-match override precedence + survival across rule refresh
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!system new fogsys
!system access fogsys set find host
!system access fogsys list
!match new m1 M1 6 6 --system fogsys
!match use m1
!ent add h H 9 1 1 1
!as player scout
!find hp>0
!as host
!host access set find all
!as player scout
!find hp>0
!as host
!system set fogsys friendlyfire true
!as player scout
!find hp>0

Expected: There are TWO access-override layers and this shows
how they stack. `!system access fogsys set find host` sets a
SYSTEM-WIDE default — every match created on `fogsys` inherits
`find` as host-gated (command_access is a dict rule, so it has
its own editor rather than `!system set`). Match `m1` is created
under fogsys, so as player `scout` the normally-free `!find` is
held for approval (request r1). `!host access set find all` is
the per-match owner override; it WINS over the system default,
so scout's next `!find` runs and lists the entity. Then
`!system set fogsys friendlyfire true` triggers a rule refresh
on the live match — the per-match override lives in its own
access_overrides field (not in the refreshed rules), so it
SURVIVES: scout's final `!find` still runs. Precedence:
per-match `!host access` > system `!system access` rule >
engine defaults.


SCENARIO 362 — default access levels: overview reads open to players, detailed/mutating gated
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new acc AccessDefaults 6 6
!match use acc
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 5
!as player bob
!state
!turn
!history
!ent info hero
!ent dump hero
!ent move hero 1 e

Expected: The match creator (`cli`) is the owner. As player
`bob` (no host role), the OVERVIEW reads run directly without
approval: `!state` (summary + entities + map), bare `!turn`
(turn order), bare `!history` (the history help/overview), and
`!ent info hero` (the entity summary). These are player-
available by default — good UX, no host round-trip just to look
at the board. The SENSITIVE / MUTATING commands are still
host-gated: `!ent dump hero` (full var tree, including any GM-
hidden data) is held for approval (request `r1`), and `!ent move
hero 1 e` (a mutation) is held too (request `r2`). The hero does
not move. This is the default split — a host can loosen `ent
dump` per match with `!host access set "ent dump" all`, or
tighten any open read for fog-of-war (see scenarios 360-361).


SCENARIO 363 — entity visibility: invisible enemy hidden from a team POV, full-reveal host-gated
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new vis Vis 6 6
!match use vis
!system set default entity_visibility_condition "is_part_of_team(self, pov_team) or not status_has(self, 'invisible')"
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 5
!ent set_var hero team red
!ent add brute Brute 25 3 3 6
!ent set_var brute team blue
!ent add sneak Sneak 20 5 5 4
!ent set_var sneak team blue
!ent status sneak add invisible
!as view red
!list
!as view omniscient
!list
!as view red
!state full
!as player watcher
!state full
!list

Expected: The visibility rule hides an entity that has the
`invisible` status UNLESS the viewer is on its team. From the
red POV (`!as view red`), `!list` shows hero (red) and brute
(blue but not invisible) and OMITS sneak (blue + invisible).
`!as view omniscient` lifts the filter — `!list` now shows all
three including Sneak. Back at red POV, `!state full` is the
host forcing the omniscient view: as the owner identity (cli)
it runs and shows everything (Sneak included on the map and
roster). As a player (`!as player watcher`), `!state full` is
host-gated (the `full` flag elevates an otherwise-open read) so
it's held for approval (request r1) rather than leaking the
hidden enemy. watcher's plain `!list` still respects the POV
(pov_override is a separate axis from identity, so it's still
red) — Sneak stays hidden.


SCENARIO 364 — per-channel POV via !match bind, shown in !match channels
------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new vis2 Vis2 6 6
!match use vis2
!system set default entity_visibility_condition "not status_has(self, 'cloaked')"
!ent add scout Scout 18 2 2 7
!ent add ghost Ghost 14 4 4 6
!ent status ghost add cloaked
!match channels
!match bind pov=red
!match channels
!list
!match bind pov=omniscient
!list

Expected: A channel's POV is stored on its binding. `!match
channels` first shows `[POV: omniscient]` (the default — a host
channel sees all). `!match bind pov=red` sets this channel to
the red team's view; `!match channels` now shows `[POV: red]`.
Under that POV, `!list` hides Ghost (it has the `cloaked`
status that the visibility rule keys on) while Scout shows.
`!match bind pov=omniscient` clears the POV back to seeing
everything, so `!list` shows both Scout and Ghost again. (The
binding-based POV is the Discord path — one channel per team;
`!as view` is the CLI preview equivalent.)


SCENARIO 365 — tile & zone visibility: hidden trap / secret region filtered from a team POV
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tvis TVis 8 8
!match use tvis
!system set default tile_visibility_condition "not tile_has(tile_x, tile_y, 'hidden')"
!system set default zone_visibility_condition "not zone_has(zone_name, 'secret')"
!tile set 3 3 glyph T
!tile set 3 3 hidden true
!tile set 5 5 glyph V
!zone new secret
!zone add secret 2 2
!zone glyph secret S
!zone set secret secret true
!zone new open
!zone add open 6 6
!zone glyph open O
!as view red
!tile list
!tile info 3 3
!zone list
!zone info secret
!map
!as view omniscient
!tile list
!zone list
!map

Expected: With the tile rule, a tile carrying a `hidden` flag is
invisible to a team POV; with the zone rule, a zone whose data
has `secret` is too. As red (a player POV), `!tile list` shows
only (5,5) — the hidden trap at (3,3) is omitted; `!tile info 3
3` reports "no data" (it won't even confirm the trap exists);
`!zone list` shows only `open`; `!zone info secret` reports "not
found". On `!map`, neither the trap glyph T at (3,3) nor the
secret zone glyph S at (2,2) is painted, but the visible tile V
(5,5) and open zone O (6,6) are. `!as view omniscient` lifts
the filter: `!tile list` now includes (3,3), `!zone list`
includes `secret`, and the map paints both T and S. (Tiles and
zones store their map glyph differently — `!tile set ... glyph`
vs the dedicated `!zone glyph` — but both filter identically.)


SCENARIO 366 — corpse visibility: enemy corpses hidden from a team POV
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cvis CVis 6 6
!match use cvis
!system set default corpse_visibility_condition "corpse_team == pov_team"
!ent add ally Ally 20 1 1 7
!ent set_var ally team red
!ent add foe Foe 15 4 4 5
!ent set_var foe team blue
!ent kill ally
!ent kill foe
!as view red
!list
!as view blue
!list
!as view omniscient
!list

Expected: A corpse is a stored snapshot, not a live entity, so
the corpse rule keys on `corpse_team` (the dead entity's team at
death) rather than `self`. Here only your own team's corpses are
visible. After killing both, as red `!list`'s Dead: section
shows Ally (team red) but NOT Foe (team blue). As blue it's the
reverse — Foe shows, Ally doesn't. `!as view omniscient` shows
both corpses. (`!list full` — host-gated — would also reveal
both from a team channel.)


SCENARIO 367 — default_entity_vars: vars injected at creation, fill-only, removable
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dv DefVar 6 6
!match use dv
!defvar add fog_vision_radius 4
!defvar add inventory.gold 100
!defvar list
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 5
!ent dump hero
!defvar remove fog_vision_radius
!ent add rogue Rogue 25 3 3 6
!ent dump rogue

Expected: `!defvar add` records a per-game-system default var
(value coerced like !ent set_var — `4` becomes the int 4); a
dotted path nests (`inventory.gold` -> {gold: 100}). `!defvar
list` shows both. Hero, created WHILE the defaults are active,
spawns carrying fog_vision_radius=4 and inventory.gold=100 in
addition to its explicit hp/max_hp — the defaults fill vars the
entity didn't already have (the engine applies them at spawn,
before vital-var validation, so a default could even supply a
required var). After `!defvar remove fog_vision_radius`, Rogue
(created next) does NOT get fog_vision_radius (removal stops
future injection) but still gets inventory.gold=100. Defaults
are injection-at-creation, not enforcement: already-spawned
entities are untouched by a later add/remove.


SCENARIO 368 — fog of war (range): a team only sees within its units' vision
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new fog Fog 9 9
!match use fog
!defvar add fog_vision_radius 2
!ent add scout Scout 20 2 2 9
!ent set_var scout team red
!ent add near Near 15 4 2 7
!ent set_var near team blue
!ent add far Far 15 8 8 6
!ent set_var far team blue
!match fog on
!as view red
!list
!map
!as view omniscient
!list

Expected: `!match fog on` turns on the per-match fog toggle.
Scout (red) has fog_vision_radius 2 (from !defvar), so under the
default square_radius metric it sees up to 2 cells in every
direction (a 5x5 area, clamped at the map edge). The blue Near
at (4,2) is exactly 2 cells away -> its cell is visible to the
red POV; the blue Far at (8,8) is out of range -> hidden. (Only
RED units spot for the red POV — Near doesn't extend red's
vision; it just stands on a cell Scout already sees.)
As red, `!list` shows Scout and Near but NOT Far, and `!map`
paints the fog_glyph `?` over every cell red can't see (the far
corner incl (8,8)) while drawing Scout and Near normally. Switch
to `!as view omniscient` (a host/omniscient channel) and `!list`
shows all three — omniscient bypasses fog entirely. (A team's
own units are always visible, since each unit sees its own cell.)


SCENARIO 369 — fog: shared (union) team vision, full-reveal, and toggle off
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new fog2 Fog2 9 9
!match use fog2
!defvar add fog_vision_radius 1
!ent add a A 20 1 1 9
!ent set_var a team red
!ent add b B 20 9 9 8
!ent set_var b team red
!ent add spy Spy 10 5 5 7
!ent set_var spy team blue
!match fog on
!as view red
!list
!map
!map full
!match fog off
!list

Expected: red fields two units, a at (1,1) and b at (9,9), each
with vision radius 1. Team vision is the UNION of what every
member sees (a scout reveals for the whole team), so red sees
the two opposite corners but nothing in the middle. The blue Spy
at (5,5) sits outside both units' radius, so under fog red's
`!list` shows a and b but NOT Spy. `!map full` is the host
forcing the omniscient view (host-gated via the `full` flag);
as the owner it runs and reveals everything including Spy at
(5,5) with no fog glyph. `!match fog off` disables fog for the
match, so red's next `!list` shows Spy again.


SCENARIO 370 — fog memory: explored terrain stays revealed (mode 'full'), toggle resets
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mem Mem 9 9
!match use mem
!defvar add fog_vision_radius 2
!tile set 5 6 glyph T
!ent add scout Scout 30 2 2 9
!ent set_var scout team red
!match fog on
!match fog memory on
!as view red
!ent tp scout 5 4
!map
!ent tp scout 8 8
!map
!match fog memory off
!map

Expected: With fog AND fog memory on, the explored set grows as
Scout moves. From (2,2) Scout can't see the tile at (5,6); after
`!ent tp scout 5 4` it does (distance 2), so (5,6) is now
explored and the first `!map` shows `T`. After `!ent tp scout 8
8` Scout no longer has (5,6) in CURRENT vision, but under the
default fog_memory_mode 'full' the remembered cell stays
revealed — the second `!map` still shows `T` there (only the
area around (8,8) is freshly lit; everything Scout ever saw
stays clear). `!match fog memory off` resets to current-vision-
only and clears the explored set, so the final `!map` re-fogs
(5,6) (it's `?` again, far from Scout at (8,8)).


SCENARIO 371 — fog memory mode 'terrain': remembered terrain shown, live units need current vision
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mem2 Mem2 9 9
!match use mem2
!defvar add fog_vision_radius 2
!system set default fog_memory_mode terrain
!tile set 5 6 glyph T
!ent add scout Scout 30 2 2 9
!ent set_var scout team red
!ent add enemy Enemy 15 5 5 5
!ent set_var enemy team blue
!match fog on
!match fog memory on
!as view red
!ent tp scout 5 4
!list
!ent tp scout 8 8
!list

Expected: fog_memory_mode is set to 'terrain'. Scout (red)
moves to (5,4) and sees the blue Enemy at (5,5) and the tile at
(5,6) — `!list` shows Enemy (currently visible). Scout then
moves to (8,8): the tile at (5,6) stays remembered (terrain is
kept), but the LIVE Enemy is no longer in current vision, so
under 'terrain' mode it drops out of `!list` (you remember the
ground, not where the enemy went). Under 'full' mode (scenario
370's default) the enemy would have stayed; 'terrain' is the
classic fog-of-war behavior.


SCENARIO 372 — impassable tiles: system rule, conditional bypass, per-tile override, mode toggle
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new wb WB 8 8
!match use wb
!defvar add flying false
!defvar add ghost false
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 9
!tile set 4 3 wall solid
!tile set 3 4 wall short
!system set default tile_block_condition "tile_get(tile_x,tile_y,'wall') == 'solid' or (tile_get(tile_x,tile_y,'wall') == 'short' and not entity[self].flying)"
!ent move hero right
!ent move hero down
!ent set_var hero flying true
!ent move hero down
!ent tp hero 5 3
!tile set 6 3 block "not entity[self].ghost"
!ent move hero right
!system set default block_walk false
!ent move hero right

Expected: tile_block_condition makes a 'solid' wall impassable to
everyone and a 'short' wall impassable unless entity[self].flying.
Hero at (3,3): moving right onto the solid wall at (4,3) is
refused ("Cell (4,3) blocks `hero`") — Hero stays put. Moving
down onto the short wall at (3,4) is refused too (Hero isn't
flying). After `!ent set_var hero flying true`, moving down onto
(3,4) succeeds (flying bypasses short walls). Hero tps to (5,3);
tile (6,3) gets its OWN `block` formula "not entity[self].ghost"
which OVERRIDES the system rule for that cell — moving right is
refused (Hero isn't a ghost). Setting block_walk False disables
walk blocking entirely, so the final move right phases onto
(6,3). (Both flying/ghost are given defaults via !defvar so the
formula's var reads always resolve; a missing var would fail the
formula open = not blocking.)


SCENARIO 373 — zone blocking (all-or-nothing walk), push knockback-stop, tp mode toggle
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new zb ZB 8 8
!match use zb
!defvar add ghost false
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 9
!zone add barrier 2 4
!zone set barrier block "not entity[self].ghost"
!ent move hero 2 down
!tile set 5 5 wall solid
!system set default tile_block_condition "tile_get(tile_x,tile_y,'wall') == 'solid'"
!ent tp hero 5 2
!ent push hero down 5
!ent tp hero 5 5
!system set default block_tp false
!ent tp hero 5 5

Expected: Zone `barrier` covers (2,4) and blocks non-ghosts via
its `block` data field (zone_block_condition's per-zone
override). Hero at (2,2) walking down 2 would cross (2,4); the
blocked cell aborts the WHOLE walk (all-or-nothing), so Hero
stays at (2,2). A solid wall is set at (5,5). Hero tps to (5,2)
and is pushed down 5: the push stops at (5,4), the cell before
the wall (knockback into a wall) — Hero ends at (5,4), 2 cells
moved. Teleporting onto the wall at (5,5) is refused while
block_tp is on. After `!system set default block_tp false`, the
same tp phases Hero onto (5,5) (teleports ignore blocking).


SCENARIO 374 — !map resize: anchors, content shift, block vs kill on shrink
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rs RS 4 4
!match use rs
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 9
!tile set 2 2 glyph T
!map resize 6 6 bottom-right
!ent add far Far 10 6 1 9
!map resize 3 3
!system set default map_resize_shrink_mode kill
!map resize 3 3
!list

Expected: The grid starts 4x4 with Hero at (1,1) and a 'T' tile
at (2,2). `!map resize 6 6 bottom-right` grows to 6x6 anchored at
the bottom-right, so all content shifts by the full delta (+2,+2):
Hero is now at (3,3) and the tile at (4,4). A second entity Far is
added at (6,1). `!map resize 3 3` (default top-left anchor, no
shift) would cut everything past column/row 3: Far at (6,1) falls
off-grid. With the default map_resize_shrink_mode=block the resize
is REFUSED — it reports Far as in the way and nothing changes
(still 6x6). After `!system set default map_resize_shrink_mode
kill`, the same resize runs the kill function on Far and completes:
the grid becomes 3x3, Hero (in-bounds at (3,3)) is kept, the tile
at (4,4) is dropped (off the new grid), and Far is gone. Far's
corpse, which sat at the now-off-grid (6,1), is dropped too, so
the final `!list` shows only Hero.


SCENARIO 377 — directional armor / weakspot (side_hit + directional_get in an action)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dir DIR 9 9
!match use dir
!ent add ogre Ogre 30 5 5 5
!ent face ogre up
!ent set_var ogre armor.front 8
!ent set_var ogre armor.back 1
!ent add rogue Rogue 20 5 8 9
!ent set_var rogue weapon.power 6
!ent set_var rogue weapon.actions.stab.target entity
!ent set_var rogue weapon.actions.stab.body "armor = directional_get(target, 'armor', entity[self].x, entity[self].y, 0)\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - max(1, source.power - armor)"
!action rogue stab ogre
!ent tp rogue 5 2
!action rogue stab ogre
!ent dump ogre

Expected: Ogre faces up (north) with directional armor front=8,
back=1. Rogue (power 6) starts at (5,8), directly SOUTH of the
Ogre — i.e. behind it. The stab action computes the struck side
from the Rogue's position via directional_get(ogre, "armor",
self.x, self.y): the hit lands on the Ogre's BACK, so armor=1 and
damage = max(1, 6-1) = 5 → Ogre 30→25. The Rogue then tps to
(5,2), directly north = in FRONT of the Ogre; the second stab
hits the front (armor 8), so damage = max(1, 6-8) = 1 (floored) →
Ogre 25→24. Same attacker, same power, very different result:
the back is the weakspot. `!ent dump ogre` shows hp 24.


SCENARIO 378 — line-of-sight fog: a wall hides what's behind it
---------------------------------------------------------------

!match new losf LOSF 7 7
!match use losf
!defvar add fog_vision_radius 10
!tile set 4 4 opaque true
!tile set 4 4 glyph #
!ent add scout Scout 30 1 4 9
!ent set_var scout team red
!ent add ogre Ogre 20 7 4 9
!ent set_var ogre team blue
!match fog on
!as view red
!list
!system set default fog_los true
!list
!map

Expected: Scout (red, vision radius 10) and a blue Ogre sit on
opposite sides of an opaque wall '#' at (4,4), same row. With fog
on but fog_los OFF (default), fog is RANGE-only: the Scout's
radius covers the whole board, so the first `!list` shows the
Ogre. After `!system set default fog_los true`, fog factors line
of sight: the wall at (4,4) blocks the Scout's line to (7,4), so
the second `!list` DROPS the Ogre (hidden behind the wall). `!map`
shows the wall '#' and the cells in front of it as visible ('.'),
while every cell behind the wall on that row — including the
Ogre's — is fog ('?'). The wall itself is still seen (a target's
own opacity never hides it); only what's beyond it is blocked.


SCENARIO 379 — has_los gates a ranged attack (cover)
----------------------------------------------------

!match new sht SHT 7 7
!match use sht
!tile set 4 3 opaque true
!ent add archer Archer 20 2 3 9
!ent set_var archer bow.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var archer bow.actions.shoot.body "if not has_los(entity[self].x, entity[self].y, entity[target].x, entity[target].y, self):\n    fail('no line of sight')\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 5"
!ent add goblin Goblin 12 6 3 9
!action archer shoot goblin
!ent tp goblin 6 5
!action archer shoot goblin
!ent dump goblin

Expected: An opaque wall sits at (4,3) between the Archer (2,3)
and the Goblin (6,3) on the same row. The shoot action checks
has_los from the archer to the target and fail()s without one.
First shot: the wall is on the line, so has_los is false — the
action fails ("no line of sight"), rolled back, Goblin stays at
12 hp. The Goblin then moves to (6,5); the line from (2,3) to
(6,5) no longer passes through (4,3) (at x=4 it's already on row
4), so has_los is clear and the second shot connects for 5 →
Goblin at 7. `!ent dump goblin` shows hp 7.


SCENARIO 380 — entities_on_los gates a projectile (a body blocks the shot)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new proj PROJ 7 7
!match use proj
!ent add gunner Gunner 20 1 4 9
!ent set_var gunner gun.actions.fire.target entity
!ent set_var gunner gun.actions.fire.body "for e in entities_on_los(entity[self].x, entity[self].y, entity[target].x, entity[target].y):\n    if not entity[e].tiny:\n        fail('a body blocks the shot')\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 6"
!ent add guard Guard 25 4 4 9
!ent set_var guard tiny false
!ent add dummy Dummy 20 7 4 9
!action gunner fire dummy
!ent set_var guard tiny true
!action gunner fire dummy
!ent dump dummy

Expected: Gunner (1,4) fires at the Dummy (7,4); a Guard stands
between them at (4,4). The fire action loops entities_on_los from
the gunner to the target — the bodies STRICTLY BETWEEN, in
near->far order — and fails if any of them is not `tiny`. First
shot: the Guard is not tiny, so the shot is blocked ("a body
blocks the shot"), rolled back, Dummy stays at 20. After the
Guard is marked tiny (a crouching/small body the shot clears),
the second shot connects for 6 → Dummy at 14. The shooter and
target themselves are never in the list (endpoints excluded), and
the GM writes the block rule inline — a different weapon could
ignore bodies entirely (skip the loop) or block only on size.
`!ent dump dummy` shows hp 14.


SCENARIO 381 — first_opaque + coord_x/coord_y; entities_in_line_ignorelos
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new beam BEAM 7 7
!match use beam
!tile set 4 3 opaque true
!eval "first_opaque(1, 3, 7, 3)"
!eval "coord_x(first_opaque(1, 3, 7, 3))"
!eval "coord_y(first_opaque(1, 3, 7, 3))"
!eval "first_opaque(1, 5, 7, 5)"
!ent add a A 10 2 6 9
!ent add b B 10 5 6 9
!eval "entities_in_line_ignorelos(1, 6, 7, 6)"

Expected: An opaque wall sits at (4,3). first_opaque(1,3,7,3)
returns the first terrain blocker strictly between the points as
an (x,y) coordinate — (4, 3). Because the sandbox bans subscript
and attribute-on-call, the coordinate is read with the new
extractors: coord_x(...) = 4 and coord_y(...) = 3. A clear line
(row 5 has no wall) makes first_opaque return None — a GM checks
`first_opaque(...) == None` before reading it. Finally, with
entities a at (2,6) and b at (5,6), entities_in_line_ignorelos(1,
6,7,6) lists every entity on the geometric line (endpoints
included, walls ignored), near->far: [a, b].


SCENARIO 382 — Large entity (2×2): footprint occupancy, movement, accessors
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new big BIG 12 12
!match use big
!ent add dragon Dragon 50 2 2 10
!ent set_var dragon footprint_w 2
!ent set_var dragon footprint_h 2
!eval "footprint_width('dragon')"
!eval "len(footprint_cells('dragon'))"
!eval "occupies('dragon', 3, 3)"
!eval "cell_entity(3, 2)"
!ent add gob Goblin 10 3 3 5
!ent move dragon right
!eval "occupies('dragon', 4, 2)"
!eval "occupies('dragon', 2, 2)"

Expected: dragon is a 2×2 anchored at its top-left cell (2,2), covering
(2,2),(3,2),(2,3),(3,3). footprint_width=2, footprint_cells has 4 cells,
occupies('dragon',3,3)=True, and cell_entity(3,2)='dragon' (the body
blocks every covered cell, not just the anchor). Adding a goblin onto
(3,3) — a cell under the dragon — fails with an occupancy ❌ (the goblin
is not added). After `!ent move dragon right` the anchor is (3,2), so the
footprint is (3,2),(4,2),(3,3),(4,3): occupies(4,2)=True and the
old anchor occupies(2,2)=False.


SCENARIO 383 — Large entity can't squeeze through a gap narrower than itself
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new gap GAP 10 6
!match use gap
!defvar add flying 0
!ent add dragon Dragon 50 2 2 10
!ent set_var dragon footprint_w 2
!ent set_var dragon footprint_h 2
!tile set 5 2 block true
!ent move dragon 4 right
!eval "entity['dragon'].x"
!tile set 5 2 block false
!ent move dragon 4 right
!eval "entity['dragon'].x"

Expected: A 2×2 dragon at anchor (2,2) tries to walk east. A wall sits at
(5,2). Because the WHOLE swept footprint is bounds/block-checked each
step, the step whose footprint would cover (5,2) is Blocked and the
all-or-nothing walk fails with a ❌ — the dragon stays at x=2 (its body
can't pass a wall that only blocks part of its width). After the wall is
cleared, the same move succeeds and the anchor advances to x=6.


SCENARIO 384 — Large entity vision union, nearest-cell distance, AoE membership
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new see SEE 20 20
!match use see
!ent add scout Scout 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var scout footprint_w 2
!ent set_var scout footprint_h 2
!ent set_var scout team red
!ent set_var scout fog_vision_radius 2
!eval "team_sees_cell_rangeonly('red', 5, 3)"
!eval "team_sees_cell_rangeonly('red', 6, 3)"
!ent add hero Hero 30 9 6 8
!eval "entities_within('hero', 2, 'square_radius_distance', '')"
!eval "nearest_entity('hero', '', 'square_radius_distance')"
!eval "entities_in_rect(7, 7, 8, 8)"

Expected: The 2×2 scout (radius 2) projects its sight from EVERY footprint
cell. Cell (5,3) is within radius 2 of its (3,3) corner, so
team_sees_cell_rangeonly('red',5,3)=True even though (5,3) is distance 3
from the anchor (2,2); (6,3) is out of every cell's range -> False.
Entity-to-entity distance is nearest-cell: hero is at (9,6); the scout's
nearest cell (3,3) is well beyond 2, so entities_within('hero',2,...) is
[] — yet nearest_entity('hero') still resolves to 'scout' (the only other
entity). entities_in_rect(7,7,8,8) is [] (no entity covers those cells).
This scenario exercises the union-vision and nearest-cell distance paths.


SCENARIO 385 — 2×2 crossing a fire band: per-cell tile hooks; zone membership
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new burn BURN 12 6
!match use burn
!ent add dragon Dragon 100 1 1 10
!ent set_var dragon footprint_w 2
!ent set_var dragon footprint_h 2
!tile def new flame
!tile def data flame burn_damage 5
!tile def hook flame on_enter "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - tile_get(tile_x, tile_y, 'burn_damage')"
!tile place flame 4 1
!tile place flame 4 2
!tile place flame 5 1
!tile place flame 5 2
!ent move dragon 4 right
!ent info dragon
!zone new gas
!zone add gas 8 1
!ent tp dragon 7 1
!eval "in_zone('dragon', 'gas')"
!eval "entities_in_zone('gas')"

Expected: A 2×2 fire band fills columns x=4 and x=5 (rows 1-2). The 2×2
dragon walks east from anchor (1,1); its body ENTERS four flame cells —
(4,1),(4,2) on one step and (5,1),(5,2) on the next — firing the flame
on_enter hook once per cell, for 4×5 = 20 damage. !ent info: hp=80.
Then a one-cell zone `gas` at (8,1): teleporting the dragon to anchor
(7,1) makes its footprint cover (7,1),(8,1),(7,2),(8,2), overlapping the
zone by one corner, so in_zone('dragon','gas')=True and
entities_in_zone('gas') lists ['dragon'] — a large entity is "in" a zone
if ANY part of its body is.


SCENARIO 386 — Large corpse keeps its footprint; revive restores it; swap sizes
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dead DEAD 12 12
!match use dead
!ent add ogre Ogre 1 3 3 5
!ent set_var ogre footprint_w 2
!ent set_var ogre footprint_h 2
!ent add knight Knight 20 3 6 7
!ent hp ogre -1
!list
!ent revive ogre
!eval "footprint_width('ogre')"
!ent swap ogre knight
!eval "entity['ogre'].x"
!eval "entity['knight'].x"

Expected: The 2×2 ogre is reduced to 0 hp and dies, leaving ONE corpse
(single identity, keyed `ogre`) whose footprint is derived from its
stored vars — it's a large corpse, listed once in the Dead: section.
Reviving it spawns the ogre back at the corpse's anchor with the
footprint intact (footprint_width('ogre')=2). Swapping the 2×2 ogre with
the 1×1 knight exchanges anchors (the swap is legal because each
relocated footprint fits in free space): ogre's anchor becomes (3,6),
knight's becomes (3,3).


SCENARIO 387 — Corpse var introspection (corpse_var / corpse_has)
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new loot LOOT 8 8
!match use loot
!ent add gob Goblin 1 3 3 5
!ent set_var gob loot.gold 50
!ent set_var gob inventory.key true
!ent hp gob -1
!list
!eval "has_corpse('gob')"
!eval "corpse_var('gob', 'loot.gold')"
!eval "corpse_has('gob', 'inventory.key')"
!eval "corpse_has('gob', 'inventory.sword')"
!eval "corpse_var('gob', 'loot.silver', 0)"
!eval "corpse_var('missing', 'x', -1)"

Expected: The goblin (hp 1) is reduced to 0 and dies, leaving a corpse
that stores its full var snapshot. corpse_var('gob','loot.gold')=50 and
corpse_has('gob','inventory.key')=True read the dead entity's frozen
vars by dotted path — the loot / "was it carrying the key" patterns.
corpse_has for a path the corpse lacks ('inventory.sword') is False.
corpse_var with a DEFAULT returns the default when the path is missing
(loot.silver -> 0) or when there's no such corpse at all ('missing' ->
-1) instead of raising. Without a default, a missing path/corpse raises
(not shown here to keep the scenario clean).


SCENARIO 388 — Entity-anchored aura: a zone that follows its caster
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new aura AURA 12 12
!match use aura
!ent add mage Mage 30 5 5 10
!zone new flame
!zone glyph flame f
!zone anchor flame mage 1
!ent move mage right
!eval "zone_size('flame')"
!eval "in_zone('mage', 'flame')"
!eval "zone_anchor_of('flame')"
!ent move mage right
!eval "cell_in_zone(7, 6, 'flame')"
!eval "cell_in_zone(4, 4, 'flame')"
!zone unanchor flame
!eval "zone_anchor_of('flame')"
!ent move mage right
!eval "cell_in_zone(8, 6, 'flame')"
!zone anchor flame mage 1
!ent move mage right

Expected: `flame` is bound to the mage as an aura of radius 1 — its cells
are stamped as the 3×3 disc around the mage at (5,5), so zone_size=9,
in_zone('mage','flame')=True, zone_anchor_of('flame')='mage'. Moving the
mage east to (6,5) RE-STAMPS the aura: it now covers (7,6) (True) and no
longer covers the old corner (4,4) (False) — the cloud rides along with
its caster. `zone unanchor` detaches it (zone_anchor_of -> ''); a further
mage move leaves the now-static cells where they were, so the cell the
aura WOULD have covered had it still followed (8,6) is False.


SCENARIO 389 — Aura anchor-loss: delete (default) vs freeze
-----------------------------------------------------------

!match new auraloss LOSS 10 10
!match use auraloss
!ent add a A 1 3 3 5
!zone new aura_a
!zone anchor aura_a a 1
!eval "zone_exists('aura_a')"
!ent hp a -1
!eval "zone_exists('aura_a')"
!system set default anchored_zone_on_anchor_loss freeze
!ent add b B 1 6 6 5
!zone new aura_b
!zone anchor aura_b b 1
!eval "zone_size('aura_b')"
!ent hp b -1
!eval "zone_exists('aura_b')"
!eval "zone_anchor_of('aura_b')"
!eval "zone_size('aura_b')"

Expected: With the default `anchored_zone_on_anchor_loss=delete`, killing
the anchor `a` deletes its aura entirely (zone_exists('aura_a') goes
True -> False — the aura vanishes with its source). After switching the
rule to `freeze`, killing `b` instead KEEPS the zone: zone_exists('aura_b')
stays True, zone_anchor_of('aura_b') becomes '' (binding cleared), and its
cells are left frozen in place (zone_size unchanged at 9) — a lingering
cloud the caster left behind.


SCENARIO 390 — Status definitions: define, stack (add_level capped), apply
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new sdef SDEF 6 6
!match use sdef
!ent add hero Hero 100 1 1 50
!status def burn
!status when burn turn_end
!status stack burn add_level
!status maxlevel burn 3
!status tick burn "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 5 * status_get(self, status_name, 'level')\nstatus_set(self, status_name, 'duration', status_get(self, status_name, 'duration') - 1)\nif status_get(self, status_name, 'duration') <= 0:\n    status_remove(self, status_name)"
!status list
!status info burn
!status apply hero burn 1 3
!ent status hero list
!status apply hero burn 2 3
!ent status hero list
!status apply hero burn 5 3
!ent status hero list

Expected: `!status def burn` plus when/stack/maxlevel/tick build a
self-describing status (the tick formula is accepted — it parses as a
multi-statement program, NOT a "Syntax error"). `!status list` shows
`burn (when=turn_end, stack=add_level, max_lvl=3)` and `!status info`
dumps the definition. Applying burn lvl1 for 3 turns gives the hero
{level:1, duration:3}. Re-applying with add_level stacks: +2 → level 3
(duration refreshed to 3). A third apply of +5 is capped at max_level 3,
so level stays 3 — `add_level` never exceeds the definition's cap.


SCENARIO 391 — Status DoT ticks at the bearer's turn end and self-expires
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dot DOT 6 6
!match use dot
!ent add hero Hero 100 1 1 50
!ent add foe Foe 100 5 5 40
!status def burn
!status stack burn add_level
!status maxlevel burn 3
!status tick burn "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 5 * status_get(self, status_name, 'level')\nstatus_set(self, status_name, 'duration', status_get(self, status_name, 'duration') - 1)\nif status_get(self, status_name, 'duration') <= 0:\n    status_remove(self, status_name)"
!status apply hero burn 3 2
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!ent info hero
!turn next
!turn next
!ent info hero
!ent status hero list

Expected: burn ticks at turn_end (the default) only for the entity whose
turn is ending. The FIRST `!turn next` starts round 1 (hero's turn
begins — no turn_end tick), so the hero is still at 100. The second
`!turn next` ENDS the hero's turn: burn fires for 5×level (level 3 = 15
damage), hp → 85, duration 2 → 1; the foe is untouched (its turn hasn't
ended). Two more `!turn next` (foe ends, then hero ends again) deal
another 15 — hp → 70 — and the duration hits 0, so the tick formula
self-removes burn: `!ent status hero list` shows (none).


SCENARIO 392 — Pierce up to N targets (entities_in_line_until)
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new pierce PIERCE 10 3
!match use pierce
!ent add archer Archer 50 1 1 9
!ent add a A 30 3 1 5
!ent add b B 30 4 1 5
!ent add c C 30 6 1 5
!ent set_var archer actions.volley.target none
!ent set_var archer actions.volley.body "for e in entities_in_line_until(2, 1, 10, 1, 2):\n    entity[e].hp = entity[e].hp - 10"
!action archer volley
!list

Expected: `volley` pierces up to 2 targets along the row. The body loops
entities_in_line_until(2,1, 10,1, 2) — the first 2 entities near→far on
the segment (started at (2,1), one cell ahead of the archer, so the
shooter at (1,1) isn't counted). Enemies sit at (3,1),(4,1),(6,1): a and
b each take 10 (→20/30), and c is beyond the cap of 2, so it's untouched
(30/30). The helper gives a clean "pierce N" without needing a loop break.


SCENARIO 393 — Armor-limited penetration (composed, no new primitive)
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new pen PEN 10 3
!match use pen
!ent add gunner Gunner 50 1 1 9
!ent add x X 40 3 1 5
!ent add y Y 40 4 1 5
!ent add z Z 40 5 1 5
!ent set_var x armor 1
!ent set_var y armor 2
!ent set_var z armor 3
!ent set_var gunner actions.snipe.target none
!ent set_var gunner actions.snipe.body "pen = 3\nfor e in entities_on_los(1, 1, 9, 1):\n    if pen > 0:\n        entity[e].hp = entity[e].hp - 20\n        pen = pen - entity[e].armor"
!action gunner snipe
!list

Expected: `snipe` fires from the gunner at (1,1) toward (9,1).
entities_on_los returns the bodies strictly between (shooter and the
empty endpoint excluded), near→far: x, y, z. The body carries a
penetration budget pen=3: x (3>0 → −20 → 20, pen 3−1=2), y (2>0 → −20 →
20, pen 2−2=0), z (0>0 is false → untouched → 40). So penetration is
limited by each target's armor — the composable alternative to a fixed
cap, and any other variable (damage falloff, etc.) drops into the same
loop. No engine primitive needed beyond the existing line queries.


SCENARIO 394 — Mid-body choices: choose / choose_number (pre-supplied answers)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ch CH 6 3
!match use ch
!ent add mage Mage 50 1 1 9
!ent set_var mage actions.cast.target none
!ent set_var mage actions.cast.body "element = choose('element', ['fire', 'ice'])\nif element == 'fire':\n    entity[self].burned = 1\nelse:\n    entity[self].chilled = 1\nentity[self].power = choose_number('power', 1, 5)"
!action mage cast answer=ice answer=3
!ent dump mage
!action mage cast answer=fire answer=5
!ent dump mage

Expected: `cast` makes two mid-body choices. choose(prompt, list) returns
the picked element and choose_number(prompt, lo, hi) a number in range;
both consume `answer=` tokens in order (the harness can't prompt
interactively, so answers are pre-supplied). First cast (answer=ice
answer=3): the 'ice' branch runs (chilled=1) and power=3. Second cast
(answer=fire answer=5): the 'fire' branch runs (burned=1) and power=5
(chilled lingers from the first cast — vars aren't auto-cleared between
actions). Sequential choices work because the body re-runs (replay) with
answers replayed in order, walking whichever branch the prior pick chose.


SCENARIO 395 — Mid-body choices: cancel rolls back; missing answer fails clean
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ch2 CH2 6 3
!match use ch2
!ent add mage Mage 50 1 1 9
!ent set_var mage actions.zap.target none
!ent set_var mage actions.zap.body "entity[self].zapped = 1\nx = choose('confirm', ['yes', 'no'])\nentity[self].confirmed = 1"
!action mage zap answer=cancel
!ent dump mage
!action mage zap

Expected: the reserved `answer=cancel` aborts at the choice — the whole
action rolls back transactionally, so `zapped` (written BEFORE the
choice) is NOT persisted and the dump shows neither zapped nor confirmed.
With NO answer supplied and no interactive surface (the harness can't
prompt), `!action mage zap` fails cleanly with a "needs a choice" ❌
rather than hanging or crashing — choices must be pre-supplied to drive
an action headlessly.


SCENARIO 396 — Body parts: damage_part HD2 routing + 0/0 passthrough zone
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new loc LOC 10 5
!match use loc
!ent add knight Knight 50 2 3 9
!ent add ogre Ogre 200 5 3 5
!part add ogre oarm arm 40 40 to_main_percent=50 to_main_cap=max_hp
!part add ogre ohead head 0 0 to_main_percent=150
!ent set_var knight inventory.weapon.actions.hit.target entity
!ent set_var knight inventory.weapon.actions.hit.body "damage_part(part(target, args.where), args.dmg)"
!action knight hit ogre where=arm dmg=20
!ent dump ogre
!action knight hit ogre where=head dmg=100
!part list ogre

Expected: `hit` routes damage to a named body part via
damage_part(part(target, where), dmg). First strike (arm, 20): the arm
(cap=max_hp) loses 20 (40→20) and 50% of 20 = 10 taps to the ogre's main
HP (200→190). Second strike (head, 100): the head is a 0/0 passthrough
zone (auto cap=none + indestructible), so the full 100 × 150% = 150 taps
to main (190→40) while the head stays at 0/0. `!part list ogre` shows
`oarm` 20/40 (50%→main) and `ohead` 0/0 (150%→main, indestructible).


SCENARIO 397 — Body parts: vital cascade + lingering destruction
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new loc2 LOC2 10 5
!match use loc2
!ent add mech Mech 300 5 3 5
!part add mech marm arm 40 40 to_main_percent=30
!part add mech mcore core 50 50 vital=true to_main_percent=0
!ent add gun Gunner 30 2 3 9
!ent set_var gun actions.blast.target entity
!ent set_var gun actions.blast.body "damage_part(part(target, args.where), args.dmg)"
!action gun blast mech where=arm dmg=100
!part list mech
!action gun blast mech where=core dmg=100
!list

Expected: blasting the arm for 100 destroys it (40→0); the arm LINGERS
attached as a dead limb (marked DESTROYED in `!part list`), and 30% of the
capped damage (cap=max_hp 40 → 30%×40 = 12) taps to the mech (300→288).
The mech survives. Blasting the vital core for 100 destroys it AND kills
the mech (vital cascade), then the parent-death cascade removes the mech's
parts — `!list`'s live roster shows only the Gunner (the Mech is a corpse
in the Dead section) and no body parts remain.


SCENARIO 398 — Body parts: hit_location aim feeds damage_part
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new loc3 LOC3 10 5
!match use loc3
!system set default random_seed bodyseed
!ent add t Target 100 5 3 5
!part add t th head 0 0 to_main_percent=150 hit_weights.front=20 hit_weights.back=20
!ent add a Attacker 30 5 1 9
!ent set_var a actions.snipe.target entity
!ent set_var a actions.snipe.body "damage_part(hit_location(target, entity[self].x, entity[self].y, args.aim, 1, 1000), args.dmg)"
!action a snipe t aim=head dmg=50
!ent dump t

Expected: snipe rolls a hit location, but the large aim_bonus (1000)
forces the aimed `head`; damage_part then routes 50 × 150% = 75 to the
target's main HP (100→25). Demonstrates hit_location's aim feeding
damage_part — the headline "aim for the head" combat flow.


SCENARIO 399 — Stat modifiers: layered fold + tags + condition via apply_mods
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mod MOD 10 5
!match use mod
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!ent add gob Goblin 200 4 2 5
!ent set_var gob undead true
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fb.stat damage_dealt
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fb.op add
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fb.value 10
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fb.tags fire
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fm.stat damage_dealt
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fm.op inc%
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fm.value 50
!ent set_var hero modifiers.fm.tags fire,melee
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vu.stat damage_dealt
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vu.op add
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vu.value 25
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vu.condition "entity[target].undead"
!ent set_var hero actions.strike.target entity
!ent set_var hero actions.strike.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - round(apply_mods(self, 'damage_dealt', args.raw, ['fire', 'melee'], target=target))"
!action hero strike gob raw=40
!list

Expected: a modifier is a data record (here a dict bundle authored with
`!ent set_var hero modifiers.<name>.<field>`; tags accept CSV). apply_mods
folds hero's `damage_dealt` modifiers for tags [fire, melee] vs the undead
goblin: adds (fire +10, vs-undead +25, the latter firing because its
condition reads `entity[target].undead`) → 40+35 = 75; then inc% (fire+melee
+50%) → ×1.5 = 112.5 → round 112. Goblin 200 → 88. Against a living target
the +25 wouldn't apply.


SCENARIO 400 — Stat modifiers: equipped source, more%, negative tags, !mod show
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mod2 MOD2 10 5
!match use mod2
!ent add fighter Fighter 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var fighter equipped.blade.modifiers.swing.stat dmg
!ent set_var fighter equipped.blade.modifiers.swing.op add
!ent set_var fighter equipped.blade.modifiers.swing.value 30
!ent set_var fighter inventory.spare.modifiers.swing.stat dmg
!ent set_var fighter inventory.spare.modifiers.swing.op add
!ent set_var fighter inventory.spare.modifiers.swing.value 999
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.berserk.stat dmg
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.berserk.op more%
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.berserk.value 50
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.holyban.stat dmg
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.holyban.op add
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.holyban.value 100
!ent set_var fighter modifiers.holyban.not_tags holy
!mod show fighter dmg 10
!mod show fighter dmg 10 holy

Expected: only the EQUIPPED blade contributes its +30 (the identical
modifier on the `inventory` spare is NOT scanned — equip = move it under a
scanned root). `!mod show fighter dmg 10`: base 10 +30 (blade) +100
(holyban, no `holy` tag present) = 140, then more% +50% → ×1.5 = 210.
`!mod show fighter dmg 10 holy`: the holyban modifier is excluded by its
negative tag, so 10 +30 = 40, ×1.5 = 60. Demonstrates source scoping,
the more% multiplicative layer, negative tags, and the read-only readout.


SCENARIO 401 — Renderer: custom entity glyphs (single + per-facing)
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rend REND 6 3
!match use rend
!ent add knight Knight 30 2 2 9
!ent set_var knight glyph K
!ent add scout Scout 30 4 2 9
!ent set_var scout glyphs.right R
!ent set_var scout glyphs.up U
!ent face scout right
!map
!ent face scout up
!map

Expected: knight renders as `K` — a single `glyph` var, direction-agnostic
(stays `K` whatever its facing). scout uses a per-facing `glyphs` table:
facing right it shows `R`, and after turning to face up it shows `U`. An
entity with neither var keeps the default DIRECTION_ARROWS arrow. Custom
glyphs must be exactly one character (anything else is ignored and falls
through to the arrow), so columns stay aligned.


SCENARIO 402 — Renderer: color settings (surface-gated)
-------------------------------------------------------

!match new col COL 6 3
!match use col
!ent add red1 Red 30 2 2 9
!ent set_var red1 team red
!map teamcolor orcs green
!map teamcolor list
!ent set_var red1 color bright_red
!map color off
!map color on
!map teamcolor orcs notacolor
!map

Expected: team text colors are a match-level setting — `!map teamcolor orcs
green` assigns one and `list` shows it. A team literally named `red`
auto-colors red without any mapping; an entity's own `color` var (here
bright_red) overrides its team color. `!map color off|on` toggles colorized
rendering for the match. Color is only emitted on a color-capable surface
(Discord ansi blocks / a terminal); the headless harness declares no color
support, so its `!map` stays plain ASCII regardless. An unknown color name
(`notacolor`) is rejected with ❌.


SCENARIO 403 — Renderer: color guide + invalid-color warning
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cg CG 5 3
!match use cg
!ent add e E 10 2 2 9
!map colors
!ent set_var e color purple
!ent set_var e color red
!map teamcolor orcs notacolor

Expected: `!map colors` lists the supported color names (all of them render
on Discord ansi blocks and ANSI terminals — there's no terminal-only set).
Setting an entity `color` var to an UNrecognized name (`purple`) still
writes the var but appends a ⚠ advisory that it renders uncolored, plus the
guide; a recognized name (`red`) writes cleanly with no warning. `!map
teamcolor orcs notacolor` rejects the unknown color outright, also citing
the guide.


SCENARIO 404 — Renderer: colored tiles & zones (glyph, fill, formula, warnings)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tz TZ 5 3
!match use tz
!tile set 2 1 glyph T
!tile set 2 1 color red
!tile set 4 1 color purple
!zone fill gas 1 2 3 2
!zone glyph gas ~
!zone color gas blue
!zone color gas "zone_get(zone_name, 'tint')"
!zone set gas tint green
!map

Expected: tile (2,1) shows glyph `T` (rendered red on a color-capable
surface; the harness is plain, so glyphs show without color). tile (4,1)
has a color but NO glyph, so it tints its `.` cell — and `purple` triggers
a ⚠ advisory since it's not a palette name. The `gas` zone fills
(1,2)-(3,2) with glyph `~`, colored by a FORMULA (`zone_get(zone_name,
'tint')` → green, resolved per render). Layering is unchanged: a tile or
entity sitting on a zone cell owns that cell's glyph and color. The plain
harness map shows `T` on row 1 and `~ ~ ~` on row 2.


SCENARIO 405 — Renderer: region-part custom glyph draws over parent
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rgp RGP 8 6

!map
