!map

Expected: the boss is a 2×2 painted with its custom glyph `B`. The `head`
region part covers the front face but has only the DEFAULT glyph, so under
the `part_custom_glyph_priority` rule (default true) it YIELDS — the first
map shows `B` on all four boss cells. After giving the head a CUSTOM glyph
`H`, the second map draws `H` over the boss's two front cells (a second
render pass) while the rear cells stay `B`.

SCENARIO 406 — Stat modifiers: source breakdown, tag-granting, per-stat cap
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mod3 MOD3 5 3
!match use mod3
!system set default modifier_stat_caps "dmg::20"
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var hero modifiers.wet.stat dmg
!ent set_var hero modifiers.wet.op add
!ent set_var hero modifiers.wet.value 0
!ent set_var hero modifiers.wet.grants_tags wet
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vswet.stat dmg
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vswet.op inc%
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vswet.value 100
!ent set_var hero modifiers.vswet.tags wet
!ent set_var hero modifiers.flat.stat dmg
!ent set_var hero modifiers.flat.op add
!ent set_var hero modifiers.flat.value 10
!mod show hero dmg 10

Expected: the `wet` modifier grants the `wet` tag in a single pre-pass,
which activates `vswet` (+100% vs wet). Fold: base 10 + flat 10 = 20, ×2
(vswet) = 40, then the modifier_stat_caps rule (`dmg::20`) clamps the FINAL
value to 20. `!mod show` lists each active modifier WITH its [source] label
(modifiers.flat / modifiers.vswet / modifiers.wet) and ends with the capped
"→ base 10 becomes 20".


SCENARIO 407 — Stat modifiers: set / min / max ops + priority tiers
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mod3 MOD3 8 4
!match use mod3
!ent add h Hero 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var h modifiers.boost.stat speed
!ent set_var h modifiers.boost.op add
!ent set_var h modifiers.boost.value 10
!ent set_var h modifiers.cap.stat speed
!ent set_var h modifiers.cap.op max
!ent set_var h modifiers.cap.value 12
!ent set_var h modifiers.floor.stat speed
!ent set_var h modifiers.floor.op min
!ent set_var h modifiers.floor.value 8
!mod show h speed 5
!ent set_var h modifiers.haste.stat speed
!ent set_var h modifiers.haste.op set
!ent set_var h modifiers.haste.value 3
!ent set_var h modifiers.haste.priority 100
!mod show h speed 5

Expected: in the default priority tier base 5 + add 10 = 15, then the max
op CAPS it to 12 and the min op (floor 8) leaves it (12 ≥ 8) → first show 12.
Adding a `set` modifier at priority 100 (its own higher tier) overrides the
value to 3 — but the min/max clamp ops carry a high op-priority offset and
so apply LAST, after the set: the floor (8) pulls 3 back up → second show 8.
Demonstrates set/min(floor)/max(cap) and that bumping a record's priority
pulls it into its own tier while clamp ops still land last.


SCENARIO 408 — Stat modifiers: defender context role + scaling value formula
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mod4 MOD4 8 4
!match use mod4
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!ent add foe Foe 200 4 2 5
!ent set_var foe undead true
!ent set_var hero modifiers.bane.stat atk
!ent set_var hero modifiers.bane.op add
!ent set_var hero modifiers.bane.value 25
!ent set_var hero modifiers.bane.condition "entity[defender].undead"
!ent set_var hero modifiers.rage.stat atk
!ent set_var hero modifiers.rage.op add
!ent set_var hero modifiers.rage.value "(entity[self].max_hp - entity[self].hp)"
!ent hp hero -30
!ent set_var hero actions.smite.target entity
!ent set_var hero actions.smite.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - apply_mods(self, 'atk', 10, [], defender=target)"
!action hero smite foe
!list

Expected: smite folds hero's `atk` modifiers with the target bound as the
`defender` context role. bane (+25) fires because its condition reads
`entity[defender].undead` (foe is undead); rage adds a FORMULA value
(`max_hp - hp` = 30 after the -30) → base 10 + 25 + 30 = 65. Foe 200 → 135.
Demonstrates a non-target context role and a modifier whose value scales via
a formula evaluated against its owner.


SCENARIO 409 — Independently-located body parts
-----------------------------------------------

!match new lp LP 8 4
!match use lp
!ent add mech Mech 200 2 2 9
!part add mech turret turret 30 30 to_main_percent=50
!map
!part locate turret 5 3
!map
!ent tp mech 6 1
!map
!part glue turret
!map

Expected: a part is glued to the parent by default — hidden from the map
(the first `!map` shows only the mech arrow at (2,2)). `!part locate turret
5 3` gives it its OWN cell: it now renders (an arrow at (5,3)) and occupies
it, alongside the mech. Moving the mech to (6,1) does NOT drag the located
turret — it stays at (5,3). It's still a part (damage_part still taps the
mech, `parent` still resolves). `!part glue turret` snaps it back onto the
parent's cell and hides it again (the last `!map` shows only the mech).


SCENARIO 410 — AoE damage spread across body parts (damage_spread)
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new aoe AOE 8 4
!match use aoe
!ent add bomber Bomber 50 1 1 9
!ent add ogre Ogre 300 4 2 5
!part add ogre chest chest 0 0 to_main_percent=100 aoe_weight=60
!part add ogre head head 0 0 to_main_percent=150 aoe_weight=10
!part add ogre arm arm 40 40 to_main_percent=50 aoe_weight=30
!ent set_var bomber actions.blast.target entity
!ent set_var bomber actions.blast.body "entity[self].lasthit = damage_spread(target, args.dmg)"
!action bomber blast ogre dmg=100
!ent dump ogre
!part list ogre

Expected: damage_spread splits the 100 across the ogre's parts by aoe_weight
(chest 60 / head 10 / arm 30 of 100 total weight) — DIVIDED among parts, not
dealt in full to each (no free AoE headshots). chest (0/0, 100%→main) routes
60; head (0/0, 150%) routes 15; arm (40hp, 50%, cap max_hp) takes 30 to its
own hp (40→10) and taps 15 to main. Ogre main 300 → 210 (took 90), and
bomber.lasthit records 90. Modes weighted (default) / uniform / fragment /
main_only are picked via a mode arg or the aoe_default_mode rule.


SCENARIO 411 — Status effects on body parts: immune + redirect
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ps PS 6 3
!match use ps
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!part add hero arm arm 30 30
!status def burning
!status def fear
!system set default part_status_immune fear
!system set default part_status_redirect burning
!status apply arm fear
!status apply arm burning
!ent dump arm
!ent dump hero

Expected: applying `fear` to the arm is a no-op — the part is immune per the
part_status_immune rule, so the arm gains no fear. Applying `burning` to the
arm is redirected to the PARENT (part_status_redirect) — hero gains burning,
the arm does not (good for per-entity DoT a system doesn't track per-limb).
Per-part `__status_immune` / `__status_redirect` vars override the rules.
Only the apply path honors these; raw `!ent status` editing force-writes.


SCENARIO 412 — Footprint-region part positioning + render priority
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mt MT 10 6
!match use mt
!ent add dragon Dragon 400 3 2 9
!ent set_var dragon footprint_w 2
!ent set_var dragon footprint_h 2
!ent face dragon up
!part add dragon head head 0 0 to_main_percent=150
!part add dragon tail tail 30 30 to_main_percent=30
!part region head front
!part region tail back
!ent set_var head glyph H
!map
!ent face dragon right
!map

Expected: the dragon is a 2×2. `part region head front` makes the head cover
the parent's front row, `tail back` the back row — facing-aware. The head has
a custom glyph `H`, so it renders ABOVE the parent on its front cells; the
tail uses the default glyph, so it yields to the parent (part_custom_glyph_
priority). Facing up: top row shows `H H`, bottom row the dragon's `^ ^`
arrows. Turning to face right rotates the `front` region to the right column,
so the `H`s move to the right side and the arrows to the left.


SCENARIO 413 — Spatial AoE on a multi-tile entity (origin + radius)
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new sa SA 10 6
!match use sa
!ent add gunner Gunner 30 1 1 9
!ent add dragon Dragon 400 4 2 5
!ent set_var dragon footprint_w 2
!ent set_var dragon footprint_h 2
!ent face dragon up
!part add dragon head head 0 0 to_main_percent=150
!part add dragon tail tail 40 40 to_main_percent=50
!part region head front
!part region tail back
!ent set_var gunner actions.frontblast.target entity
!ent set_var gunner actions.frontblast.body "entity[self].dealt = damage_spread(target, 80, 'weighted', 0, 4, 2, 0)"
!action gunner frontblast dragon
!ent dump dragon

Expected: damage_spread with origin (4,2) + radius 0 only includes parts
with a cell reaching that point — the head (front row, which includes (4,2))
but NOT the tail (back row). So the whole 80 lands on the head (150%→main =
120); dragon main 400 → 280, gunner.dealt = 120, the tail untouched. That's
how a blast that doesn't reach the whole big body is modeled.


SCENARIO 414 — Composite multi-tile entity: region head + torso parts
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new comp COMP 12 6
!match use comp
!ent add boss Boss 300 3 3 9
!ent set_var boss footprint_w 2
!ent set_var boss footprint_h 2
!ent face boss right
!part add boss head head 0 0 to_main_percent=150
!part region head front
!part add boss torso torso 0 0 to_main_percent=100
!part region torso all
!eval "len(footprint_cells('boss'))"
!eval "len(footprint_cells('head'))"
!eval "len(footprint_cells('torso'))"
!ent add atk Atk 30 9 3 7
!ent set_var atk actions.hit.target entity
!ent set_var atk actions.hit.body "damage_part(part(target, args.p), args.d)"
!action atk hit boss p=head d=40
!action atk hit boss p=torso d=40
!list
!part list boss

Expected: boss is a 2×2 entity (footprint_w/h = 2) facing right, so its
footprint is 4 cells. The `head` region part = the `front` face → the 2
forward (x=4) cells; the `torso` region part = `all` → 4 cells (region cells
re-derive from the parent's live facing). Both are 0/0 indestructible
passthrough zones, so damage routes fully to main by their percent: head 40
× 150% = 60 (300→240), torso 40 × 100% = 40 (240→200). `len(footprint_cells())`
returns 4 / 2 / 4 for boss / head / torso. The user's 2×2-with-front-head
composite shape, end to end.


SCENARIO 415 — Body part detach becomes a free standalone entity
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dp DP 10 5
!match use dp
!ent add ogre Ogre 100 5 3 5
!part add ogre arm arm 30 30 to_main_percent=50
!eval "has_part('ogre', 'arm')"
!eval "part_of('arm')"
!part detach arm
!eval "has_part('ogre', 'arm')"
!eval "part_of('arm')"
!list

Expected: while attached, `has_part('ogre','arm')` is true and
`part_of('arm')` is `ogre`. `!part detach arm` turns the part into a FREE
standalone entity at the parent's cell, keeping its hp (30/30): afterwards
`has_part('ogre','arm')` is false and `part_of('arm')` is `''` (empty), and
`!list` shows both Ogre and Arm as independent live entities.


SCENARIO 416 — Parent death snapshots parts; revive restores them
-----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new pr PR 10 5
!match use pr
!ent add golem Golem 40 5 3 5
!part add golem core core 25 25 to_main_percent=30
!part add golem fist fist 20 20 to_main_percent=50
!ent add cleric Cleric 30 1 3 12
!ent set_var cleric actions.raise.target corpse
!ent set_var cleric actions.raise.body "revive(target)"
!ent hp golem -50
!list
!eval "has_corpse('golem')"
!action cleric raise golem
!list
!part list golem

Expected: golem (40 hp) dies to -50 damage. Its parts (core, fist) are
snapshotted into the corpse and removed from the live roster, so `!list`
shows only Cleric live + golem in the Dead: section (no orphaned limbs);
`has_corpse('golem')` is true. `cleric raise golem` revives the corpse, and
the parent's footprint/parts are restored for free — `!part list golem`
again shows core and fist attached.


SCENARIO 417 — Killing a body part destroys it (no corpse); only parents corpse
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new pc PC 10 5
!match use pc
!ent add ogre Ogre 60 5 3 5
!part add ogre arm arm 30 30 to_main_percent=50
!part add ogre core core 20 20 vital=true
!eval "kill('arm')"
!eval "has_corpse('arm')"
!list
!eval "kill('core')"
!eval "has_corpse('ogre')"
!eval "has_corpse('core')"
!list

Expected: `kill('arm')` (a non-vital part) destroys the arm IN PLACE — it
lingers as a dead 0-hp limb attached to the ogre, and `has_corpse('arm')` is
False (a part never leaves its own revivable corpse). Killing the `vital`
core cascades to the parent: the ogre dies and leaves ONE corpse
(`has_corpse('ogre')` True) with its parts snapshotted inside, while
`has_corpse('core')` is False. Corpses are a parent-only concept.

SCENARIO 418 — Destroyer: body segments trail the head; damage routes to main
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dz DZ 16 5
!match use dz
!ent add d Destroyer 120 8 2 9
!ent face d right
!part segment d b0 Body0 0 0 to_main_percent=100
!part segment d b1 Body1 0 0 to_main_percent=100
!part segment d b2 Body2 0 0 to_main_percent=100
!list
!ent move d right
!ent move d right
!list
!map
!ent add wall Wall 10 13 2
!ent tp wall 8 2
!ent add gun Gunner 30 2 4 7
!ent set_var gun actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var gun actions.shoot.body "damage_part(part(target, args.p), args.d)"
!action gun shoot d p=b1 d=25
!list

Expected: a head with three 0/0 indestructible body segments trailing behind
it (laid to the left of the head at (8,2), so b0 (7,2), b1 (6,2), b2 (5,2)).
Each `ent move d right` shifts the whole chain one cell into the head's
vacated path — after two moves the head is at (10,2) and the body at (9,2)/
(8,2)/(7,2). The whole worm RENDERS on the map (head + three body cells in a
row) even though the segments are at 0/0 hp — an indestructible 0/0 entity
reads as alive, so it isn't dropped from the map/occupancy. The body is solid
to other movers: teleporting Wall onto a body cell (8,2) is blocked. Shooting
body segment b1 routes the full 25 × 100% to the head's main HP (120 → 95)
while the 0/0 segment is unharmed: hit any part of the worm, damage the whole
worm.


SCENARIO 419 — Snake sever (cascade): a cut destroys everything behind it

Cutting s1 (99 damage) destroys it AND every segment behind it (s2, s3) —
the back of the worm is severed and removed (no corpses). The head w and the
front segment s0 survive; `!part list w` shows only s0 still attached.


SCENARIO 420 — Snake split (Eater of Worlds): a cut spawns a second head

SCENARIO 421 — Snake self-collision: pass-through vs blocked

!ent face b right
!part segment b b0 B0 5 5
!part segment b b1 B1 5 5

Expected: SnakeA uses the default (self-collision OFF), so moving its head
LEFT — into the cell its own segment a0 occupies — is allowed (the Destroyer
passes through itself); A's head ends at (4,2). After turning self-collision
ON, SnakeB's head moving LEFT into its own body cell (b0) is BLOCKED, so B's
head stays at (5,5). Other entities are blocked by segments either way.

SCENARIO 423 — Range-band falloff (band primitive)
--------------------------------------------------

!match new rb RB 12 3
!match use rb
!ent add archer Archer 50 1 2 9
!ent add t1 T1 200 3 2 5
!ent add t2 T2 200 6 2 5
!ent add t3 T3 200 11 2 5
!ent set_var archer actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var archer actions.shoot.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - band(distance(entity[self].x, entity[self].y, entity[target].x, entity[target].y), '1-2:120,3-5:100,6-9:80,10+:0')"
!action archer shoot t1
!action archer shoot t2
!action archer shoot t3
!list

Expected: `shoot` deals damage by range band. archer at (1,2): t1 (3,2) is
distance 2 → band 1-2 → 120 (200→80); t2 (6,2) is distance 5 → band 3-5 →
100 (200→100); t3 (11,2) is distance 10 → band 10+ → 0 (untouched, 200).
band(value, spec) returns the first matching band's result — the doc's
munition falloff without a chain of conditionals.


SCENARIO 424 — Range-band: inclusive / open-ended / exact / default forms
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new bnd BND 6 3
!match use bnd
!ent add d Dummy 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var d actions.t.target none
!ent set_var d actions.t.body "entity[self].a = band(1, '1-3:10,4+:20')\nentity[self].b = band(5, '1-3:10,4+:20')\nentity[self].c = band(2, '-1:1,3+:3', 99)\nentity[self].e = band(100, '1-2:5', -1)"
!action d t
!ent dump d

Expected: `a` = 10 (1 falls in the inclusive 1-3 band); `b` = 20 (5 matches
the open `4+` band); `c` = 99 (2 matches neither `-1` [≤1] nor `3+` [≥3], so
the default 99 is returned); `e` = -1 (no band matches 100, default -1).
Exercises lo-hi, lo+, -hi and the default fall-through.


SCENARIO 425 — Reusable macro with positional args
--------------------------------------------------

!match new mc MC 8 4
!match use mc
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!macro set buff "ent set_var $1 blessed 1\nent set_var $1 power $2"
!macro run buff hero 7
!ent dump hero
!macro list

Expected: `macro set` stores a two-line sequence using $1/$2. `macro run
buff hero 7` substitutes $1=hero, $2=7 and runs both lines as ONE undo
entry, so hero gets blessed=1 and power=7. `macro list` shows `buff`.


SCENARIO 426 — Macro: $@ all-args, $() formula token preserved, one-undo-entry
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mcr MCR 8 4
!match use mcr
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!macro set buff "ent set_var $1 atk $(10+5)\nent set_var $1 turns $2"
!macro run buff hero 3
!ent dump hero
!macro set hurt "ent hp $@"
!macro run hurt hero -40
!list
!undo command
!list

Expected: `macro run buff hero 3` substitutes $1=hero, $2=3, and leaves the
$(10+5) formula token untouched for the dispatcher to evaluate → atk=15,
turns=3. The `hurt` macro forwards $@ (ALL args, space-joined) as the
command's arguments, so `macro run hurt hero -40` runs `ent hp hero -40` →
hero 100→60. The whole macro is ONE undo entry, so `!undo command` reverts
the macro — hero is back to 100.


SCENARIO 427 — Condition-watcher (edge-triggered)
-------------------------------------------------

!match new wt WT 8 4
!match use wt
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!watch add lowhp "entity[hero].hp < 50" "entity[hero].alarms = var_get('hero', 'alarms', 0) + 1"
!ent hp hero -60
!ent dump hero
!ent hp hero -10
!ent dump hero

Expected: the watcher fires when hero's hp crosses below 50. `ent hp hero
-60` (hp 40) trips the false→true edge on the post-command check, so the
effect runs once → alarms=1. A further `-10` (hp 30) keeps the condition
true (no NEW edge), so alarms STAYS 1 — watchers fire on the transition,
not every poll. (Re-arms only after the condition goes false again.)


SCENARIO 428 — Watchers: single-pass, next-poll chaining, once-removal
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new wt2 WT2 8 4
!match use wt2
!ent add hero Hero 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var hero stage 0
!watch add w1 "entity[hero].hp < 70" "entity[hero].stage = 1"
!watch add w2 "entity[hero].stage == 1" "entity[hero].stage = 2" once
!ent hp hero -40
!ent dump hero
!ent face hero left
!ent dump hero
!watch list

Expected: `ent hp hero -40` (hp 60) trips w1's edge; because all edges are
recorded BEFORE any effect runs, w2 still reads stage 0 this pass and does
NOT fire — first dump shows stage 1. The next command (`ent face`) polls
again: w1's condition is still true (no new edge), but w2 now sees stage==1,
fires (false→true), sets stage 2, and `once` removes it — second dump shows
stage 2. `watch list` shows only w1 remaining. Single-pass + next-poll
chaining + once.


SCENARIO 429 — Team resources + team-scoped modifiers
-----------------------------------------------------

!match new tm TM 8 4
!match use tm
!ent add red1 Red1 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var red1 team red
!ent add blue1 Blue1 100 5 2 5
!ent set_var blue1 team blue
!team set red command_points 3
!team add red command_points 2
!team set red modifiers.rally.stat atk
!team set red modifiers.rally.op add
!team set red modifiers.rally.value 10
!team passive add red onrnd on_round_start "entity[self].rallied = 1"
!mod show red1 atk 5
!mod show blue1 atk 5
!team get red command_points

Expected: team `red` has a shared pool — command_points 3, then +2 = 5
(team_get/team_set/team_add). Its `modifiers.rally` (+10 atk) auto-applies
to every red member: `!mod show red1 atk 5` folds to 15 (5 base + 10, source
`team:red`), while blue1 (other team) stays 5. The team passive `onrnd`
fires for red members on round start (self = the member). `!team get` reads
the pool back.


SCENARIO 430 — Team passives fire for members on turn start (not other teams)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tmp TMP 8 4
!match use tmp
!ent add r1 R1 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var r1 team red
!ent add r2 R2 100 3 2 8
!ent set_var r2 team red
!ent add b1 B1 100 5 2 5
!ent set_var b1 team blue
!team set red morale 0
!team passive add red rally on_turn_start "team_add('red', 'morale', 1)"
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!team get red morale

Expected: the team passive `rally` fires on each red member's turn-start
(self = that member) and bumps the shared `red.morale` via team_add. Turn
order by initiative is r1(9), r2(8), b1(5): the first `turn next` starts
r1's turn (red → morale 1), the second starts r2's (red → morale 2), the
third starts b1's (blue → rally does NOT fire). `team get red morale` → 2.
Demonstrates team-scoped passives firing for members only and team_add from
a formula.


SCENARIO 431 — Team modifier folds into a member's apply_mods; team_get gate
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tmm TMM 8 4
!match use tmm
!ent add r1 R1 100 2 2 9
!ent set_var r1 team red
!ent add foe Foe 200 4 2 5
!ent set_var foe team blue
!team set red modifiers.warcry.stat atk
!team set red modifiers.warcry.op add
!team set red modifiers.warcry.value 15
!team set red power 1
!ent set_var r1 actions.strike.target entity
!ent set_var r1 actions.strike.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - apply_mods(self, 'atk', 20, []) * team_get('red', 'power', 0)"
!action r1 strike foe
!list

Expected: red's `modifiers.warcry` (+15 atk) auto-applies to member r1, so
apply_mods(r1,'atk',20,[]) folds to 35; multiplied by the team resource
team_get('red','power') = 1 → 35 damage. Foe 200 → 165. A team modifier
flowing into a member's combat formula AND a team resource read in the same
body.





SCENARIO 432 — alive_condition rule: custom aliveness + is_indestructible
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ac AC 12 5
!match use ac
!ent add boss Boss 60 5 2
!part segment boss seg Seg 0 0 to_main_percent=100
!map
!system set default alive_condition "entity[self].hp > 0"
!map
!system set default alive_condition "entity[self].hp > 0 or is_indestructible(self)"
!map

Expected: with the default (empty) alive_condition, the 0/0 indestructible
body segment counts as alive and renders on the map alongside the boss
(built-in carve-out). Setting alive_condition to `entity[self].hp > 0`
REPLACES the built-in rule, so the 0/0 segment now reads as not-alive and
drops off the map (only the boss glyph remains). Re-adding the carve-out with
the is_indestructible(self) primitive brings the segment back — the GM owns
the rule, and the primitive lets a custom condition reproduce the default
behavior.


SCENARIO 433 — body_part_entity_line_suffix: sub-entities show their parent
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new sf SF 12 5
!match use sf
!ent add dragon Dragon 80 6 2
!part add dragon head Head 20 20
!part locate head 7 2
!part segment dragon tail Tail 10 10
!list
!system set default body_part_entity_line_suffix " «{parent_name}#{parent}»"
!list
!system set default body_part_entity_line_suffix ""
!list

Expected: by default every sub-entity row in !list carries the
` [part of {parent}]` suffix — the located Head and the Tail segment both
show `[part of dragon]`, while Dragon's own line has none. A custom template
` «{parent_name}#{parent}»` renders ` «Dragon#dragon»` on those rows instead.
Setting the suffix empty removes the annotation entirely (the rows render as
plain entity lines).


SCENARIO 434 — Box-face side_hit: a multi-tile flank reads "side", not "front"
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new bf BF 14 12
!match use bf
!ent add tower Tower 60 5 4 9
!ent face tower up
!ent set_var tower footprint_w 1
!ent set_var tower footprint_h 4
!eval "side_hit('tower', 6, 4)"
!eval "side_hit('tower', 6, 4, 4, 30, 'center')"
!ent add small Small 10 10 4 9
!ent face small up
!eval "side_hit('small', 11, 4)"
!eval "side_hit('small', 11, 4, 4, 30, 'center')"

Expected: Tower is a 1×4 body (a tall, thin column) facing up, occupying
(5,4)-(5,7). An attacker at (6,4) is directly EAST of the tower's front cell —
right beside the thin body. The default `box` hitbox aspect-corrects by the
footprint (it's only 1 wide), so side_hit reads `right_side`. The legacy
`center` mode measures the bare bearing to the body's distant center (5,5.5),
a shallow angle, and reads `front`. The 1×1 Small entity is identical under
both modes — `box` and `center` both read `right_side` for a hit from (11,4) —
because the aspect correction is uniform when width == height.


SCENARIO 435 — Box-face directional armor on a large body (flank beats front)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ba BA 14 12
!match use ba
!ent add tower Tower 60 5 4 9
!ent face tower up
!ent set_var tower footprint_w 1
!ent set_var tower footprint_h 4
!ent set_var tower armor.front 8
!ent set_var tower armor.right_side 2
!ent add gun Gunner 20 6 4 7
!ent set_var gun weapon.power 10
!ent set_var gun weapon.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var gun weapon.actions.shoot.body "armor = directional_get(target, 'armor', entity[self].x, entity[self].y, 0)\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - max(1, source.power - armor)"
!eval "directional_get('tower', 'armor', 6, 4, 0)"
!eval "directional_get('tower', 'armor', 6, 4, 0, 4, 30, 'center')"
!action gun shoot tower
!ent dump tower

Expected: the 1×4 Tower (facing up) has front armor 8 and right_side armor 2.
The Gunner at (6,4) is beside the tower's front. With the default box hitbox
the struck side is `right_side`, so directional_get reads armor 2 → the stab
deals max(1, 10-2) = 8 → Tower 60→52. The contrast `!eval` with `center`
shows the legacy geometry would have read the FRONT (armor 8), which would
have floored the hit at max(1, 10-8) = 2. Aspect-aware hit geometry makes a
long body's flank a real weak point. `!ent dump tower` shows hp 52.


SCENARIO 436 — raycast: a beam lands on the cell before cover
-------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rc RC 10 8
!match use rc
!tile set 5 4 opaque true
!eval "coord_x(raycast(5, 1, 5, 7))"
!eval "coord_y(raycast(5, 1, 5, 7))"
!eval "coord_y(first_opaque(5, 1, 5, 7))"
!eval "coord_y(raycast(7, 1, 7, 7))"

Expected: an opaque tile sits at (5,4). A beam cast from (5,1) toward (5,7)
is stopped by it: raycast returns the IMPACT point (5,3) — the last clear cell
before the wall — while first_opaque returns the wall itself (5,4). A beam
down the clear column x=7 reaches its target: raycast(7,1,7,7) returns (7,7).
raycast answers "where does the beam land", first_opaque answers "what did it
hit".


SCENARIO 437 — Event bus: a global handler decouples cause from effect
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ev EV 8 6
!match use ev
!gpassive add onwave event:wave_cleared "match_var_set('waves', match_var_get('waves') + 1)"
!match var set waves 0
!emit wave_cleared
!emit wave_cleared
!eval "match_var_get('waves')"

Expected: a global passive subscribes to the custom event `wave_cleared`
(when = `event:wave_cleared`). Each `!emit wave_cleared` fires it once,
bumping the match var `waves` 0→1→2. The emitter knows nothing about the
handler — the event bus decouples cause from effect. `!eval` shows 2.


SCENARIO 438 — Event bus: directed emit carries a payload; untargeted skips entity handlers
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new evh EVH 8 6
!match use evh
!ent add ogre Ogre 40 4 3 9
!passive add ogre takehit event:damage "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - event_get('amount', 0) * event_get('mult', 1)"
!emit damage to=ogre amount=5 mult=2
!ent dump ogre
!emit damage amount=5 mult=2
!ent dump ogre

Expected: the Ogre has an entity passive on `event:damage` that reads the
event PAYLOAD via event_get. `!emit damage to=ogre amount=5 mult=2` is a
DIRECTED emit — it fires the Ogre's own handler with self=ogre, applying
5 × 2 = 10 → hp 40→30. The second emit OMITS `to=`, so it's untargeted: only
global handlers (there are none) fire and the Ogre's entity handler is
skipped — hp stays 30. (For a broadcast the GM loops emit per target.)


SCENARIO 439 — Event bus: emit from a formula, event chaining + event_name
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new evc EVC 8 6
!match use evc
!ent add bell Bell 10 2 2 9
!gpassive add chain event:ring "emit('echo')"
!gpassive add onecho event:echo "match_var_set('echoed', event_name)"
!match var set echoed none
!ent set_var bell actions.toll.target none
!ent set_var bell actions.toll.body "emit('ring')"
!action bell toll
!eval "match_var_get('echoed')"

Expected: tolling the Bell runs an action body that calls `emit('ring')`. The
global `ring` handler in turn calls `emit('echo')`, and the `echo` handler
records its own `event_name` ('echo') into the match var `echoed`. So emit
works from a formula, events chain handler→handler, and the `event_name`
binding identifies the firing event. `!eval` shows 'echo'.


SCENARIO 440 — Shields: multiple coexisting absorb pools, typed ward, priority
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new sh SH 12 6
!match use sh
!ent add hero Hero 40 2 2 9
!ent set_var hero shields.plate 15
!ent set_var hero shields.ward.amount 10
!ent set_var hero shields.ward.tags fire
!ent set_var hero shields.ward.priority 5
!eval "shield_total('hero')"
!eval "shield_total('hero', 'fire')"
!ent set_var hero actions.bite.target none
!ent set_var hero actions.bite.body "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - absorb_damage(self, 12)"
!action hero bite
!ent dump hero
!ent set_var hero actions.flame.target none
!ent set_var hero actions.flame.body "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - absorb_damage(self, 20, 'fire')"
!action hero flame
!ent dump hero

Expected: Hero has two independent absorb pools — a generic `plate` (15,
priority 0) and a fire `ward` (10, priority 5, tags=fire). shield_total with
no tags = 15 (the fire ward doesn't apply to an untagged hit); for a fire hit
= 25 (both apply). The `bite` (untagged 12) drains only the plate (15→3) and
0 penetrates, so Hero stays at 40 hp. The `flame` (fire 20) drains the
higher-priority ward first (10→gone), then the plate (3→gone), leaving 7 to
penetrate → Hero 40→33. Emptied pools are removed.


SCENARIO 441 — Chain / bounce attack: chain lightning with falloff
------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cl CL 16 6
!match use cl
!ent add coil Coil 20 2 3 9
!ent add e1 E1 30 5 3 5
!ent add e2 E2 30 7 3 5
!ent add e3 E3 30 9 3 5
!ent set_var coil actions.zap.target entity
!ent set_var coil actions.zap.body "entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 12\ndmg = 8\nfor t in chain_targets(target, 2):\n entity[t].hp = entity[t].hp - dmg\n dmg = dmg - 4"
!action coil zap e1
!list

Expected: the zap hits the primary target e1 for 12 (30→18), then
chain_targets walks the two nearest-unvisited entities out of e1 — e2 then e3
— and the action applies a decaying bolt (8, then 4): e2 30→22, e3 30→26. The
caster Coil is never chained (count stops at 2). The GM owns the falloff;
chain_targets is just the nearest-neighbour walk.


SCENARIO 442 — Channeled ability (composed): breaks on move or damage
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ch CH 12 6
!match use ch
!defvar add channeling 0
!ent add mage Mage 30 2 2 9
!passive add mage brkmove on_entity_moved "entity[self].channeling = 0"
!passive add mage brkdmg on_var_changed target=hp "if new_value < old_value:\n entity[self].channeling = 0"
!ent set_var mage channeling 1
!ent move mage right
!eval "entity[mage].channeling"
!ent set_var mage channeling 1
!ent set_var mage hp 25
!eval "entity[mage].channeling"

Expected: a channeled ability needs NO new engine primitive — it's a
`channeling` flag plus two passives. Starting the channel sets channeling=1.
Moving fires on_entity_moved, which clears it → 0. Re-starting then taking
damage fires on_var_changed (hp 30→25, new < old), which clears it → 0. Both
!eval read 0: the channel broke. (Completion is a turn-hook that resolves the
effect when channeling survives N turns — see the charge-up scenario.)


SCENARIO 443 — Charge-up attack (composed): wind up over turns, release at threshold
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cu CU 10 6
!match use cu
!defvar add charge 0
!defvar add charging 0
!ent add hero Hero 30 2 2 9
!ent add dummy Dummy 50 4 2 5
!passive add hero windup on_turn_start "if entity[self].charging > 0:\n entity[self].charge = entity[self].charge + 1\n if entity[self].charge >= 3:\n  entity[dummy].hp = entity[dummy].hp - 25\n  entity[self].charging = 0\n  entity[self].charge = 0"
!ent set_var hero charging 1
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!turn next
!ent dump dummy

Expected: a charge-up attack also needs no new primitive — a `charging` flag
+ `charge` counter advanced by an on_turn_start passive. While charging, each
of Hero's turn-starts adds 1; on the third the wound-up attack releases (25 to
Dummy) and the charge resets. After cycling through enough turns Dummy has
taken the hit: 50→25. Clearing `charging` mid-wind-up would cancel it.


SCENARIO 444 — Dice DSL: keep-highest/lowest (advantage), exploding
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new dc DC 6 6
!match use dc
!system set default random_seed showcase
!eval "roll('3d6+2')"
!eval "roll('4d6kh3')"
!eval "roll('2d20kh1')"
!eval "roll('2d20kl1')"
!eval "roll('1d6!')"

Expected: roll() now understands keep-highest/lowest and exploding dice on
top of the existing NdM±k notation. With random_seed=showcase the rolls are
reproducible: `3d6+2`=12, `4d6kh3`=14 (roll 4d6, keep the best 3),
`2d20kh1`=17 (ADVANTAGE — best of two d20), `2d20kl1`=6 (DISADVANTAGE — worst
of two), `1d6!`=3 (exploding: a die showing its max face rolls again and
adds; here it didn't hit 6 so it's a flat 3). Each die is an independent
randint, and the match RNG makes a seeded session replay identically.


SCENARIO 445 — Dice in an action: advantage to-hit + exploding damage
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new at AT 8 6
!match use at
!system set default random_seed atk
!ent add knight Knight 30 2 2 9
!ent add troll Troll 40 6 2 5
!ent set_var knight actions.smite.target entity
!ent set_var knight actions.smite.body "tohit = roll('2d20kh1')\nif tohit >= 12:\n dmg = roll('2d6!') + 3\n entity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - dmg"
!action knight smite troll
!ent dump troll

Expected: the smite rolls 2d20kh1 (an advantage to-hit) and, on a 12+, deals
roll('2d6!')+3 exploding damage. With random_seed=atk the to-hit clears the
threshold and the damage roll totals 9 → Troll 40→31. The whole attack is
assembled from the dice primitive in an ordinary action body; the GM owns the
threshold and the damage application.


SCENARIO 446 — Weighted random table: loot drop + crit table
------------------------------------------------------------

!match new lt LT 8 6
!match use lt
!system set default random_seed loot
!ent add chest Chest 1 4 2 1
!ent set_var chest actions.open.target none
!ent set_var chest actions.open.body "entity[self].contents = roll_table('sword:1,potion:3,gold:6,nothing:2')"
!action chest open
!ent dump chest
!eval "roll_table('crit:1,hit:3,miss:2')"

Expected: roll_table picks a key with probability proportional to its weight
(the discrete-choice companion to band, which buckets a number). Opening the
chest rolls the loot table `sword:1,potion:3,gold:6,nothing:2`; with
random_seed=loot the drop is `gold` (stored in the chest's `contents` var).
`roll_table('crit:1,hit:3,miss:2')` similarly resolves an attack outcome —
here `hit`. Weights need not sum to anything in particular; a 0-weight entry
is never chosen, and the match RNG makes seeded rolls reproducible.


SCENARIO 447 — Corpse status introspection: read a dead entity's frozen statuses
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cs CS 8 6
!match use cs
!ent add ghoul Ghoul 12 3 3 5
!status apply ghoul poisoned 3 2
!status apply ghoul cursed 1 5
!ent kill ghoul
!eval "corpse_status_has('ghoul', 'poisoned')"
!eval "corpse_status_has('ghoul', 'burning')"
!eval "corpse_status_get('ghoul', 'poisoned', 'level')"
!eval "corpse_status_get('ghoul', 'poisoned', 'duration', -1)"
!eval "corpse_status_names('ghoul')"

Expected: killing the Ghoul (poisoned level 3 / cursed level 1) freezes its
statuses into the corpse snapshot. corpse_status_has reads them back —
poisoned True, burning False; corpse_status_get pulls a dotted field
(poisoned.level = 3, poisoned.duration = 2 via the default arg), raising on a
missing corpse/status/path unless a default is supplied (mirrors corpse_var);
corpse_status_names lists ['cursed', 'poisoned']. The "did it die cursed?" /
"raise it with the same affliction" pattern — the status analog of corpse_var.


SCENARIO 448 — Corpse occupancy: a corpse blocks movement (conditional + footprint)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new co CO 10 6
!match use co
!defvar add flying 0
!ent add ogre Ogre 30 5 3 5
!ent set_var ogre footprint_w 2
!ent kill ogre
!ent add scout Scout 8 3 3 9
!ent set_var scout flying 0
!ent tp scout 5 3
!list
!system set default corpse_block_condition "not entity[self].flying"
!ent tp scout 5 3
!list
!ent set_var scout flying 1
!ent tp scout 6 3
!list

Expected: the Ogre (footprint_w 2) leaves a 2×1 corpse covering (5,3) and
(6,3). With the default (empty) corpse_block_condition corpses are passable —
the non-flying Scout teleports onto (5,3) fine. After setting
corpse_block_condition to `not entity[self].flying`, a non-flyer is blocked
from the corpse cell (Scout, moved back, stays put — the tp is rejected), but
once flying it teleports onto a footprint cell (6,3) freely. A large corpse
blocks its whole footprint, and blocking honors the same block_walk / block_tp
movement toggles as tile/zone blocking.


SCENARIO 449 — Status tags / categories: tag statuses and query/purge by tag
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new st ST 8 6
!match use st
!status def burn
!status def poison
!status def regen
!status tags burn fire,debuff
!status tags poison debuff
!status tags regen buff
!ent add hero Hero 30 3 3 5
!status apply hero burn 2 3
!status apply hero poison 1 5
!status apply hero regen 1 5
!eval "status_tags('burn')"
!eval "status_has_tag('hero', 'burn', 'fire')"
!eval "statuses_with_tag('hero', 'debuff')"
!func def cleanse who "for s in statuses_with_tag(who, 'debuff'): status_remove(who, s)"
!eval "cleanse('hero')"
!eval "status_names('hero')"

Expected: tags are a definition-level category (status_tags('burn') = ['fire',
'debuff'], the order declared). status_has_tag checks the bearer has the status AND its def carries the
tag (burn/fire = True). statuses_with_tag('hero','debuff') lists burn + poison
(not the buff-tagged regen). The cleanse func loops statuses_with_tag and removes
every debuff in one pass — after it, only regen remains on the hero. Tags are the
foundation the cross-status / resistance tokens (`tag:<x>`) key on.


SCENARIO 450 — Cross-status interactions: removes + blocked_by (burn↔freeze)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new cx CX 8 6
!match use cx
!status def burn
!status def freeze
!status tags burn fire
!status tags freeze ice
!status removes freeze tag:fire
!status blockedby burn tag:ice
!ent add mob Mob 30 3 3 5
!status apply mob burn 2 4
!eval "status_has('mob', 'burn')"
!status apply mob freeze 1 3
!eval "status_has('mob', 'burn')"
!eval "status_has('mob', 'freeze')"
!status apply mob burn 2 4
!eval "status_has('mob', 'burn')"

Expected: applying burn lands (fire). Applying freeze (which `removes tag:fire`)
clears the burn AND lands freeze — so after it, burn is gone, freeze present.
Then re-applying burn is rejected: burn is `blocked_by tag:ice` and the mob is
frozen, so the application is a no-op (burn stays absent, message reports it was
blocked by `freeze`). Cancellation lives in the status definition as data — "what
freeze does is stored in freeze."


SCENARIO 451 — Status resistance / immunity: source-gated, level-reducing
-------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rs RS 10 6
!match use rs
!status def burn
!status def poison
!status tags burn fire
!ent add golem Golem 40 3 3 5
!ent set_var golem status_immune tag:fire
!status apply golem burn 3 3
!eval "is_status_immune('golem', 'burn')"
!eval "status_has('golem', 'burn')"
!ent add knight Knight 40 5 5 5
!ent set_var knight equipped.ring.status_resist.poison 2
!ent set_var knight inventory.spare.status_resist.poison 5
!eval "status_resist_of('knight', 'poison')"
!status apply knight poison 5 4
!eval "status_get('knight', 'poison', 'level')"
!ent add squire Squire 30 7 7 5
!ent set_var squire equipped.ring.status_resist.poison 5
!status apply squire poison 2 3
!eval "status_has('squire', 'poison')"

Expected: the Golem's innate `status_immune = tag:fire` blocks burn entirely
(is_status_immune True, burn never lands). The Knight's resistance is
source-gated like modifiers: the EQUIPPED ring (-2) counts, the one in inventory
(-5) does NOT, so status_resist_of = 2; poison applied at level 5 lands at level
3 (5 − 2). The Squire's equipped ring (-5) fully resists an incoming level-2
poison (2 − 5 ≤ 0) so it never lands. Resistances aggregate from the
status_resist_sources roots and combine per status_resist_stack (default sum).


SCENARIO 452 — Universal status counters: charges and durations (no auto-decay)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ct CT 8 6
!match use ct
!status def ward
!status def poison
!ent add mage Mage 24 3 3 5
!status apply mage ward 1 0
!ent set_var mage hp 24
!status counter mage ward set 3 charges
!eval "status_get('mage', 'ward', 'charges')"
!eval "status_counter_add('mage', 'ward', -1, 'charges')"
!eval "status_counter_add('mage', 'ward', -1, 'charges')"
!eval "status_counter_add('mage', 'ward', -1, 'charges')"
!eval "status_has('mage', 'ward')"
!status apply mage poison 1 4
!status counter mage poison add -1
!eval "status_get('mage', 'poison', 'duration')"
!status counter mage poison set 0
!eval "status_has('mage', 'poison')"

Expected: a charge-based ward — set to 3 charges, then status_counter_add(-1)
three times. The third decrement drops charges to 0, which auto-removes the
status (status_has ward = False). The SAME counter tool works on a time
duration: poison starts at duration 4, `counter add -1` → 3, and `counter set 0`
removes it. Charges differ from durations only in that nothing auto-decrements
them from the turn clock — the GM calls status_counter_add from whatever the
trigger is (here, manual). One universal add/subtract/set, auto-clearing at ≤ 0.


SCENARIO 453 — Tile line/fill builder: draw walls and rooms in one command
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new tb TB 10 6
!match use tb
!tile line 2 2 6 2 glyph #
!tile line 2 2 6 2 block true
!tile fill 8 3 9 5 glyph ~
!tile info 4 2
!tile line 8 1 12 1 glyph *
!map

Expected: `!tile line 2 2 6 2 glyph #` stamps the glyph `#` on the five cells
(2,2)..(6,2) in one shot; the second line adds `block true` to the same row
(a wall you draw with two commands instead of ten). `!tile fill 8 3 9 5 glyph ~`
fills the whole 2×3 bounding rectangle (6 cells) with `~`. `!tile info 4 2`
shows glyph `#` and block true. The last line runs from x=8 to x=12 on a
width-10 grid, so cells x=11 and x=12 are off-grid and reported skipped (3
set, 2 skipped). Both builders are pure sugar over `!tile set` (same path=value
shape) — line uses the engine's segment geometry, fill the bounding box.


SCENARIO 454 — Toggleable map layers: persistent toggle + one-off hide
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ml ML 8 6
!match use ml
!tile set 3 3 glyph #
!ent add hero Hero 20 4 4 5
!map
!map layer tiles off
!map
!map layer list
!map layer tiles on
!map hide=entities
!map
!map layer list
!map layer bogus off

Expected: the base `!map` shows both the tile glyph `#` and the hero. `!map
layer tiles off` hides the tile layer persistently — the next `!map` has no `#`,
and `!map layer list` reports tiles hidden. `!map layer tiles on` restores it.
`!map hide=entities` is a ONE-OFF: that single render drops the hero glyph, but
the following `!map layer list` shows nothing hidden (the one-off arg didn't
mutate state). `!map layer bogus off` is rejected (unknown layer). Layers are
zones / tiles / entities / fog; `!map layer` is host-gated, the one-off `hide=`
arg is player-available.


SCENARIO 455 — Cross-match entity transfer: copy keeps source, transfer moves
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new src Source 8 6
!match new bench Bench 10 8
!match use src
!ent add knight Knight 25 4 4 5
!ent set_var knight strength 7
!status def blessed
!status apply knight blessed 2 3
!part add knight arm Arm 8 8
!ent copy knight bench 5 5
!ent add rogue Rogue 12 2 2 5
!ent transfer rogue bench
!ent copy knight bench
!match use bench
!list
!eval "var_get('knight', 'strength')"
!eval "status_has('knight', 'blessed')"
!eval "has_part('knight', 'arm')"
!match use src
!list

Expected: `!ent copy knight bench 5 5` duplicates the knight — with its
`strength` var, its `blessed` status, and its `arm` body part — into the Bench
match at (5,5), leaving the original in Source. `!ent transfer rogue bench`
MOVES the rogue (it leaves Source). The second `!ent copy knight bench`
collides with the already-copied knight id, so it's auto-suffixed to
`knight_2`. Switching to Bench, `!list` shows knight, rogue, knight_2; the
evals confirm the copied knight kept strength=7, the blessed status, and its
arm part. Switching back to Source, `!list` still has knight (copied, not
moved) but no rogue (transferred away).


SCENARIO 456 — Match outcome: manual victory + prims + a goal-tile win condition
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new win Win 8 6
!match use win
!eval "match_over()"
!match win red Total domination
!eval "match_winner()"
!eval "match_over()"
!match outcome
!match win clear
!eval "match_over()"
!ent add runner Runner 10 1 1 5
!tile set 4 1 hooks.on_enter "declare_winner('blue', 'reached the goal')"
!ent tp runner 4 1
!match outcome

Expected: no outcome at first (match_over False). `!match win red ...` declares
a manual victory; match_winner() = 'red', match_over() True, `!match outcome`
shows red. `!match win clear` resets it (match_over False again, play resumes).
Then a GOAL TILE: the cell (4,1) carries an on_enter hook that calls
declare_winner. Teleporting the runner onto it fires the hook, so `!match
outcome` now shows blue won. There is NO built-in objective evaluator — the win
condition is just a tile hook calling the declare_winner primitive.


SCENARIO 457 — Win conditions from an action and an on_death passive
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new fin Fin 8 6
!match use fin
!ent add hero Hero 20 2 2 5
!ent set_var hero actions.exodia.target none
!ent set_var hero actions.exodia.body "declare_winner('heroes', 'EXODIA assembled')"
!action hero exodia
!match outcome
!match win clear
!ent add boss Boss 10 6 6 9
!passive add boss deathwin on_death "declare_winner('heroes', 'boss slain')"
!ent set_var boss hp 0
!match outcome

Expected: declare_winner works from any formula context. An ACTION whose body
calls declare_winner (the "Exodia auto-win" pattern) declares heroes the winner
when used. After clearing, a per-entity on_death PASSIVE on the boss declares
victory the moment the boss dies (setting its hp to 0 runs the death pipeline,
which fires on_death → declare_winner). Same primitive, two more trigger
sources (action body, death hook) — alongside the watcher and tile-hook paths.

SCENARIO 458 — Mounts: slots, capacity budget + cost + condition, carry & driving
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mnt Mounts 12 8
!match use mnt
!ent add car Car 30 3 3 0
!ent set_var car footprint_w 2
!ent set_var car slots.driver.capacity 1
!ent set_var car slots.driver.controls_movement true
!ent set_var car slots.driver.region front
!ent set_var car slots.seats.capacity 3
!ent set_var car slots.seats.cost "entity[self].size"
!ent set_var car slots.seats.condition "entity[self].size <= 2"
!ent add drv Driver 10 1 1 5
!ent set_var drv size 1
!ent add p1 Pass1 10 2 1 5
!ent set_var p1 size 2
!ent add p2 Pass2 10 5 1 5
!ent set_var p2 size 2
!ent add ogre Ogre 10 6 1 5
!ent set_var ogre size 5
!mount drv car driver
!mount p1 car seats
!mount p2 car seats
!mount ogre car seats
!mount list car
!ent move drv 2 right
!ent info car
!ent info drv
!ent info p1
!ent move p1 1 right
!mount dismount p1 1 5
!ent info p1

Expected: `car` is a 2-wide vehicle with a `driver` slot (capacity 1, drives,
shown at the front) and a `seats` slot (capacity 3, each rider costs its `size`,
riders must be size<=2). drv mounts driver; p1 (size 2) mounts seats (used 2/3);
p2 (size 2) is REFUSED — 2+2 > 3 capacity. ogre (size 5) is REFUSED by the
condition (size<=2). `!mount list car` shows driver 1/1 with drv, seats 2/3 with
p1. `!ent move drv 2 right` REDIRECTS to the car (drv is in a control slot): the car
moves from (3,3) to (5,3), and drv + p1 are carried (drv at the car's front cell,
p1 hidden at the anchor). `!ent move p1 1 right` is REFUSED with a ❌ — p1 is a plain
passenger and can't move on its own. Dismounting p1 to (1,5) puts it back on the
ground there.


SCENARIO 459 — Mounts: slot actions, allowed_slots, and rider-vs-vehicle actor
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mnt2 MountActions 12 8
!match use mnt2
!ent add tank Tank 40 3 3 0
!ent set_var tank footprint_w 2
!ent set_var tank ammo 3
!ent set_var tank honks 0
!ent set_var tank slots.gunner.capacity 1
!ent set_var tank slots.gunner.region back
!ent set_var tank slots.gunner.actions.shoot.target entity
!ent set_var tank slots.gunner.actions.shoot.body "entity[vehicle].ammo = entity[vehicle].ammo - 1\nentity[target].hp = entity[target].hp - 7"
!ent set_var tank actions.horn.target none
!ent set_var tank actions.horn.allowed_slots gunner,driver
!ent set_var tank actions.horn.body "entity[vehicle].honks = entity[vehicle].honks + 1"
!ent add gun Gunner 10 6 1 5
!ent add foe Foe 25 5 3 5
!mount gun tank gunner
!action list gun
!action gun shoot foe
!ent info foe
!ent info tank
!action gun horn
!ent dump tank
!ent set_var tank mount_action_actor vehicle
!action gun horn
!ent dump tank

Expected: the gunner slot carries a `shoot` action and the tank carries a
vehicle-wide `horn` action shared with the gunner/driver slots via
`allowed_slots`. After gun mounts the gunner slot, `!action list gun` shows
shoot + horn under a "Via vehicle `tank`" section. `!action gun shoot foe`
runs the slot action: foe drops to 18 and the tank's ammo goes 3->2 (the body
reads the `vehicle` binding). `!action gun horn` fires the shared vehicle
action; honks becomes 1. The default actor is the RIDER. Setting the tank's
`mount_action_actor` var to `vehicle` makes the next `horn` run as the vehicle
(honks -> 2 either way; both bindings are always available, this only changes
which one is `source`).


SCENARIO 460 — Mounts: visible vs hidden riders, render and ground occupancy
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mnt3 MountRender 8 6
!match use mnt3
!ent add bus Bus 30 2 2 0
!ent set_var bus footprint_w 2
!ent set_var bus glyph B
!ent set_var bus slots.roof.capacity 2
!ent set_var bus slots.roof.region front
!ent set_var bus slots.hold.capacity 4
!ent add rg Rooftop 10 5 1 5
!ent set_var rg glyph R
!ent add cg Cargo 10 6 1 5
!mount rg bus roof
!mount cg bus hold
!list
!map
!mount dismount cg 6 5
!ent add box Box 10 6 5 5
!mount cg bus hold
!ent add box2 Box2 10 6 5 5
!ent info box2

Expected: `bus` is a 2-wide vehicle. rg mounts the visible `roof` slot (it shows
on the map at the bus's front cell, glyph R drawn over the bus's B); cg mounts
the hidden `hold` slot (tucked inside — no map glyph). `!list` shows all three
entities, the two riders with a "riding bus" suffix. `!map` shows B (and R over
the front cell), but NOT cg (it's inside the hold). Dismounting cg to (6,5) puts
it on the ground there, so adding `Box` at (6,5) is REFUSED (cell occupied).
Re-mounting cg takes it OFF the ground — so a second add at (6,5) now SUCCEEDS.
Occupancy toggles exactly with mount state: a rider blocks the ground only while
dismounted.
ground, so the cells the bus covers are blocked only by the bus itself, and the
riders never add extra blocking. (walker stops adjacent to the bus's footprint.)


SCENARIO 461 — Mounts: switching slots and host-death ejection
--------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mnt4 MountDeath 10 8
!match use mnt4
!ent add boat Boat 20 3 3 0
!ent set_var boat footprint_w 2
!ent set_var boat slots.helm.capacity 1
!ent set_var boat slots.helm.controls_movement true
!ent set_var boat slots.deck.capacity 3
!ent add sailor Sailor 10 1 1 5
!ent add cap Captain 10 8 1 5
!mount sailor boat deck
!mount cap boat helm
!mount switch sailor helm
!mount switch sailor deck
!mount list boat
!ent set_var boat hp 0
!list
!ent info sailor
!ent info cap

Expected: sailor boards the deck, cap takes the helm. `!mount switch sailor helm`
is REFUSED (helm is capacity 1, cap is in it) — sailor stays on deck. Switching
sailor to deck (already there) is a no-op ❌. `!mount list boat` shows helm with
cap, deck with sailor. Setting the boat's hp to 0 KILLS it (default death
condition hp<=0); the default `mount_on_host_death` is `eject`, so both riders
are dismounted to free cells near the boat's last position and survive. `!list`
no longer shows the boat but shows sailor + cap as ordinary ground entities.


SCENARIO 462 — Mounts: group move skips (or aborts on) carried riders
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mnt5 MountGroup 14 10
!match use mnt5
!ent add car Car 30 3 3 0
!ent set_var car footprint_w 2
!ent set_var car slots.seat.capacity 2
!ent add foot Foot 10 3 6 5
!ent add pax Pax 10 5 1 5
!mount pax car seat
!ent group add squad foot pax
!ent move group:squad 2 right
!ent info foot
!ent info pax
!ent group add convoy car pax
!ent move group:convoy 2 right
!ent info car
!ent info pax
!system set default mount_group_move_mode abort
!ent move group:squad 2 right
!ent info foot

Expected: `pax` rides the car (seat slot). With the default
`mount_group_move_mode` = skip, `!ent move group:squad 2 right` moves only the
free member foot (3,6)->(5,6); pax is SKIPPED — it stays aboard at the car's
cell, not force-displaced. When the VEHICLE is itself in the group (`convoy` =
car + pax), moving the group moves the car two east and pax is carried along (it
ends on the car's cell), so the rider isn't double-moved. Switching the rule to
`abort`, a group move that includes the riding pax is REFUSED with a ❌ naming
pax, and foot does NOT move (all-or-nothing).


SCENARIO 463 — Map viewport: windowing, panning, and centering a large map
--------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new vp Viewport 50 8
!match use vp
!system set default viewport_mode on
!system set default viewport_width 20
!system set default viewport_height 20
!ent add scout Scout 10 2 2 5
!ent set_var scout glyph s
!ent add boss Boss 30 45 4 9
!ent set_var boss glyph B
!map
!map center boss
!map pan left 5
!map view reset
!map view 30 1

Expected: the match is 50 wide × 8 tall; with viewport_mode forced on and the
cap set to 20×20, a viewport engages on width (50 > 20) but not height (8 ≤ 20),
so each render is a 20-wide × 8-tall window. The bare `!map` shows the top-left
window (cols 1-20): the scout `s` at (2,2) appears, the boss `B` at (45,4) does
not. `!map center boss` recenters the window around x=45 (clamped to the right
edge, cols 31-50) so `B` shows and `s` doesn't. `!map pan left 5` shifts the
window 5 columns west. `!map view reset` snaps back to the top-left (scout
visible again); `!map view 30 1` jumps the top-left anchor to column 30. Each
reply carries a "viewport (...)" header naming the visible window.


SCENARIO 464 — Map auto-legend: glyph→meaning key honors the current window
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new lg Legend 40 6
!match use lg
!system set default viewport_mode on
!system set default viewport_width 12
!ent add gob Goblin 10 3 3 5
!ent set_var gob glyph g
!ent add orc Orc 12 5 2 5
!ent set_var orc glyph g
!ent add drag Dragon 80 38 4 9
!ent set_var drag glyph D
!zone fill water 1 4 2 4
!zone glyph water ~
!map legend on
!map
!map center drag

Expected: legend lists only what's actually on screen, grouped by glyph. The
default window (cols 1-12) shows the two `g` entities (Goblin at (3,3), Orc at
(5,2)) and the `~` water zone, so the legend reads `g — Orc, Goblin` (row-major
scan order: Orc on row 2 precedes Goblin on row 3) and `~ — zone: water`; the
Dragon `D` (at x=38, off-window) is NOT listed. After
`!map center drag` the window moves to the right edge — now `D — Dragon` appears
in the legend and the goblins/zone drop out (they're no longer visible). The
auto-legend reflects the current viewport, not the whole map.


SCENARIO 465 — Mounts: a vehicle-on-a-vehicle carries its own rider (nested)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new nv NestedVeh 20 20
!match use nv
!ent add gunship Gunship 30 5 5 0
!ent set_var gunship slots.cargo.capacity 1
!ent set_var gunship slots.cargo.controls_movement true
!ent add cart Cart 20 1 1 0
!ent set_var cart slots.driver.capacity 1
!ent set_var cart slots.driver.controls_movement true
!ent add rider Rider 10 2 2 5
!mount cart gunship cargo
!mount rider cart driver
!ent dump rider
!ent move gunship 5 right
!ent dump rider
!ent dump cart

Expected: cart mounts into the gunship's cargo slot (cart snaps to the gunship
cell 5,5); rider mounts the cart's driver slot (rider snaps to 5,5 too). After
`!ent move gunship 5 right` the gunship moves to (10,5) and carries the WHOLE
nested stack: cart → (10,5) AND rider → (10,5). Before the nested-restamp fix
the rider was stranded at (5,5) because the cart (itself a rider) was
repositioned by a raw move that didn't re-run its own carry. The two `!ent dump
rider` calls show x going from 5 to 10.


SCENARIO 466 — Mounts: a rider that dies revives UNMOUNTED (no phantom links)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mr MountRevive 20 20
!match use mr
!ent add horse Horse 30 3 3 0
!ent set_var horse slots.saddle.capacity 1
!ent add knight Knight 10 4 4 5
!mount knight horse saddle
!ent kill knight
!ent move horse 3 right
!ent revive knight
!ent dump knight
!mount list horse

Expected: the knight mounts the horse (snaps to the horse cell 3,3) and is then
killed — its corpse is stored at (3,3). The horse moves away (to 6,3), freeing
the cell, and the knight is revived there at full hp. The revived knight is a
NORMAL ground entity: its corpse snapshot dropped the `mounted_on` / `mount_slot`
links at death, so revive does NOT re-seat it onto the horse for free (which had
previously produced an invisible "rider" standing on the ground). `!mount list
horse` shows no riders.


SCENARIO 467 — Body parts: a multi-level part subtree dies and revives whole
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new hp HierParts 20 20
!match use hp
!ent add dragon Dragon 40 5 5 5
!part add dragon wing wing 20 20
!part add wing feather feather 10 10
!part list dragon
!ent kill dragon
!list
!ent revive dragon
!part list dragon
!ent dump feather

Expected: the dragon has a wing (a part), and the wing has a feather (a part of
a part). `!part list dragon` shows the wing. Killing the dragon removes the
ENTIRE part subtree — wing AND feather — so `!list` shows no orphaned, suddenly-
free feather entity (before the fix the deeper feather survived as a visible
zombie with a dangling parent). Reviving the dragon restores the whole tree: the
wing re-attaches to the dragon and the feather re-attaches to the wing (`!ent
dump feather` shows it's a body part of `wing`), because the corpse now snapshots
the full subtree in parent-before-child order.


SCENARIO 468 — Group move validates the WHOLE footprint (bounds + occupancy)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new gfv GroupFootprint 10 6
!match use gfv
!ent add big Big 30 7 2 5
!ent set_var big footprint_w 2
!ent set_var big footprint_h 2
!ent group new gg
!ent group add gg big
!ent move group:gg right right right
!ent dump big
!ent add wall Wall 30 4 4 9
!ent set_var wall footprint_w 2
!ent set_var wall footprint_h 2
!ent add runner Runner 20 1 4 6
!ent group new gr
!ent group add gr runner
!ent move group:gr right right right
!ent dump runner

Expected: the 2×2 `big` is anchored at (7,2), covering (7,2)-(8,3). A group move
of three steps right would push its right edge to column 11, off the 10-wide
grid — the move is REJECTED (❌ out of bounds) atomically, so `big` stays at
(7,2) (the `!ent dump big` still shows 7,2). Then a 2×2 `wall` at (4,4) covers
(4,4)-(5,5); the 1×1 `runner` at (1,4) moving three right would land on (4,4) —
the wall's cell — and is REJECTED (❌ occupied), so runner stays at (1,4).
Before the fix the group path only checked the anchor cell, so a multi-tile
member could march its footprint off-grid or onto another body's non-anchor
cells.


SCENARIO 469 — Group move respects movement blocking (impassable zone)
---------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new gbl GroupBlock 12 5
!match use gbl
!ent add hero Hero 30 1 1 5
!ent group new band
!ent group add band hero
!zone fill wall 5 1 5 3
!zone set wall block true
!ent move group:band right right right right right
!ent dump hero

Expected: an impassable zone `wall` covers column 5 (rows 1-3). A group move of
five steps right from (1,1) would cross x=5 — it is REJECTED (❌ blocked) and
the whole group move is aborted atomically, so `hero` stays at (1,1). Before the
fix `move_group_dirs` had no block check at all and the group walked straight
through the wall.


SCENARIO 470 — A large viewer casts line-of-sight from its WHOLE body
--------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new lbv LargeViewerLOS 12 8
!match use lbv
!ent add scout Scout 30 2 2 5
!ent set_var scout footprint_w 3
!ent set_var scout footprint_h 1
!ent set_var scout team blue
!zone fill smoke 2 3 2 7
!zone set smoke opaque true
!eval "can_see_losonly('scout', 4, 7)"
!eval "has_los(2, 2, 4, 7, 'scout')"

Expected: the 3-wide `scout` covers (2,2)-(4,2). An opaque smoke zone fills
column 2 (rows 3-7), blocking the anchor cell (2,2)'s downward sight. The pure
line-of-sight query `can_see_losonly('scout', 4, 7)` returns True because the
scout's right body cell (4,2) has a clear column down to (4,7) — a large viewer
sees from any footprint cell. The raw `has_los` from the ANCHOR (2,2) to (4,7)
returns False (its line clips the smoke), showing why the anchor-only check was
wrong before the fix.


SCENARIO 471 — A body part's aura and its sub-parts follow the parent's move
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new paf PartAuraFollow 20 20
!match use paf
!ent add dragon Dragon 40 5 5 5
!part add dragon wing wing 20 20
!part add wing feather feather 10 10
!zone new aura
!zone anchor aura wing 1
!ent dump feather
!ent move dragon 4 right
!ent dump feather
!zone cells aura

Expected: the dragon has a wing (a part) and the wing has a feather (a part of a
part); an aura zone is anchored to the wing with radius 1. Moving the dragon 4
right to (9,5) carries the WHOLE part tree — the feather (a part of the wing)
rides along to (9,5), shown by the two `!ent dump feather` calls (x 5 → 9) — and
the wing's anchored aura re-stamps around the wing's new cell (`!zone cells aura`
now centers on column 9). Before the fix the parts-restamp moved only the
direct part's position and never re-stamped a part's aura or its sub-parts.


SCENARIO 472 — hidden_rider_grants_vision gamerule (passenger sight)
-------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new hrv HiddenRiderVision 14 5
!match use hrv
!ent add veh Veh 30 2 2 5
!ent set_var veh team red
!ent set_var veh slots.hold.capacity 1
!ent add pax Pax 20 3 3 5
!ent set_var pax team red
!ent set_var pax fog_vision_radius 9
!mount pax veh hold
!eval "team_sees_cell_rangeonly('red', 11, 2)"
!system set default hidden_rider_grants_vision true
!eval "team_sees_cell_rangeonly('red', 11, 2)"

Expected: `pax` (a vision radius of 9) is mounted into a hidden slot (no region)
inside `veh`, so it's tucked inside. With the default `hidden_rider_grants_vision`
= false, the hidden passenger does NOT contribute to the team's vision, so
`team_sees_cell_rangeonly('red', 11, 2)` is False (the vehicle's own radius
doesn't reach 9 cells away). After enabling the rule, the passenger's eyes count
and the same query returns True. (Note: the rule flows into the match's rules on
the next refresh; this eval reads the live rule.)


SCENARIO 473 — resize_grid shifts the per-channel viewport camera
----------------------------------------------------------------

!match new rvc ResizeCam 50 50
!match use rvc
!system set default viewport_mode on
!map view 20 20
!map resize 60 60 center
!map view 1 1

Expected: with the viewport forced on, `!map view 20 20` parks the camera's
top-left at (20,20). Resizing to 60×60 with the `center` anchor shifts all
content (and now the camera) by +5,+5, so the camera follows to (25,25) — the
`!map resize` reply's viewport header reads "(25,25)…". Before the fix the camera
stayed at (20,20) while the content moved, framing the wrong region. `!map view
1 1` then resets it. (The harness surface isn't viewport-capable, so viewport_mode
must be forced on for the window to engage.)


SCENARIO 474 — A status DoT on a body part ticks (shares the parent's clock)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new spt StatusPartTick 10 6
!match use spt
!ent add ogre Ogre 30 3 3 40
!part add ogre oarm arm 20 20
!part add oarm ofinger finger 8 8
!status def burn
!status when burn turn_end
!status tick burn "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 3"
!status apply oarm burn 1 5
!status apply ofinger burn 1 5
!ent dump oarm
!ent dump ofinger
!turn next
!turn next
!ent dump oarm
!ent dump ofinger

Expected: the ogre has an arm (a part) and the arm has a finger (a part of a
part). A `burn` DoT (tick_when=turn_end, −3 hp) is applied to BOTH parts. Parts
have no initiative of their own, so before the fix their statuses never ticked.
Now they share the parent ogre's status clock: ending the ogre's turn ticks the
ogre AND every attached part lacking its own initiative. (The first `!turn next`
just begins round 1; the second ends the ogre's turn and fires the turn_end
tick.) So `oarm` drops 20→17 and the sub-part `ofinger` drops 8→5. (Each part's own tick_when still gates it;
a part with a different tick_when wouldn't fire here.)


SCENARIO 475 — A part's tick routes damage to the parent via damage_part
-----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new spr StatusPartRoute 10 6
!match use spr
!ent add troll Troll 30 4 3 50
!part add troll tleg leg 25 25 to_main_percent=100 to_main_cap=max_hp
!status def acid
!status when acid turn_end
!status tick acid "damage_part(self, 4)"
!status apply tleg acid 1 5
!ent dump troll
!ent dump tleg
!turn next
!turn next
!ent dump troll
!ent dump tleg

Expected: the troll's leg has an `acid` DoT whose tick calls `damage_part(self,
4)` — the headline pattern the doc describes for limb DoTs. (The first `!turn next`
begins round 1; the second ends the troll's turn.) Ending the troll's
turn ticks the leg (it shares the parent's clock); the leg's tick routes 4
damage through the part-damage pipeline: with to_main_percent=100 the parent
troll takes 4 (50→46) and the leg itself drops 25→21. This proves a status on a
limb can both live on the limb and bleed into the main body.


SCENARIO 476 — A body part's turn/round passive fires on the parent's clock
---------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new ptp PartTurnPassive 10 6
!match use ptp
!ent add ogre Ogre 30 3 3 40
!part add ogre arm arm 20 20
!part add arm finger finger 8 8
!passive add arm bleed on_turn_end "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 2"
!passive add finger bleed on_turn_end "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 1"
!ent dump arm
!ent dump finger
!turn next
!turn next
!ent dump arm
!ent dump finger

Expected: parts carry no initiative (excluded from turn_order), so before the
fix an on_turn_end passive on a part never fired. Now a part shares its parent's
turn/round clock: ending the ogre's turn fires the ogre's hooks AND every
attached part's OWN passives (globals/team passives still fire only once per
acting unit, NOT per part). So `arm` drops 20→18 and the sub-part `finger` drops
8→7. (The first `!turn next` begins round 1; the second ends the ogre's turn and
fires on_turn_end.)


SCENARIO 477 — A turn-scheduled effect on a body part fires on the parent's turn
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new psp PartSchedule 10 6
!match use psp
!ent add troll Troll 30 4 3 50
!part add troll leg leg 25 25
!schedule turn leg 1 "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 5"
!schedule list
!ent dump leg
!turn next
!turn next
!ent dump leg
!schedule list

Expected: an entity-attached turn schedule bound to the leg (a part) would never
fire before the fix, because fire_scheduled_turn was only invoked for the active
turn_order entity. Now a part's turn schedule fires on the parent's turn start:
the leg's −5 effect (delay 1) fires once, dropping it 25→20, and the schedule is
consumed (the second `!schedule list` is empty).


SCENARIO 478 — Action rollback preserves the live event-bus stack (no "pop from empty list")
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new evr EventRollback 8 6
!match use evr
!ent add a a 30 2 2 10
!ent set_var a actions.outer.target none
!ent set_var a actions.outer.body "emit('zap', {'mark': 42}, self)\nentity[self].after = event_has('mark')"
!ent set_var a actions.bad.target none
!ent set_var a actions.bad.body "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 1\nfail('nope')"
!passive add a h event:zap "entity[self].log = event_get('mark')\nuse_action(self, 'bad')\nentity[self].log2 = event_get('mark')"
!action a outer
!ent dump a

Expected: action `outer` emits `zap` (pushing a frame on the event-bus stack),
whose handler reads the payload (`log`=42), then runs the sub-action `bad` which
deducts hp and `fail()`s — rolling back. Before the fix the rollback rebuilt the
match from a snapshot and clobbered the LIVE event-bus runtime fields, wiping the
in-flight emit frame; the handler's next `event_get` and the emit's own cleanup
then hit "pop from empty list", crashing the whole `outer` action. Now
`_rollback_match` preserves the event stack (and every other runtime-only
field), so `outer` succeeds: `log`=42 AND `log2`=42 (the payload is still
readable after the rolled-back sub-action), `a.hp` stays 30 (the sub-action's −1
was rolled back), and `after`=false (the emit popped its frame normally on
completion).


SCENARIO 479 — A turn_end tick that empties the turn order doesn't crash next_turn
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new doom Doomtick 8 6
!match use doom
!ent add solo solo 3 3 3 5
!status def doom
!status when doom turn_end
!status tick doom "entity[self].hp = entity[self].hp - 10"
!status apply solo doom 1 5
!turn next
!turn next
!list

Expected: `solo` is the only combatant and carries a `doom` DoT that fires at
turn_end for −10. The first `!turn next` begins round 1 (turn_start only); the
second ends solo's turn, the doom tick drops it to −7 and it dies — emptying the
turn order. Previously `next_turn` then computed `(active_index + 1) %
len(turn_order)` against an empty order and crashed with ZeroDivisionError
(surfacing as 💥). Now the turn clock detects the emptied order at each point a
hook/tick could clear it (turn_end, the round-wrap ticks, and the opening
round_start) and ends the turn cleanly. `!list` shows no living entities (solo
is dead/gone) and no error.


SCENARIO 480 — !mod show flags an unrecognized modifier op (typo guard)
----------------------------------------------------------------------

!match new mop ModOpWarn 8 6
!match use mop
!ent add h h 30 2 2 5
!ent set_var h modifiers.fm.stat atk
!ent set_var h modifiers.fm.op inc%
!ent set_var h modifiers.fm.value 50
!mod show h atk 10
!ent set_var h modifiers.bad.stat atk
!ent set_var h modifiers.bad.op inc
!ent set_var h modifiers.bad.value 5
!mod show h atk 10

Expected: the first `!mod show` lists the well-formed `inc%` modifier and folds
base 10 → 15 with no warning. After adding a second modifier with the op `inc`
(a typo for `inc%`), the second `!mod show` marks that line with ⚠️ and appends
an advisory: "unrecognized op(s) `inc` — folded as a lenient add. Valid ops:
add, inc%, more%, set, min, max." The unknown op still folds (as a lenient add,
so base 10 → 22.5), but the warning surfaces the likely typo rather than letting
a silent flat bonus pass unnoticed. The recognized ops (add/inc%/more%/set/min/
max) never warn.
